601 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hon


Case No. 05-CAA-04-023


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DELAWARE COUNTY


2006-Ohio-1668; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 1557



March 31, 2006, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from the Delaware County. Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 04-CR-1-10-439.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Delaware County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which convicted him of possession of drugs with a forfeiture specification, in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2925.11, and sentenced him to a period of community control sanctions (CCSs).


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to the bill of information and he was referred to the Adult Parole Authority for a pre-sentence investigation. After a hearing, the trial court sentenced defendant. The judgment entry indicated that if defendant violated the CCSs, he could be sentenced for up to 12 months in prison. The State's motion to terminate defendant's CCSs for an alleged failure to comply with the terms, based to his failure to report his whereabouts, was granted. Defendant was sentenced to the maximum term of 12-months' imprisonment. On appeal, the court reviewed the Foster decision and held that defendant's sentence required vacatur because it was based on unconstitutional statutes and was therefore void. Accordingly, a new sentencing hearing was to be held pursuant to the Ohio Supreme Court's dictate in Foster, which was aligned with the procedure used in Geiger.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, vacated the sentence imposed, and remanded the matter for re-sentencing.

 

602 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Conley


C.A. No. 27869


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


2016-Ohio-5310; 2016 Ohio App. LEXIS 3170



August 10, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE STOW MUNICIPAL COURT, COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE No. 2014CRB03864.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant failed to show that his Tier I sex offender registration requirements under the Adam Walsh Act (Act), R.C. Chapter 2950, constituted cruel and unusual punishment because there was no reason to conclude that his 15-year registration period was so severe as to reach the level of unconstitutionality. Defendant was culpable for his actions of recording a 20-year-old coworker while she used the toilet; [2]-Defendant was not denied due process because a hearing was not required and the inconsistency among the maximum jail term for his voyeurism conviction and his 15-year registration period and 18-month maximum prison term for a failure to register violation did not implicate a violation of procedural due process; [3]-Defendant failed to establish standing for his substantive due process claim.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Ferguson v. State


No. 102553


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2015-Ohio-4499; 42 N.E.3d 804; 2015 Ohio App. LEXIS 4435



October 29, 2015, Released 
October 29, 2015, Journalized


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by Ferguson v. State, 145 Ohio St. 3d 1421, 2016-Ohio-1173, 2016 Ohio LEXIS 833, 47 N.E.3d 165 (Mar. 23, 2016)
Reversed by Ferguson v. State, 2017-Ohio-7844, 2017 Ohio LEXIS 2007 (Ohio, Sept. 28, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Civil Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CV-13-810584.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court properly found that the 2006 amendment to R.C. 4123.512(D) was unconstitutional because it conflicted with Civ.R. 41(A)(1)(a) and violated the basic principles of separation of powers, due process, and equal protection in Ohio Const. art. I, §§ 2, 16, and art. IV, § 5(B) where the court's rules prevailed over conflicting statutes, workers' compensation proceedings did not constitute "special proceedings" under Civ.R. 1(C)(7), the amendment restricted the rights of an injured employee to voluntarily dismiss his complaint without obtaining the consent of the employer and to utilize R.C. 2305.19 to refile his case, and there was no rational relationship between stripping injured workers of their rights provided under the Rules of Civil Procedure and the fundamental purposes of workers' compensation.


OUTCOME: Decision affirmed.

 

604 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Dayton Supply & Tool Co. v. Montgomery County Bd. of Revision


No. 2005-1464


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


111 Ohio St. 3d 367; 2006-Ohio-5852; 856 N.E.2d 926; 2006 Ohio LEXIS 3282


February 22, 2006, Submitted  
November 29, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Dayton Supply & Tool Co. v. Montgomery County Bd. of Revision, 2007 Ohio Tax LEXIS 362 (Ohio B.T.A., Feb. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Board of Tax Appeals, No. 2003-G-1851.
Dayton Supply & Tool Co. v. Montgomery County Bd. of Revision, 2005 Ohio Tax LEXIS 859 (Ohio B.T.A., July 8, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Decision reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the decision of the Board of Tax Appeals (Ohio), which remanded the corporation's appeal from the decision of a county board of revisions (BOR) with instructions to dismiss the complaint because the corporation's corporate officer had engaged in the unauthorized practice of law by preparing and filing the complaint with the BOR, thereby depriving the BOR of jurisdiction to hear the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The officer prepared and filed a valuation complaint with the BOR alleging that the market value of a parcel owned by the corporation was worth less than the amount assessed by an auditor. The officer appeared on behalf of the corporation. After the officer appealed from the BOR's decision, the Board found that the officer had engaged in the unauthorized practice of law by preparing and filing the complaint with the BOR and had deprived the BOR of jurisdiction to hear the complaint. On appeal, the court held that, pursuant to R.C. § 5715.19, a corporate officer did not engage in the unauthorized practice of law by preparing and filing a complaint with the BOR and by presenting the claimed value of the property before the BOR on behalf of his or her corporation as long as the officer did not make legal arguments, examine witnesses, or undertake any other tasks that could be performed only by an attorney. Since the officer made no legal arguments and did not introduce any evidence or present any witnesses, the hearing did not require legal training or expertise; thus, the officer did not engage in the unauthorized practice of law under Ohio Sup. Ct. R. Gov't Bar VII(2)(A).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Board's decision and remanded the cause to the Board with instructions to consider the corporation's appeal.

 

605 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Marcum


CASE NO. 10 CO 17


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, COLUMBIANA COUNTY


2012-Ohio-2721; 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 2387



June 13, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Motion to Reopen Direct Appeal.
State v. Marcum, 2011 Ohio 6140, 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 5023 (Ohio Ct. App., Columbiana County, Nov. 21, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of assault on a peace officer, in violation of R.C. 2903.13(C)(3), and aggravated burglary, in violation of R.C. 2911.11(A). He was sentenced to 10 years and two months in prison. The convictions were affirmed on appeal. He filed an application under App.R. 26(B) to reopen the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he received ineffective assistance of appellate counsel because counsel did not challenge the duration of his sentence and did not challenge the imposition of consecutive sentences. The appellate court denied the application to reopen because appellate counsel's performance was not deficient. The trial court had complete discretion to impose a sentence within the statutory range, pursuant to former R.C. 2929.14. It could have exercised its discretion to impose a maximum of 18 months for the assault and a maximum of 11 years for the aggravated burglary, but did not do so. Also, defendant was sentenced two years before the consecutive sentencing provisions were recodified by the legislature. Thus, there was nothing that suggested error with regard to sentences within the statutory range. Appellate counsel's decision not to challenge the duration of defendant's sentences and the application of consecutive sentences was not error because the sentences were entirely compliant with applicable law. Defendant was in no way prejudiced by the fact that appellate counsel did not raise an argument that had no chance of success.


OUTCOME: The application to reopen was denied.

Apple Group Ltd. v. Bd. of Zoning Appeals Granger Twp.


C.A. No. 12CA0065-M, 12CA0068-M


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MEDINA COUNTY


2013-Ohio-4259; 2013 Ohio App. LEXIS 4480



September 30, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Apple Group, Ltd. v. Granger Twp. Bd. of Zoning Appeals, 139 Ohio St. 3d 1404, 2014-Ohio-2245, 2014 Ohio LEXIS 1243, 9 N.E.3d 1062 (2014)
Affirmed by Apple Group, Ltd. v. Granger Twp. Bd. of Zoning Appeals, 2015-Ohio-2343, 2015 Ohio LEXIS 1540 (Ohio, June 17, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS COUNTY OF MEDINA, OHIO. CASE No. 08CIV0090.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A trial court correctly determined that a zoning resolution was adopted in accordance with a comprehensive plan under R.C. 519.02 because competent, credible evidence in the record showed that the zoning resolution addressed the entire geographic area of the township, was all-encompassing in that it addressed use, height, and area and was intended to operate on a permanent basis to manage development of the township, and a person examining it could ascertain to what use property may be put; [2]-The trial court also correctly determined that a township's zoning resolution was constitutional as applied to a developer's property because the lot size, frontage and setback requirements reasonably advanced the township's legitimate goal of maintaining its rural character and the developer's plan to cluster homes on less-than-one-acre lots conflicted with the township's vision.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

607 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Lloyd v. Lovelady


NO. 83090


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2004-Ohio-3617; 2004 Ohio App. LEXIS 3294



July 8, 2004, Date of Announcement of Decision


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by State ex rel. Lloyd v. Lovelady, 104 Ohio St. 3d 1425, 2004 Ohio 6585, 819 N.E.2d 708, 2004 Ohio LEXIS 2882 (2004)
Affirmed by State ex rel. Loyd v. Lovelady, 108 Ohio St. 3d 86, 2006 Ohio 161, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 218 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Civil appeal from Juvenile Court Division. Common Pleas Court. Case No. 9572567.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 1997, a judgment was entered finding defendant father to be the father of a minor child and ordered him to pay child support. Years later, the father filed a motion to terminate the support order based on genetic test results. The Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denied the motion finding that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3119.961 et seq. was unconstitutional as it violated the separation of powers. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the trial court erred. The appellate court agreed and held that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3119.961 et seq. was constitutional, as there was no violation of the separation of powers. Because Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3119.961 et seq. provided a substantive right and not a procedural right, no tension existed between it and Ohio Const. art. IV, § 5(B). Further, the trial court had the authority pursuant to its continuing jurisdiction over all judgments or orders issued in accordance with Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 3111.01 to .19, which included judgments or orders that concerned the duty of support or involved the welfare of the child. Therefore, the matter was returned to the trial court for a hearing on the father's arrearages pursuant to Guthrie, wherein the trial court vacated a paternity determination after the putative father presented DNA evidence approximately two years later that he was not the father. The instant father's inexcusable conduct was comparable to that in Guthrie, in that he voluntarily and deliberately disregarded proceedings wherein he could have addressed his grievance.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

608 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Ridenour v. Wilkinson


No. 07AP-200


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2007-Ohio-5965; 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 5238



November 8, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Ridenour v. Wilkinson, 2008 Ohio 1279, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 752 (Ohio, Mar. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 06CVH01-1142).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prison inmates sought review of a judgment from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which granted the motion under Civ. R. 12(C) of appellee, the Director of the Ohio State Department of Rehabilitation and Correction (ODRC), for judgment on the pleadings. The inmates had challenged the retroactive application of R.C. 5120.56, Ohio Admin. Code 5120:5-13, and ODRC policies to them.


OVERVIEW: The inmates were each convicted and sentenced for crimes that were committed prior to July 1, 1996. They received free healthcare from the ODRC until R.C. 5120.56 was enacted, after which they were charged co-payments for certain medical services based on § 5120.56, Ohio Admin. Code 5120:5-13(B), and accompanying ODRC policies. The inmates sought injunctive and declaratory relief, and the trial court granted judgment on the pleadings to the ODRC. On appeal, the court initially noted that the trial court erred in failing to fully consider and decide various claims raised by the inmates. However, upon de novo review, the court found no merit to the issues raised. The court concluded that R.C. 5120.021, as amended, did not preclude the ODRC from charging and collecting healthcare co-payments and fees from the inmates. There was no breach of the inmates' plea agreements and no violation of their due process rights by the retroactive application pursuant to Ohio Const. art. I, § 16 and Ohio Const. art. II, § 28. Their property interests were not violated under due process. Ex post facto claims did not apply, and there were no procedural errors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Haight v. Minchak


No. 2014-1241


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


146 Ohio St. 3d 481; 2016-Ohio-1053; 58 N.E.3d 1135; 2016 Ohio LEXIS 743; 26 Wage & Hour Cas. 2d (BNA) 619; 166 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P61,692


September 2, 2015, Submitted 
March 17, 2016, Decided

Greene v. Ohio Adult Parole Auth.


No. 08AP-555


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2008-Ohio-5972; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 5007



November 18, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Greene v. Ohio Adult Parole Auth., 121 Ohio St. 3d 1428, 2009 Ohio 1296, 903 N.E.2d 326, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 786 (2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Greene v. Knab, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 90950 (S.D. Ohio, July 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 08CVH03-3476).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a complaint for declaratory judgment, injunctive relief, and monetary damages in the amount of $ 667,448. Appellees, the Ohio Adult Parole Authority (OAPA), the chair of the parole board, and 10 parole board members, filed a Civ. R. 12(C) motion for judgment on the pleadings. The Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) granted the motion and entered judgment for appellees. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that he suffered prejudice because the trial court misconstrued the facts in his complaint. The appellate court held that, although the inmate did not ask expressly for a declaration that he be released from prison, asking instead for a declaration that his constitutional rights had been violated, he suffered no prejudice from the error. Further, while the inmate did not use the term "guidelines," Harris adequately supported the trial court's conclusion that the inmate was not entitled to declaratory relief on the challenge to the parole guidelines or a finding that a change in his parole eligibility amounted to a ex post facto imposition of punishment. Also, because the Ex Post Facto Clause did not prohibit the retroactive application of R.C. 5149.101 and related notice provisions, the trial court properly dismissed those claims. While many of the provisions at issue became effective after the inmate's conviction, they had no substantive impact on his sentence or his eligibility for parole. Finally, his retroactivity claim under Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 was not a claim upon which relief could have been granted in his favor as R.C. 2967.12 was remedial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

612 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Watkins


C.A. CASE NO. 2008 CA 41


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, GREENE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3043; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2562



June 19, 2009, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
(Criminal appeal from Common Pleas Court). T.C. NO. 1996 CR 119.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment from the Greene County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which held that it lacked jurisdiction to address constitutional challenges to R.C. Chapter 2950, as amended by S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007), in the inmate's challenge to his reclassification as a Tier III sex offender (SO) pursuant to R.C. 2950.031(E) and 2950.032(E).


OVERVIEW: The inmate entered a guilty plea to attempted rape, in violation of R.C. 2923.02(A) and 2907.02(A)(1)(B), and he was designated as a sexually oriented offender. After the enactment of S.B. 10, which implemented the federal Adam Walsh Child Protection and Safety Act of 2006, the inmate was reclassified as a Tier III SO, which imposed different registration and community notification requirements. The inmate filed a petition to contest the reclassification, wherein he raised various constitutional challenges to S.B. 10. The trial court granted the State's motion to dismiss upon finding that it lacked jurisdiction to rule on the constitutional issues, and that the inmate did not sufficiently show an error in the reclassification. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in finding that it lacked jurisdiction over the challenges, as it had authority and responsibility to review challenged legislation prior to applying it. However, any error was harmless because the trial court's determination that S.B. 10 was properly applied included the implicit presumption that S.B. 10 was constitutional. Further, based on prior precedent, the constitutional challenges lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

613 of 997 DOCUMENTS



City of E. Liverpool v. Columbiana County Budget Comm'n


Case No. 2006-1129


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


114 Ohio St. 3d 133; 2007-Ohio-3759; 870 N.E.2d 705; 2007 Ohio LEXIS 1868


April 4, 2007, Submitted 
August 8, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by City of E. Liverpool v. Columbiana County Budget Comm'n, 116 Ohio St. 3d 1201, 2007 Ohio 5505, 876 N.E.2d 575, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2560 (2007)
Reconsideration denied by E. Liverpool v. Columbiana County Budget Comm., 2007 Ohio 5636, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2576 (Ohio, Oct. 23, 2007)
Judgment entered by City of E. Liverpool v. Columbiana County Budget Comm'n, 2007 Ohio Tax LEXIS 1557 (Ohio B.T.A., Nov. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Board of Tax Appeals, Nos. 2003-T-1301, 2004-T-844, 2005-T-1474.
City of East Liverpool v. Columbiana County Budget Comm'n, 2006 Ohio Tax LEXIS 586 (Ohio B.T.A., May 12, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision from the Ohio Board of Tax Appeals, which upheld an apportionment of funds to a county's political subdivision by appellee county budget commission (CBC) based on an alternative method under Am. Sub. H.B. 329, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2002) with respect to the Undivided Local Government Fund (ULGF) and the Undivided Local Government Revenue Assistance Fund (ULGRAF).


OVERVIEW: The county political subdivisions utilized the procedures under H.B. 329 to adopt a new method of apportioning the ULFG and the ULGRAF money for various distribution years. They initially passed resolutions to exclude the city's approval, and then passed resolutions that approved a new method of apportionment. Accordingly, the city had no right to vote on the adoption of the alternative method. The city challenged the CBC's apportionment of funds for various years in two separate matters. The Board upheld the apportionments, but it did not consider the city's constitutional claims. On appeal, the court noted that the results from apportioning the ULGF and the ULGRAF by the alternative formula in the county differed significantly from the prior apportionment method. It found that there was nothing unconstitutional on the face of the H.B. 329 amendments to R.C. 5747.43 and 5747.63. They were uniform for purposes of Ohio Const. art. II, § 26. Under the rational basis test, there was no equal protection violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ohio Const. art. I, § 2, and a retroactivity challenge under Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 was not reviewed where it did not apply to the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Board.


 

614 of 997 DOCUMENTS



O'Brien v. City of Olmsted Falls


Nos. 89966 and 90336


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2008-Ohio-2658; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 2240



May 22, 2008, Released 
June 2, 2008, Journalized


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CV-577126.
City of Olmsted Falls v. O'Brien, 2005 Ohio 1317, 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 1286 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, Mar. 24, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee/cross-appellant motorist sued appellants/cross-appellees police officers and cross-appellee city in the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) for spoliation of evidence, malicious prosecution, civil aiding and abetting, civil conspiracy, and state constitutional violations. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment except as to spoliation against the officers. The officers appealed and the motorist cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The motorist's conviction of a traffic offense the officers investigated was reversed. The appellate court held the trial court could not consider the officers' immunity because they waived that defense. The motorist did not claim they destroyed or altered physical evidence, leaving no fact issue as to her spoliation claim, which was limited to destroying physical evidence. Her claim that R.C. Chapter 2744, immunizing the city and officers, violated Ohio Const. art. I, §§ 5 and 16, on the right to a jury trial and to sue the state, was not well-taken as the Ohio Supreme Court had not so ruled. Summary judgment was proper for the officers as to malicious prosecution because they did not prosecute the motorist, there was probable cause to cite her, and her case was not terminated in her favor, even though her conviction was reversed. The city was immune as to her spoliation claim. Once her malicious prosecution and spoliation claims were dismissed, the officers and city were entitled to summary judgment as to her civil aiding and abetting and civil conspiracy claims. Her claim of abuse of police powers in violation of her state constitutional rights was vague and untenable.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment denying summary judgment to the officers was reversed, and the judgment otherwise granting summary judgment against the motorist was affirmed.

City of Dayton v. State


C.A. CASE NO. 26643


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2015-Ohio-3160; 36 N.E.3d 235; 2015 Ohio App. LEXIS 3082



August 7, 2015, Rendered

Reversed by City of Dayton v. State, 2017 Ohio LEXIS 1450 (Ohio, July 26, 2017)

(Ohio 2014), which amended and enacted several statutory provisions governing traffic law photo-monitoring devices, including R.C. 4511.093(B)(1), (3), 4511.095, and 4511.0912, violated the Home Rule Amendment, Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3, and was unconstitutional. HOLDINGS: [1]-Am. Sub. S.B. 342 was constitutional because the statute applied to all parts of the State, operated uniformly throughout, was not enacted to limit municipal legislative powers, prescribed a rule of conduct upon citizens generally, and, as such, was a general law.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and permanent injunction vacated.

 

616 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Trs. of the Tobacco Use Prevention & Control Found. v. Boyce


No. 2010-0118


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


127 Ohio St. 3d 511; 2010-Ohio-6207; 941 N.E.2d 745; 2010 Ohio LEXIS 3176


July 6, 2010, Submitted 
December 22, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Franklin County, Nos. 09AP-768, 09AP-769, 09AP-785, 09AP-786, 09AP-832, and 09AP-833,
Bd. of Trs. of the Tobacco Use Prevention & Control Found. v. Boyce, 185 Ohio App. 3d 707, 2009 Ohio 6993, 925 N.E.2d 641, 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 5858 (Ohio Ct. App., Franklin County, 2009).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a foundation and former cigarette smokers, sued appellee, the Treasurer of Ohio, for injunctive relief regarding a contract and to contest the constitutionality of Am. Sub. H.B. 544, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2008) and Am. Sub. S.B. 192, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2008). The court entered judgment against the foundation, but for the former smokers. The Court of Appeals of Ohio found that no contract was formed. A discretionary appeal was granted.


OVERVIEW: An endowment fund for tobacco use prevention and control was liquidated and the money in the fund was placed in a jobs fund. The issue presented was whether sections of Am. Sub. H.B. 544 and Am. Sub. S.B. 192 were constitutional. The state supreme court found that in 2000, a state agency was created to oversee the endowment fund. The agency, which entered into a contract with the foundation, was abolished in 2008. Further, the law enacted in 2000 did not create a right that was terminated by Am. Sub. H.B. 544 and, therefore, Am. Sub. H.B. 544 was not an unconstitutionally retroactive law under Ohio Const. art. II, § 28. In addition, Am. Sub. H.B. 544 and Am. Sub. S.B. 192 did not violate the Contract Clauses of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 because the agency was not a trust. Therefore, reallocating the funds appropriated to the endowment fund was not a violation of a trust contract. Furthermore, the agency's board violated R.C. 121.22 by deliberating in executive session upon contract matters that it was required to discuss in open session. Therefore, there was no violation of the Contract Clauses because no contract was formed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

 

617 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Kasich


No. 2012-0019


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


134 Ohio St. 3d 221; 2012-Ohio-5367; 981 N.E.2d 814; 2012 Ohio LEXIS 2899


April 24, 2012, Submitted 
November 27, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
ORIGINAL ACTION filed pursuant to Ohio Constitution, Article XI, Section 13.
Wilson v. Kasich, 131 Ohio St. 3d 1519, 2012 Ohio 1783, 965 N.E.2d 1002, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 876 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Relief denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, electors living in various house districts as reapportioned by the Ohio Apportionment Board, filed suit against respondents, four of the five Board members, seeking a judgment declaring that the apportionment plan approved by the Board did not comply with Ohio Const. art. XI, §§ 7 and 11, and a prohibitory injunction preventing respondents from conducting elections using the legislative districts set forth in the plan.


OVERVIEW: Relators did not name as parties the Board and the member who voted against the apportionment plan. The high court held that neither was a necessary and indispensable party to the action under Civ.R. 19. As long as the plan satisfied the requirements of Ohio Const. art. XI, respondents were not precluded from considering political factors in drafting it. The Board considered political factors only after the applicable constitutional and other legal requirements were met. The high court rejected relators' claim that the Board erred in relying on Ohio Const. art. XI, § 7(D) to justify violations of art. XI, § 7(A), (B), and (C) because § 7(D), being the last subsection, was subordinate to the other subsections. Art. XI, § 7(D) was coequal with art. XI, § 7(A), (B), and (C), and the high court would not order the Board to correct a violation of § 7(A), (B), and (C) by violating § 7(D). Given the discretion accorded respondents under § 7(D) and related provisions, relators did not establish beyond a reasonable doubt that respondents' purported failure to use the exact same boundary lines as the prior apportionment plan for a few districts constituted a violation of § 7(D).


OUTCOME: The relief requested was denied.

 

618 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Montgomery v. Leffler


Court of Appeals No. H-08-011


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, HURON COUNTY


2008-Ohio-6397; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 5334



December 5, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Trial Court No. CVH 20080142.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 1998, defendant was convicted of two counts of unlawful sexual conduct with a minor. Under the version of R.C. 2950 then effective, he was classified as a sexually oriented offender. In 2007, the Ohio Attorney General sent him a letter saying that, pursuant to Ohio's Adam Walsh Act, he was being reclassified as a Tier II offender. The Huron County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) that he had been appropriately reclassified. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that R.C. Chapter 2950, as amended by Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007), violated the federal and Ohio constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto or retroactive laws. The appellate court held that the approach employed in the new Adam Walsh Act remained only a modification in the classification, frequency, and duration of sexual offender registration and thus, was remedial and civil in nature. As the amendments were remedial in nature, they were not unconstitutional on retroactivity grounds. The prohibition against ex post facto laws concerned criminal matters only and had no application with respect to civil law. Since the amendments at issue were not punitive, but civil remedial measures, no multiple punishments were at issue, nor was the Eighth Amendment protection against cruel and unusual punishment implicated. Further, amended registration requirements did not offend defendant's right to contract as there was no evidence to establish that defendant's conviction was the result of a plea agreement, nor any suggestion of the terms of any such agreement. The trial court was not a party to such an agreement, and was not bound by its terms.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

619 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parker


CASE NO. 09 MA 136


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MAHONING COUNTY


186 Ohio App. 3d 600; 2010-Ohio-1092; 929 N.E.2d 516; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 899



March 18, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Common Pleas Court, Case No. 09CR384.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Mahoning County Common Pleas Court, Ohio, which convicted him of driving under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for driving under the influence after a police officer observed defendant's vehicle go left of center 4 times. The indictment indicated that defendant had been previously convicted of 5 or more violations of R.C. 4511.19(A) or (B). Defendant sought to dismiss the charge on the basis that the twenty year look back provision violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws. The motion was denied, defendant entered a no contest plea, and he was convicted. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that both the Ohio and United States Constitutions prohibited ex post facto laws. Such a law punished a crime as an act previously committed, which was innocent when done or which made more burdensome the punishment for a crime after its commission. The twenty year look back provision used past conduct to determine the classification and penalty for current conduct; it did not punish past conduct or create new penalties for the past conduct. An enhancement statute did not violate the prohibition against ex post facto laws. Therefore, the twenty year look back provision in R.C. 4511.19(G)(1)(d) was not an ex post facto law.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

620 of 997 DOCUMENTS


McCostlin v. State


CASE NO. 2008-L-117


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-4097; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3491



August 14, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by McCostlin v. State, 122 Ohio St. 3d 1497, 2009 Ohio 4221, 912 N.E.2d 103, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2282 (2009)
Discretionary appeal allowed by McCostlin v. State, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1506, 2009 Ohio 6210, 917 N.E.2d 810, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3362 (2009)
Affirmed by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Lake County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 M 000032.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual battery and ordered to register annually for a period of 10 years as a sexually oriented offender. He filed a petition to contest his sexual offender reclassification under the Adam Walsh Act. The Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denied the petition finding he was properly reclassified as a Tier III offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his reclassification as a Tier III offender was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the trial court erred. Since defendant's classification as a sexually oriented offender with definite registration requirements constituted a final order of the trial court, defendant could not, under separation of powers and res judicata principles, be reclassified under the provisions of the amended Adam Walsh Act, R.C. Chapter 2950, with differing registration requirements. Defendant's reclassification, as a practical matter, nullified that part of the trial court's previous judgment ordering him to register for a period of 10 years as a sexually oriented offender. A final judicial decision had been abrogated. Thus, to the extent that the Adam Walsh Act required the modification of existing final sentencing judgments, such as defendant's sentence, it violated the doctrine of separation of powers based on the finality of judicial judgments.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court reclassifying defendant as a Tier III sex offender was reversed. Defendant was required to continue registering as a sexually oriented offender as mandated in the original sentence.

 

621 of 997 DOCUMENTS


STATE ex rel. KILBANE v. INDUSTRIAL COMM'N OF OHIO


No. 99-1749


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


91 Ohio St. 3d 258; 744 N.E.2d 708; 2001 Ohio LEXIS 999


March 14, 2001, Submitted  
April 11, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Franklin County, No. 98AP-1210.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee moved for a hearing on the issue of settling her workers' compensation claim asserting that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4123.65 (1991), as it existed at the time her injury, applied. Appellee Ohio Industrial Commission denied her motion. Subsequently, the Court of Appeals for Franklin County (Ohio) denied appellant's writ of mandamus to invalidate the retroactive application of the statute. Appellant filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The reviewing court affirmed the denial of the writ of mandamus. Applying the test for unconstitutional retroactivity, the court determined that first, the legislature expressly intended § 4123.65 to apply retroactively, and second, that the law was not substantive, but remedial. Although appellant's entitlement to workers' compensation, being a substantive right, was measured by the statutes in force on the date of her injury, the same was not true for laws affecting only the enforcement of that right, such as § 4123.65. The prohibition against the legislature's passing of retroactive laws did not apply to remedial laws. Therefore, the statutory provisions could be changed or revoked by the legislature without offending the Ohio Constitution.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's denial of the writ of mandamus was affirmed.

Pickaway County Skilled Gaming LLC v. Cordray


No. 08AP-1032


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


183 Ohio App. 3d 390; 2009-Ohio-3483; 917 N.E.2d 305; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3025



July 16, 2009, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Discretionary appeal not allowed by Pickaway County Skilled Gaming L.L.C. v. Cordray, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1506, 2009 Ohio 6210, 917 N.E.2d 810, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3381 (2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by Pickaway County Skilled Gaming, L.L.C. v. Cordray, 2010 Ohio 4908, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 2499 (Ohio, Oct. 12, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 07CVH10-14821).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part; cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant amusement game arcade (AGA) owners sought review of a judgment from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which granted SJ to appellees, the Ohio Attorney General and other state and county officials, in the owners' action, challenging the constitutionality of R.C. 2915.01(AAA) and 2915.06, as well as Am. Sub. H.B. 177, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007).


OVERVIEW: The AGA was a members-only organization that required members to pay an annual fee for membership rights and privileges. The Ohio Governor declared an emergency and he authorized the immediate implementation of Ohio Admin. Code 109:4-3-31 regarding skill-based amusement machines. The owners were issued a cease and desist order. Due to passage of H.B. 177, the owners' declaratory judgment action was dismissed as moot. The owners thereafter filed their challenge to the constitutionality of §§ 2915.01(AAA) and 2915.06, which was resolved by SJ for appellees. On appeal, the court found that H.B. 177 was not a manifestly gross and fraudulent violation of the one-subject rule under Ohio Const. art. II, § 15 because the bill as a whole concerned gambling. Section 2915.06 was not vague or overbroad because it required a finding of recklessness under R.C. 2901.21(B) and 2901.22(C). However, R.C. 2915.01(AAA)(2) was violative of equal protection. A vagueness challenge to § 2915.01(AAA)(1) lacked merit, and the court lacked authority to review the emergency enactment of H.B. 177 based on a challenge to the right to referendum under Ohio Const. art. II, § 1c.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court with respect to a constitutionality determination regarding one provision of the challenged statute, and the matter was remanded with instructions to enter partial SJ to the owners regarding the statutory unconstitutionality under the equal protection clauses. The remainder of the trial court judgment was affirmed.

 

623 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Elswick


CASE NO. 2006-L-075


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2006-Ohio-7011; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 6957



December 29, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Elswick, 2007 Ohio 2208, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 1175 (Ohio, May 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 05 CR 000894.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) to failure to comply with the order or signal of a police officer and receiving stolen property and was sentenced to a total of four years in prison, including consecutive and greater than minimum sentences. Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said ex post facto and due process provisions barred his more than minimum sentences. The appellate court held he knew his potential sentences when committing his crimes and Foster did not change them. He had notice that Ohio's sentencing statutes were subject to judicial scrutiny, and he was unlikely to amend his criminal behavior due to a sentencing change, so Foster did not violate federal due process, nor was it impermissibly retroactive, under Ohio Const. art. II, § 28, because it created no substantively retroactive law, as any sentence presumed before Foster could be removed without defendant's consent, so it was not vested, nor could he enforce a specific sentence before sentencing. Foster's severance of unconstitutional sentencing statutes did not offend separation of powers because R.C. § 1.50 let the judiciary sever unconstitutional statutes. The rule of lenity did not apply to defendant because the statutes he was sentenced under were not ambiguous. Foster did not deprive him of meaningful appellate review by excising findings formerly required for certain sentences because it did not remove a requirement to consider other statutory factors.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

 

624 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Charette


CASE NO. 2008-L-069


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-2952; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2518



June 19, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 MS 000043.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition to contest his reclassification as a tier III sex offender under Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) (S.B. 10), in the Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio). The trial court denied his petition, after holding a hearing, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said S.B. 10's retroactive application to him was an ex post facto law barred by U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. The appellate court disagreed because S.B. 10 was civil. Its retroactive application did not violate Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 because it was remedial and procedural in nature. Its application did not violate the separation of powers doctrine, due to his prior adjudication as a sexually oriented offender, because (1) it did not order a court to reopen a final judgment but only changed the classification scheme, and (2) its requirements had always been the legislature's province. Its application did not violate his procedural due process rights by basing its requirements on his crime without a hearing because (1) a hearing was unnecessary as he was not denied a protected liberty or property interest, and (2) he had a hearing on the statute's application to him. He could not claim S.B. 10's residency restrictions violated his substantive due process rights in U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ohio Const. art. I, § 16, as well as the right to privacy guaranteed by Ohio Const. art. I, § 1, because he did not show or allege an actual injury.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Petralia


CASE NO. 2008-L-095


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-4450; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3774



August 28, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, in part State v. Petralia, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1522, 2009 Ohio 6487, 918 N.E.2d 525, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3577 (2009)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 MS 000058.
State v. Petralia, 2003 Ohio 1745, 2003 Ohio App. LEXIS 1659 (Ohio Ct. App., Lake County, Apr. 4, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sexual offender pled guilty to four counts of gross sexual imposition and was found to be a sexual predator. He was later notified that he had been reclassified as a Tier III sex offender. He petitioned to contest the reclassification. The Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denied the petition, finding that he had been properly reclassified under the new version of R.C. Chapter 2950. The offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: The offender argued that S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2008) was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the Adam Walsh Child Protection and Safety Act (AWA), as applied to the offender, did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The registration and notification scheme was not punitive in nature, but rather civil and remedial. Thus, no abrogation of final judicial decisions occurred when the offender was reclassified and subjected to additional requirements. Because it was civil in nature and not punitive in intent of effect, and not substantive, it was not an ex post facto law, or a retroactive law, and it did not constitute a second punishment prohibited by the double jeopardy provision. Additionally, because the offender failed to show an actual deprivation of his property rights, he did not have standing to challenge the residency restriction of S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2008). Finally, the new sexual offender scheme did not constitute a breach of a prior plea agreement as the registration and notification requirements did not affect any plea agreement previously entered into between the offender and the State.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Cisternino


CASE NO. 2010-L-031


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2011-Ohio-2453; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 2092



May 20, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 09 CR 000544.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of burglary, in violation of R.C. 2911.12(A)(4), and two counts of receiving stolen property, in violation of R.C. 2913.51(A). The Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) sentenced him to 60 months in prison and ordered him to pay restitution to three of the four victims. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by imposing consecutive sentences. The appellate court held that the trial court was not required to make judicial fact-finding prior to imposing consecutive sentences for defendant's multiple offenses. Further, the sentence was not clearly and convincingly contrary to law because the trial court properly applied the purposes and factors in R.C. 2929.11 and R.C. 2929.12 and was not an abuse of discretion because the trial court emphasized defendant's lengthy criminal record and noted that he had been preying on society for most of his adult life. Further, the trial court's statement that it had considered defendant's ability to pay restitution satisfied the requirement of R.C. 2929.19(B)(6). Finally, there was no error in the amount of restitution under R.C. 2929.18. Although the total amount of restitution ($15,750) defendant was ordered to pay slightly exceeded the total amount stipulated in the plea agreement ($15,000), the trial court ensured that defendant understood that he was waiving any error in the restitution amount regarding one count. Defendant waived any claim by not objecting.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Yarbrough


CASE NO. 17-2000-10


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT, SHELBY COUNTY


2001-Ohio-2351; 2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 1930



April 30, 2001, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Common Pleas Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Shelby County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) which dismissed his petition for postconviction relief brought pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2953.21.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated murder, including death penalty specifications, and conspiracy to commit aggravated murder. Later, appellant filed a petition for postconviction relief. The trial court granted the State's motion to dismiss. On appeal, the appellate court determined that because appellant had failed to produce sufficient, credible evidence demonstrating that he had suffered an infringement or deprivation of his constitutional rights, substantive grounds for relief did not exist. Therefore, the appellate court concluded appellant was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing on his claims for relief, and the trial court properly dismissed his petition for postconviction relief. Further, the appellate court could not say that the failure to afford appellant discovery during the initial proceeding to determine whether an evidentiary hearing was warranted rendered the postconviction relief process unconstitutional. Finally, the appellate court determined the doctrine of cumulative error was not applicable as the appellate court had found no merit to appellant's claims of trial court error.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Maynard


No. 11AP-697


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2012-Ohio-2946; 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 2576



June 28, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Maynard, 133 Ohio St. 3d 1467, 2012 Ohio 5149, 977 N.E.2d 694, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 2808 (2012)
Reopening denied by State v. Maynard, 2013 Ohio 802, 2013 Ohio App. LEXIS 714 (Ohio Ct. App., Franklin County, Mar. 7, 2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Maynard v. Oppy, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 18686 (S.D. Ohio, Feb. 17, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 10CR-05-3189).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Franklin County Court of Common Plea (Ohio), convicting him, upon a jury's verdict, of felony murder, in violation of R.C. 2903.02(B), aggravated robbery, aggravated burglary, felonious assault, and the accompanying firearm specifications.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted as an accomplice in connection with the murder of a victim, who was shot during a home invasion in which the offenders planned to rob a drug dealer. The dealer was shot at the scene, but survived his injuries. Defendant first challenged the constitutionality of the felony murder statute, arguing that it impermissibly allowed the State to ignore its standard of proof and to prove its case by stacking one inference on top of another. While R.C. 2903.02(B) did not require proof of specific intent to kill, the statue was constitutional. Whether the conviction was based upon inference stacking went to the sufficiency of the evidence, not the constitutionality of the statute. Moreover, there was no impermissible inference stacking in the instant matter, and the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for felony murder as an accomplice under R.C. 2923.03(A)(2). Next, defendant's decision to attend the birth of his child instead of appearing for one day of his trial was a voluntary absence, not a violation of Crim.R. 43(A), as it was the product of defendant's own free choice and unrestrained will. Finally, there was no prosecutorial misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Patrick v. Larson


CASE NO. 99 CA 222


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MAHONING COUNTY


2000-Ohio-2569; 2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 4607



September 29, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from Common Pleas Court, Domestic Relations Division, Case No. 92 DR 650.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed the decision of the Mahoning County Common Pleas Court, Domestic Relations Division (Ohio), which denied defendant father's motion to emancipate his minor child in cause of action brought against defendant by plaintiff mother for child support.


OVERVIEW: After plaintiff mother and defendant father were divorced, defendant was order to pay child support to plaintiff for plaintiff and defendant's son until the son reached the age of 18 or graduated from high school, which ever event came last. Defendant stopped paying child support when his son turned 19-years old. Plaintiff brought a cause of action against defendant for child support. Defendant motioned to emancipate his son. The magistrate denied defendant's motion to emancipate. The trial court adopted the magistrate's decision. The court affirmed. The 19-year cut-off age for child support found in Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3109.05(E) (amended 1997) did not apply retroactively to the child support order detailing defendant's obligations. Former Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3109.05(E) did not contain a cut-off age for a child attending high school; therefore, defendant was obligated to pay child support until his son left high school.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Defendant father was obligated to pay child support until his son left high school because the 19-year cut-off age did not apply retroactively to the child support order detailing the father's obligations.

N&G Constr. v. City of Pataskala


Case No. 01CA00057


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LICKING COUNTY


2001-Ohio-1810; 2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 5216



November 21, 2001, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Licking County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 00CV876.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, reversed, in part, and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed a denial of its motion for summary judgment by the Licking County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) in its suit against defendant city, claiming error in applying the statute of limitations and in dismissing its substantive due process and selective enforcement claims.


OVERVIEW: The landowner purchased property in an agricultural zone of a township with 10-acre size limitations. An amendment changed the size to two acres. The township and a village merged to become the city. In a special meeting and an executive session the city refused to recognize the amendment. The public never received notice of the meeting or of the proposed amendment. The landowner sued, claiming the city's actions were unconstitutional. The trial court overruling the landowner's motion for summary judgment and sua sponte dismissed the case in its entirety. The appellate court held that any procedural due process claims must have been brought within two years. However, the landowner's substantive due process claims were not barred. Because the claim for selective enforcement of the amendment was not a procedural attack, it was also not barred.


OUTCOME: The denial of the landowner's procedural due process claims was affirmed. The denial of its substantive due process and selective enforcement claims was reversed and remanded.

State v. Millhoan


Court of Appeals Nos. L-10-1328, L-10-1329


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LUCAS COUNTY


2011-Ohio-4741; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 3941



September 2, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Trial Court Nos. CR0201002702, CR0201001265.



DISPOSITION: JUDMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, in consolidated cases, was convicted in the Lucas County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) of multiple counts of rape, in violation of R.C. 2907.02, gross sexual imposition, in violation of R.C. 2907.05, and unlawful sexual conduct with a minor, in violation of R.C. 2907.04(A). The trial court imposed a sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his guilty pleas were not entered knowingly and voluntarily, that the imposition of near-maximum consecutive sentences was unwarranted, and that he was denied effective assistance of trial counsel. On appeal, the court found that Crim. R. 11 did not require the court to explain that defendant's sentences for multiple offenses could be run consecutively. Moreover, although not required, the trial court did essentially advise defendant of the maximum consecutive penalty he could receive for all the offenses. In addition, the trial court did not err by imposing consecutive sentences without making findings pursuant to R.C. 2929.14(E)(4) because R.C. 2929.14(E)(4) was declared unconstitutional and severed from the sentencing code. Furthermore, the trial court did not err in imposing near-maximum consecutive sentences because the trial court considered the purposes and principles of sentencing under R.C. 2929.11, as well as the seriousness and recidivism factors listed in R.C. 2929.12. Additionally, the rape and sexual imposition counts were not allied offenses under R.C. 2941.25. Finally, defendant's trial counsel was not prejudicially ineffective.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Foster


Case No. 2006 CA 00152


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LICKING COUNTY


2008-Ohio-29; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 25



January 7, 2008, Date of Judgment Entry


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Foster, 118 Ohio St. 3d 1461, 2008 Ohio 2823, 888 N.E.2d 1113, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 1701 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Foster v. Ohio, 555 U.S. 1052, 129 S. Ct. 633, 172 L. Ed. 2d 620, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 8591 (2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Adams v. Kelly, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 54026 (N.D. Ohio, Mar. 8, 2011)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal Appeal From Licking County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 03 CR 152.
State v. Foster, 109 Ohio St. 3d 1, 2006 Ohio 856, 845 N.E.2d 470, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 516 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed after the Licking County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), in a Foster remand, resentenced defendant on 26 felony counts, to which he had entered no contest pleas. In a sentencing memorandum filed before the resentencing, defendant had argued that the application of Foster violated the ex post facto and due process clauses of the federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Alternatively, defendant had asked for a continuance of the resentencing hearing so he could file a motion to withdraw his no contest pleas. As to the constitutionality of the sentences imposed at the resentencing, the appellate court noted that it had previously rejected similar ex post facto and due process arguments. Further, post-Foster, trial courts were still required to consider the purposes of sentencing found in R.C. 2929.11 and the factors found in R.C. 2929.12 relating to the seriousness of the offense and the recidivism of the offender. Thus, Foster did not unconstitutionally prohibit meaningful appellate review or destroy the legislative intent of the purpose and principles of sentencing. Defendant's claim that the trial court abused its discretion in failing to grant defendant a hearing on his motion to withdraw his guilty plea also failed. The minimum mandates of due process were satisfied because defendant was allowed to present the substance of his argument as to why he should be allowed to withdraw his plea during the resentencing hearing, and the trial court sufficiently inquired into the reasons for the motion to withdraw.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

635 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Alsina


CASE NO. 2011-A-0016


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ASHTABULA COUNTY


2011-Ohio-6692; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 5530



December 27, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Criminal Appeal from the Ashtabula County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 2011 CR 18.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Ashtabula County Court of Common Pleas, Ohio, which imposed a sentence for attempted aggravated murder of a police officer, felonious assault, and having weapons while under disability.


OVERVIEW: Defendant opened fire on a police officer, who was patrolling an area known for illegal narcotics. Defendant later entered a guilty plea to three offenses, and a sentence was imposed. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that there was no violation of defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. VI. After the decision in State v. Foster, judicial fact-finding was not required before the imposition of a consecutive sentence. The sentence imposed in this case was not clearly and convincingly contrary to law because the sentence was within the statutory range for each offense. The trial court considered both R.C. 2929.11 and R.C. 2929.12. Moreover, the sentence did not amount to an abuse of discretion because due deliberation was given to the relevant statutory considerations. The trial court emphasized defendant's lengthy criminal record and found that consecutive sentences were necessary to protect the public and to punish defendant. Finally, the decision in Foster did not prohibit the trial court from considering sentencing factors found in the portions of the sentencing statute that had been declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

City of Tipp City v. Peachey


Appellate Case No. 99-CA-27


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MIAMI COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 3147



July 14, 2000, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Trial Court Case No. 98-CRB-4844.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court reversed, and the fine and assessment of court costs vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Miami County (Ohio) Municipal Court, which found her guilty of violating Tipp City, Ohio, Code of Ordinances § 154.052, and ordered her to pay a fine and court costs.


OVERVIEW: Appellant installed an awning on the front of her restaurant, which was located within the city's restoration and architectural district. Appellee city sent a notice to appellant, informing her that the awning was in violation of local ordinance, and ordering her to return the building to its previous condition or to obtain a certificate of appropriateness for the awning from the architectural review board. Appellant took no action in response to the letter. Appellee filed a complaint, and the trial court found appellant guilty and assessed a $ 50 fine and court costs. On appeal, appellant argued that the statute, as applied, was unconstitutionally vague. The court agreed and reversed, holding that, in particular, the phrase "material change" in the ordinance did not mean only a "change of materials" as contended by appellee. Clearly, a "material change" would not encompass just any change of materials at all.


OUTCOME: Trial court reversed. Appellee failed to enact guidelines governing application of the ordinance, and it was unconstitutionally vague as applied. In particular, "material change" in the ordinance would not encompass just any change of materials.

Amburgy v. Village of South Lebanon


CASE NO. CA2001-07-065


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, WARREN COUNTY


2002 Ohio App. LEXIS 2670



May 20, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CIVIL APPEAL FROM COMMON PLEAS COURT.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff gravel company sued defendant village seeking relief from South Lebanon, Ohio, Ordinance 2000-15, in the form of preliminary and permanent injunctions, declaratory relief, and money damages. The Warren County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) granted the gravel company's motion for preliminary and permanent injunctions. The village appealed.


OVERVIEW: The village argued that the trial court failed to review the ordinance in question under the mandatory equal protection analysis required under a rational-basis test. The village maintained the court failed to give the village legislation the presumption of validity with regard to South Lebanon, Ohio, Ordinance 2000-15; failed to presume the validity of the distinction between "through trucks" and other trucks; and further failed to acknowledge the evidence before it regarding the different impacts "through trucks" were having on the village. The court of appeals noted that the ordinance infringed upon a fundamental right, and therefore, should have been evaluated under a compelling-interest test. The court of appeals concluded that South Lebanon, Ohio, Ordinance 2000-15 was not narrowly tailored to serve a compelling state interest and it gave preference to one class of truck over another; consequently it was invalid. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting the injunction and finding the village ordinance unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

638 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Candela


CASE NO. 2008-A-0068


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ASHTABULA COUNTY


2009-Ohio-4096; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3495



August 14, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Ashtabula County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 2007 CR 266.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered an Alford plea to attempted rape and gross sexual imposition. He filed a motion opposing the retroactive application of the Adam Walsh Child Protection and Safety Act (AWA), R.C. Chapter 2950, and requested that he be classified pursuant to the former law. The Ashtabula County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) classified him as a Tier III offender under the AWA. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the retroactive application of the AWA violated the Ex Post Facto Clause of the United States Constitution and the Retroactivity Clause of the Ohio Constitution. The appellate court held that the trial court had no discretion not to apply the current version of the statute. The AWA was applicable because of defendant's sentencing date. However, even if the AWA had been applied retroactively, the retroactive application would still have been constitutional in the absence of a prior final sentencing judgment or order. Since the two prongs of the intent-effects ex post facto test were satisfied, the Ohio General Assembly intended that the current provisions of R.C. Chapter 2950 be remedial and any punitive affect of the provisions were insufficient to negate the remedial purpose. Therefore, the AWA did not violate ex post facto or the prohibition against retroactive laws. Further, there was no violation of separation of powers or res judicata because defendant had never been classified as a sexual offender since his original classification was under the AWA. Thus, the judgment of the trial court was never annulled, reversed, or modified.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Robins


C.A. CASE NO. 23437


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2010-Ohio-2842; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 2321



June 18, 2010, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
(Civil appeal from Common Pleas Court). T.C. NO. 08 CV 924.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a convicted sex offender, sought review of the judgment of the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which held that R.C. 2950.02 et seq. was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The offender was classified as a sexually oriented offender. He later received a notice of new classification and registration duties from the attorney general, reclassifying him, pursuant to the Adam Walsh Act (AWA), as a Tier I sex offender and requiring him to register with the local sheriff's office once a year for 15 years. The offender filed a petition to contest the AWA, arguing that the AWA violated the separation of powers doctrine. However, the trial court held that the AWA did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. On appeal, the court noted that, following the trial court's decision, the Supreme Court of Ohio had held in Bodyke that portions of the AWA found in R.C. 2950.031 and 2950.032 violated the separation of powers doctrine, and it excised these provisions from the AWA. Thus, the court reversed the trial court's judgment that the AWA did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The court reinstated the offender's previous classification.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Delgado


No. 90331


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2008-Ohio-3545; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 3001



July 17, 2008, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Criminal Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CR-469536.
State v. Delgado, 2006 Ohio 5928, 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 5848 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, Nov. 9, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which, upon resentencing under Foster, imposed consecutive terms of imprisonment on him. He had been convicted of five counts of vehicular assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for 18 counts of vehicular assault. He entered a guilty plea to five of the charges and the remainder were dismissed. The trial court imposed consecutive terms of imprisonment on defendant. Upon a prior direct appeal, the conviction was affirmed, but the sentence was vacated and remanded for resentencing pursuant to Foster. Upon resentencing, the trial court imposed the same consecutive terms of imprisonment on defendant. On appeal again, the court found that defendant's argument that application of post-Foster sentencing principles to him violated his due process and ex post facto protections lacked merit. Foster did not judicially increase the range of defendant's sentence, it did not retroactively apply a new statutory maximum to an earlier committed crime, and it did not create the possibility of consecutive sentences where none existed previously.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


 

642 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cole


CASE NO. 01 CA 73


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MAHONING COUNTY


2002-Ohio-5191; 2002 Ohio App. LEXIS 5233



September 26, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from the Youngstown Municipal Court of Mahoning County, Ohio. Case No. 00 TRD 4216.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a plea of no contest, pursuant to Ohio R. Crim. P. 11, to violating a loud music ordinance. He was sentenced on the charge, as a second offense. Following the entry of judgment and sentence, by the Youngstown Municipal Court of Mahoning County, Ohio, defendant appealed, arguing that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague, overbroad, and violated the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's plea of no contest was an admission that he was playing loud music in and from his automobile, so as to violate the ordinance. The appellate court found that an enactment was void for vagueness if its prohibitions were not clearly defined. In the instant case, the fact that the ordinance did not define the phrase, "disturb the quiet, comfort, or repose," did not render the ordinance impermissibly vague. The phrase was substantially synonymous with "disturbing the peace." Whether or not conduct was deemed to "disturb the peace" was measured by the reasonableness of the conduct as viewed in the light of the surrounding facts and circumstances. It was not unconstitutionally vague. Nor was it unconstitutionally overbroad. The city had an interest in protecting its citizens from unwelcome noise. The ordinance was not primarily directed at the content of the speech but at the volume of the noise coming from automobile audio systems. The ordinance's prescription against loud noises was primarily an attempt to control conduct, i.e., the use of the volume control, rather than an attempt to control the type of speech being broadcast. None of defendant's arguments were persuasive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Antonellis


Case No. 2005-CA-31


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LICKING COUNTY


2005-Ohio-5381; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 4879



October 6, 2005, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from the Licking County Municipal Court, Case No. 04TRC09097.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Municipal Court of Licking County, Ohio, which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited concentration of alcohol on his breath. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to dismiss based on the destruction of the videotape evidence and also erred in allowing evidence of field sobriety tests that were not administrated in compliance with regulations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for a traffic offense and performed field sobriety tests. While the trooper had defendant perform the finger-to-nose test, the videotape of this test was inadvertently taped over later. Defendant submitted to a breath test, which registered .088. He was arrested. On appeal from the judgment of conviction, the court found that defendant's motion to dismiss the charges against him based on the destruction of the videotape evidence was properly overruled because defendant did not show bad faith on the part of the police relating to the destruction of the evidence, and the State did not use the evidence in its prosecution of the case. With respect to defendant's contention that evidence of the horizontal gaze nystigmus test performed was erroneously admitted when it was not administered in strict compliance with the National Highway Transportation Safety Administration (NHTSA) requirements, the court declined to determine the constitutionality of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.19(D), which required only substantial compliance with NHTSA requirements, because the jury acquitted defendant on the charge of violating § 4511.19(A)(1) and, thus, the issue was rendered moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Home Builders Ass'n v. City of Lebanon


CASE NO. CA2003-12-115


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, WARREN COUNTY


2004-Ohio-4526; 2004 Ohio App. LEXIS 4111



August 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Home Builders Ass'n of Dayton v. City of Lebanon, 2006 Ohio 595, 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 560 (Ohio Ct. App., Warren County, Feb. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CIVIL APPEAL FROM WARREN COUNTY COURT OF COMMON PLEAS. Case No. 02CV59491.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas reversed; matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After plaintiffs, a home builders association and others, sued defendant city in the Warren County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), challenging an ordinance requiring a connection to the city's broadband system, for a fee, intervenor cable service provider intervened, claiming the ordinance violated Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1332.04. The trial court granted the city's motion to dismiss the cable service's complaint, and the cable service appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1332.04, precluding political subdivisions providing cable service from discriminating against private providers, was an unconstitutional interference with the city's exercise of its police power. The appellate court held the cable service's complaint that the town's ordinance violated Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1332.04(B)(1)(a) and (b), that the service was a cable provider in the city, and that the provider was adversely affected as the city's violations of § 1332.04(B) gave an advantage to the city's telecommunications system, contrary to the statute, was improperly dismissed pursuant to Ohio R. Civ. P. 12(B)(6), as all elements of a cause of action were adequately pled. When the trial court entertained the parties' constitutional arguments, it exceeded the appropriate scope of review on a motion to dismiss. When appealing the trial court's denial of its motion to dismiss, the cable provider did not point to an exception to the general rule that denials of summary judgment were not appealable, so the appellate court had no jurisdiction to consider the issue.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was reversed, and the matter was remanded.
