State v. Brownlee


Appellate Case No. 2008-CA-105


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, GREENE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-5396; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 4564



October 9, 2009, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Brownlee, 124 Ohio St. 3d 1477, 2010 Ohio 354, 921 N.E.2d 247, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 378 (Ohio, Feb. 10, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
(Criminal Appeal from Common Pleas Court). Trial Court Case No. 2003-CR-260.
City of Middleburg Heights v. Brownlee, 2008 Ohio 2036, 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 1739 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, May 1, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Greene County Common Pleas Court (Ohio) that denied his motion for "declassification" as a registered sex offender; defendant claimed the trial court erred in applying R.C. 2950.15 because he was sentenced before its effective date.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to community control and classified as a sexually oriented offender following his 2003 conviction on charges of importuning, attempted unlawful sexual conduct with a minor, pandering sexually oriented material involving a minor, and illegal use of a minor in nudity oriented material. When the Ohio legislature enacted S.B. 10 in 2008, defendant was not reclassified, apparently due to his move to Pennsylvania. The trial court denied defendant's motion for declassification due to the absence of the required documentation. The appellate court found, inter alia, that although the trial court should not have denied defendant's motion for failure to comply with the documentation requirements of R.C. 2950.15, its error was harmless as a matter of law. Rather, it should have denied the motion for a more fundamental reason. Defendant was not a Tier I sex offender, and nothing in the law that existed prior to the S.B. 10 amendments provided for declassification before expiration of the 10-year registration term. Accordingly, the trial court did not err in overruling defendant's motion for declassification under § 2950.15.


OUTCOME: The assignment of error was overruled, and the judgment was affirmed.

Burden v. Ohio Dep't of Job & Family Servs.


No. 11AP-832


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2012-Ohio-1552; 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 1366



April 5, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Burden v. Ohio Dep't of Job & Family Servs., 132 Ohio St. 3d 1514, 2012 Ohio 4021, 974 N.E.2d 112, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 2121 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 10CVF-08-12006).
Burden v. Ohio Dep't of Job & Family Servs., 2011 Ohio Misc. LEXIS 20708 (Ohio C.P., Sept. 13, 2011)
Burden v. Life Ins. Co. of N. Am., 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 50154 (S.D. Ohio, Apr. 27, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee department of jobs and family services informed appellant home care giver that it intended to terminate her Ohio Medicaid provider agreement. A hearing examiner determined that the department was entitled to terminate the provider agreement for violations of former Ohio Admin. Code 5101:3-1-17.6(D). The Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) affirmed the decision. The care giver appealed.


OVERVIEW: The care giver argued that the trial court erred by affirming the department's order. The appellate court held that the trial court did not err by deferring to the department's reasonable interpretation of former Ohio Admin. Code 5101:3-45-10(C)(7) or by concluding that the care giver had accepted, obtained, or attempted to obtain something of value from the consumer during her provision of authorized services. She knew that she was listed as the sole beneficiary of his life insurance policy several years prior to his death. It was not unreasonable to conclude that the beneficiary designation constituted something of value and that, at the very least, the care giver attempted, during her provision of authorized services, to obtain something of value from the consumer, regardless of the purity of her motives or intentions. Further, even assuming the care giver's standing to raise constitutional challenges, Ohio Admin. Code 5101:3-45-10(C)(7) was not unconstitutional as applied because it did not substantially impair the consumer's contractual relationship or his contractual right to designate a life insurance beneficiary.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Delgado


No. 87614


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2006-Ohio-5928; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 5848



November 9, 2006, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Delgado, 113 Ohio St. 3d 1444, 2007 Ohio 1266, 863 N.E.2d 659, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 714 (2007)
Appeal after remand at State v. Delgado, 2008 Ohio 3545, 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 3001 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, July 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CR-469536.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to five counts of vehicular assault. The Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) accepted the plea and sentenced him to five consecutive one-year terms of imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his guilty plea was not knowingly, intelligently or voluntarily made. The appellate court held that the trial court fully complied with both the constitutional and non-constitutional provisions of Crim. R. 11 before accepting defendant's plea. It also properly explained that by pleading guilty, defendant waived his right to confront witnesses, his right to compulsory process, and his right to require the State to prove his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. Moreover, contrary to defendant's claim, the trial court informed defendant of his right against self-incrimination in a reasonably intelligible manner which did not convey to defendant that if he elected to testify, such testimony would have been meaningless. There was no indication that the remark engendered any confusion or misunderstanding. Further, defendant's counsel stated on the record that he had explained defendant's rights to him. However, because the trial court relied upon statutory provisions when it imposed sentencing, which had been found to be unconstitutional due to judicial factfinding, the sentences were vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The sentencing judgment was vacated and the cause was remanded for resentencing.

Stay lifted by Tribett v. Shepherd, 144 Ohio St. 3d 1474, 2016-Ohio-467, 2016 Ohio LEXIS 279, 45 N.E.3d 242 (2016)
Motion denied by Tribett v. Shepherd, 145 Ohio St. 3d 1413, 2016-Ohio-957, 2016 Ohio LEXIS 706, 47 N.E.3d 159 (2016)

City of Canton v. State


Case No. 2000CA00076


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, STARK COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 4761



October 10, 2000, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Stark County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 1999CV00689.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; Final judgment entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State and officials appealed Stark County Common Pleas Court (Ohio) declaration, sought by plaintiff city, finding Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3781.194, which among other things limited municipalities' rights to exclude manufactured housing from single-family residence zones, to violate the home rule amendment, Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city's zoning ordinance banning manufactured housing from single-family residence zones conflicted with Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3781.184, which banned such ordinances. Plaintiff argued that the statute was a special statute that unconstitutionally limited the home rule rights guaranteed by Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3, rather than a general statute, that would have pre-empted its ordinance. The court held, looking to the statute as a whole, that it was a general statute, because although one provision dealt with zoning, there were other provisions dealing with various aspects of manufactured housing, so that its clear intent was to regulate the whole subject matter. The statute operated uniformly throughout the state, prescribed rules for citizens generally, and operated uniformly throughout the state under the same circumstances and conditions. The mere fact that the legislature decided not to proscribe private restrictive covenants forbidding such housing did not make the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, and entered final judgment of constitutionality. Viewed as a whole, the statute clearly sought to regulate manufactured housing throughout Ohio, so it was a general statute, not a special one, and pre-empted conflicting ordinances of individual cities.

 

654 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ferguson


No. 88450


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2007-Ohio-2777; 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 2570



June 7, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, in part State v. Ferguson, 115 Ohio St. 3d 1472, 2007 Ohio 5735, 875 N.E.2d 626, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2809 (2007)
Motion denied by State v. Ferguson, 117 Ohio St. 3d 1494, 2008 Ohio 2151, 885 N.E.2d 952, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 1766 (2008)
Affirmed by State v. Ferguson, 2008 Ohio 4824, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 2589 (Ohio, Oct. 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CR-254450.
State v. Ferguson, 1992 Ohio App. LEXIS 2822 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, June 4, 1992)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which adjudicated him as a sexual predator pursuant to R.C. § 2950.09(B)(2). Defendant had been convicted of rape and kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to a term of imprisonment after he was convicted, which convictions were affirmed on direct appeal. Years later, defendant was classified as a sexual predator. On appeal, the court found that the trial court properly addressed the necessary statutory factors under § 2950.09(B)(2) in finding that defendant was a sexual predator. The court noted that the trial court did not have to individually assess each of the statutory factors in making its sexual predator determination. Further, the trial court made findings regarding the sexual predator classification based on defendant's prior rape conviction as well as his moderate to high risk of reoffense. The trial court was not required to find that defendant was an habitual sexual offender, as he was convicted before January 1, 1997 and he was found to have been a sexual predator. The sexual predator legislation pursuant to R.C. § 2950.01 et seq. was not an unconstitutional ex post facto law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Beaver Excavating Co. v. Levin


No. 10AP-581


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2011-Ohio-3649; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 3085



July 26, 2011, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by Beaver Excavating Co. v. Testa, 130 Ohio St. 3d 1493, 2011 Ohio 6556, 958 N.E.2d 956, 2011 Ohio LEXIS 3186 (2011)
Motion granted by Beaver Excavating Co. v. Levin, 131 Ohio St. 3d 1451, 2012 Ohio 578, 961 N.E.2d 688, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 391 (2012)
Motion granted by Beaver Excavating Co. v. Testa, 131 Ohio St. 3d 1513, 2012 Ohio 1720, 965 N.E.2d 313, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 869 (2012)
Reversed by, Cause remanded by Beaver Excavating Co. v. Testa, 2012 Ohio 5776, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 3153 (Ohio, Dec. 7, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 08CVH-03-3921).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, contractors and county engineers, brought a declaratory judgment action against appellee, the Tax Commissioner of Ohio, in the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), to challenge the constitutionality of the Ohio Commercial Activity Tax (CAT), R.C. 5751.01 et seq. The court found that the CAT was constitutional and granted summary judgment to the Tax Commissioner. The contractors and the county engineers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The contractors and the county engineers contended that the CAT was unconstitutional to the extent that moneys derived from the CAT which related to sales of motor vehicle fuel were not being expended for the purposes enumerated in Ohio Const. art. XII, § 5a. On appeal, the court found that Ohio's CAT, measured by gross receipts, including receipts from the sale of motor vehicle fuel, was not a tax upon motor vehicle fuel. Whether the CAT related to the sale of motor vehicle fuel was not supported by the background and history of § 5a which historically was interpreted to apply to the specific taxes and not to general taxes. While in a sense the CAT, as applied to the contractors and the county engineers, had some relation to motor vehicle fuel, the relationship was too attenuated to find that the statutory allocation of the CAT moneys violated § 5a. The contractors and the county engineers were not able to show beyond a reasonable doubt that the legislation and constitutional provisions were clearly incompatible.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. VFW Post 431

On appeal, defendant argued, among other things, that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2915.01 et seq. was unconstitutional.

State ex rel. Donovan v. Zajac


ACCELERATED CASE NO. 2001-G-2331


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, GEAUGA COUNTY


2001-Ohio-4294; 2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 4448



September 28, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas/Juvenile Division. Case No. 95 PN 000608.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a judgment from the Geauga County Court of Common Pleas, Juvenile Division (Ohio) that denied his motions: (1) to stay an ex parte order/notice to withhold child support, (2) for a hearing on order/notice to withhold income for child support, (3) to prohibit an award of arrearages for child support, and (4) for other relief.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the father argued that: (1) the child support enforcement agency failed to send him advance notice of the child support order; the amount withheld from his disability benefits should have been determined by the trial court and not by the agency; and (3) he should not have been required to pay child support arrearages because he did not know that the child was his until 1995, when she was almost 18 years old. The father's receipt of the appellate court's previous opinion telling him he owed $ 54,450 was insufficient to constitute advance notice. In the absence of advance notice and the opportunity to request an administrative hearing with the agency, the father's request for a hearing by the trial court should have been honored. The trial court did not meet the level of specificity required by Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3113.21(A)(1) in ordering the amount to be withheld from the father's disability benefits. The father's argument that he should not have been required to pay child support arrearages was without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

State v. Caudill

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from the Ashland County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 02-CRI-075.

DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Ashland County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which convicted him of felonious assault and tampering with evidence, in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 2903.11 and 2921.12. Defendant was sentenced to consecutive terms of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted and sentenced, he filed a prior appeal which resulted in a remand for re-sentencing pursuant to Comer. Upon remand, the same sentence was imposed by the trial court without a hearing. On a second appeal, the court again remanded for re-sentencing, based on its holding that the trial court erred in holding the re-sentencing proceeding outside of defendant's presence. At the re-sentencing hearing on remand, all parties had an opportunity to be heard. The trial court thereafter entered consecutive terms of imprisonment and ordered defendant to pay restitution to the victim for medical bills. On appeal, the court found that the sentence was based on unconstitutional statutes pursuant to the Foster decision. OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, vacated the sentence imposed after re-sentencing, and remanded the matter for re-sentencing.

Woods v. Telb


No. 99-1419


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


89 Ohio St. 3d 504; 2000-Ohio-171; 733 N.E.2d 1103; 2000 Ohio LEXIS 1856


April 12, 2000 Submitted at the Geauga County Session  
August 3, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 20, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Lucas County, No. L-99-1083.

On September 13, 1996, Milton Woods, the petitioner herein, pled guilty to theft ( R.C. 2913.02[A]), a fifth-degree felony. Petitioner executed the plea form in open court which provided that, "If I receive prison for a felony 3, 4, or 5, I may be given up to 3 years of post release control. If I violate conditions of supervision while under post release control, the parole board could return me to prison for up to nine months for each violation, for a total of 50% of my originally stated term. If the violation is a new felony I could receive a new prison term of the greater of one year or the time remaining on post release control."

On September 25, 1996, pursuant to the plea, petitioner was sentenced to serve ten months in prison. The sentencing entry provided: "Defendant is notified that * * * after prison release, if post-release control is imposed, for violations of post release control conditions, the adult parole authority or parole board may impose a more restrictive or longer control sanction, return defendant to prison for up to nine months for each violation, up to a maximum of [***2] 50% of the stated term. If the violation is a new felony, defendant may receive a new prison term of the greater of one year or the time remaining on post release control."

Petitioner served his complete ten-month prison sentence and on June 17, 1997, the APA placed him on three years of post-release control. On June 18, 1997, petitioner reported to the Toledo District Office and signed the conditions of supervision. As part of his post-release control, petitioner was placed in a substance abuse program and ordered to submit to weekly urine screenings. In addition, he was ordered to report to the APA office monthly and to actively seek employment. When petitioner failed to attend the substance abuse program, failed to report to his post-release control officer, and failed to report for his weekly drug screening, an arrest order was issued July 2, 1997. Petitioner was arrested on July 10, 1997, and under the terms of his post-release control, the APA imposed sanctions that petitioner attend and successfully complete a day-reporting program and that petitioner report to one of the APA's chemical dependency specialists. After petitioner tested positive for alcohol and cocaine use, the [***3] Toledo Police Department arrested him on July 22, 1997, for drug abuse, a charge that was later dismissed due to the fact that the substance found in petitioner's possession was counterfeit.

As a result of the drug abuse charge, the APA held a violation hearing on August 19, 1997, and at that time, the hearing officer sanctioned petitioner to a halfway house, where he was also to become involved in a substance abuse program, attend daily Narcotics Anonymous and Alcohol Anonymous meetings, and submit to weekly urine screenings. On October 17, 1997, petitioner was arrested at the halfway house when he was suspected of a theft, but that charge was later dropped. Petitioner was successfully discharged from the halfway house on December 17, 1997, but was instructed to continue to leave weekly urine screens at the APA office.

On February 18, 1998, the APA issued an arrest order and declared petitioner a parole violator at large due to his failure to report to his parole officer and failure to report for his weekly urine screen. The Toledo Police Department arrested petitioner again on March 18, 1998, for giving false information about his identity, possession of drug paraphernalia, and [***4] post-release control violations. The APA held a violation hearing on March 30, 1998 and, at that time, petitioner admitted to all violations and the hearing officer imposed a prison term of one hundred fifty-one days, which was one half of the original term of his imprisonment. On April 2, 1998, petitioner was returned to the prison. On August 28, 1998, he was released again on post-release control.

On October 5, 1998, the Toledo Police Department arrested petitioner for loitering and obstructing official business. On November 4, 1998, petitioner was released from custody and the following sanctions were imposed: that there be no more arrests; and that he gain employment, successfully complete substance abuse counseling, report for office visits twice per week, and successfully complete a halfway house program. Petitioner reported to the office on November 12, 1998, claiming that he had missed his appointment with the substance abuse counselor. At that time, he submitted to a urine screen that tested positive for cocaine. On January 16, 1999, petitioner was arrested for drug abuse, a charge for which he was later convicted and then sentenced to a community-based correctional facility [***5] for one hundred eighty days. In addition, he was charged with escape ( R.C. 2921.34) in relation to his failure to report to his post-release control officer. 1 On March 7, 1999, petitioner was mistakenly released from the community-based correctional facility. On March 10, 1999, he voluntarily turned himself in to his post-release control officer.


1 At the time of his hearing on the petition for a writ of habeas corpus, petitioner's felony escape charge was still pending.

On March 18, 1999, petitioner filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus in the Sixth Appellate District against the Lucas County Sheriff's Department and the Adult Parole Authority. On March 25, 1999, the last violation hearing was held and petitioner was sentenced to thirty days in the county jail and was subject to the control and supervision of the APA.

The Sixth District held a hearing on the petition on April 6, 1999, and discharged petitioner from custody pending the decision of the court. On June 23, 1999, the Sixth District held that R.C. 2967.28 is unconstitutional in that it violates both the separation of powers doctrine and the Due Process [***6] Clauses of the United States and Ohio Constitutions. Accordingly, the Sixth District granted habeas corpus relief to the petitioner and released him from the control and supervision of the Ohio Adult Parole Authority. On August 3, 1999, the court of appeals granted a motion for stay of judgment pending appeal.

The cause is now before this court upon an appeal as of right.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed of right from Court of Appeals for Lucas County, Ohio, order discharging petitioner defendant from custody on petition for habeas corpus, declaring Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2967.28, Ohio's post-release control statute, unconstitutional for violating the separation of powers doctrine and due process clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Over several years, petitioner was arrested, sentenced, served time, was placed on conditional post-release control, which included a substance abuse program and weekly urine screenings. He was released, rearrested and resentenced several times, for probation violation and other, unrelated, offenses, including failure to report and failure to pass his drug screenings. In 1999, he petitioned the appellate court for writ of habeas corpus against respondents, the sheriff's department and adult parole authority (APA), after being sentenced to 30 days in county jail. The appellate court held Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2967.28 unconstitutional for violating the separation of powers doctrine and the Due Process Clauses of the United States and Ohio Constitutions. Accordingly, it granted habeas corpus relief and released petitioner, but stayed the judgment pending appeal. The Ohio Supreme Court reversed the holding of unconstitutionality, finding no separation of powers or due process violation, but affirmed the grant of habeas corpus, because the jail/prison sanction imposed on petitioner exceeded the statutory maximums, as the county jail was the functional equivalent of prison.


OUTCOME: Judgment of unconstitutionality was reversed, as agency's discretion in managing post-release control did not impede judicial branch, violating separation of powers, and petitioner's post-release control violation hearings were conducted by neutral hearing officer and did not violate due process. But petitioner's habeas corpus grant was affirmed, as jail/prison sanction was exceeded.

Ohio Roundtable v. Taft


No. 02CVC01-491.


STATE OF OHIO, COURT OF COMMON PLEAS, FRANKLIN COUNTY


119 Ohio Misc. 2d 49; 2002-Ohio-3669; 773 N.E.2d 1113; 2002 Ohio Misc. LEXIS 20



July 15, 2002, Decided



DISPOSITION:  Decision on the merits was issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individuals challenged the legitimacy of Ohio's participation in the multi-state lottery game by asserting that the lottery was unconstitutional, that the proceeds would not go to support public education, and that H.B. 405 (Ohio) violated the Ohio Constitution's single-subject rule, among other things. Defendants, governor and others, asserted the defense of lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: The court found the individuals had standing to pursue their claims under both a private and a public action. The administrative rules originally filed by the lottery commission on February 14, 2002, were not invalid because they were filed prior to the effective date of H.B. 405. In addition, the Ohio General Assembly did not unconstitutionally delegate its authority to authorize a state agency to conduct a lottery. Further, H.B. 405 did not delegate to other states that part of the general assembly's authority that could be possessed only by the general assembly. The commission retained sufficient control to satisfy the constitutional requirement that the commission "conduct" the lottery. Also, the Ohio Constitution did not require that the multi-state consortium's entire net proceeds be deposited into the Ohio Lottery Profit Education Fund. However, the sentence in H.B. 405, § 36 (Ohio) which allowed the budget director to decrease the fiscal year appropriation was unconstitutional, as it caused lottery proceeds to be used for purposes other than to support public education. Finally, the inclusion of the multi-state lottery provisions did not violate the single-subject rule.


OUTCOME: The individuals had standing. The lottery was found to be legitimate and statutorily and constitutionally permissible.

In re James


No. 2005-1994


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


113 Ohio St. 3d 420; 2007-Ohio-2335; 866 N.E.2d 467; 2007 Ohio LEXIS 1300


September 19, 2006, Submitted  
May 30, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by In re James, 114 Ohio St. 3d 1484, 2007 Ohio 3699, 870 N.E.2d 734, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 1682 (2007)
Related proceeding at In re B.J., 2009 Ohio 6485, 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 5434 (Ohio Ct. App., Hamilton County, Dec. 11, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Hamilton County, No. C-040533, 163 Ohio App.3d 442, 2005 Ohio 4847, 839 N.E.2d 39.
In re James, 163 Ohio App. 3d 442, 2005 Ohio 4847, 839 N.E.2d 39, 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 4394 (Ohio Ct. App., Hamilton County, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The juvenile court awarded legal custody of a minor child to his maternal grandparents. Three years later, the child's natural parents filed a motion to obtain custody of their son, which was granted. The Court of Appeals for Hamilton County (Ohio) affirmed the judgment on appeal. A discretionary appeal as to the constitutionality of R.C. § 3109.04(E)(1)(a) was accepted.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents argued that the statutory "change in circumstances" requirement conformed with the Ohio Constitution because the juvenile court had adjudicated the child to be abused and dependent and also because the parents stipulated to the court order that granted the grandparents legal custody of the child. The state supreme court held that the appellate court erred in finding it proper to return the child to his parents because R.C. § 3109.04(E)(1)(a) unconstitutionally deprived the parents of their fundamental right to parent their child. R.C. § 3109.04(E)(1)(a) did not violate the fundamental rights of parents either on its face or as applied in the instant case. The juvenile court adjudicated the child as abused and dependent, and the parents voluntarily relinquished custody of him to his grandparents. In addition, the grandparents had raised the child in a stable home environment, and the parents enjoyed residual parental rights, privileges, and responsibilities as set forth in R.C. § 2151.011(B)(19) and (46). Although the record did not establish a change in the child's circumstances, that failure did not prevent the parents from ever regaining custody of him.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the cause was remanded.

663 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Icon Entm't Group, Inc.


Case No. 2009 CRB 030175, Case No. 2010 CRB 004041


STATE OF OHIO, COLUMBUS MUNICIPAL COURT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


160 Ohio Misc. 2d 9; 2010-Ohio-5719; 937 N.E.2d 1112; 2010 Ohio Misc. LEXIS 371



September 23, 2010, Decided


DISPOSITION: Motions denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant business was charged with two counts of illegally operating a sexually oriented business, in violation of R.C. 2907.40(B). Defendant filed motions to dismiss. In the first motion, it alleged that the complaints were deficient in that they did not allege that it acted with recklessness. In the second motion, defendant argued that R.C. 2907.40(B) was unconstitutionally vague on its face. The State opposed the motions.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the legislature deliberately created a strict-liability offense. The court held that R.C. 2907.40(B) stated a strict-liability offense pursuant to R.C. 2901.21(B). Further, with respect to free speech, R.C. 2907.40(B) violated neither the First Amendment to the Constitution of the United States nor Ohio Const. art. I, § 11. The statute promoted the government's substantial interest in mitigating the adverse secondary effects of adult businesses and any incidental restriction on protected speech was no greater than necessary to meet that valid and content-neutral goal. Finally, R.C. 2907.40(B) was not unconstitutionally vague on its face. The only reasonable reading of R.C. 2907.40(B) was that it would, at the very least, prohibit an adult cabaret from featuring any sexually oriented performances of which it was a purveyor after midnight. Since that conduct would fall well within what can reasonably be understood as the core meaning of R.C. 2907.40(B), then R.C. 2907.40(B) could validly be applied to prohibit that conduct. Since there was a valid application of the statute under those circumstances, it was impossible to conclude that it was vague on its face.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motions to dismiss were denied.

 

664 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carswell


No. 2006-0151


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


114 Ohio St. 3d 210; 2007-Ohio-3723; 871 N.E.2d 547; 2007 Ohio LEXIS 1654


December 12, 2006, Submitted 
July 25, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Carswell, 115 Ohio St. 3d 1414, 2007 Ohio 4884, 873 N.E.2d 1317, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2261 (Ohio, Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Warren County, No. CA2005-04-047, 2005 Ohio 6547.
State v. Carswell, 2005 Ohio 6547, 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 5903 (Ohio Ct. App., Warren County, Dec. 12, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the trial court with domestic violence, under R.C. § 2919.25, against a victim to whom he was not married. The trial court found the indictment unconstitutional, under Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11, and dismissed it, but the Court of Appeals for Warren County (Ohio) reversed. Defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held the domestic violence statute's protection for a "person living as a spouse" recognized a relationship approximating marriage, contrary to Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11. The supreme court held art. XV, § 11 did not implicitly repeal R.C. 2919.25 because the two were not clearly incompatible as Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11 barred the state's creation or recognition of a legal status for unmarried persons bearing the attributes of marriage, but R.C. 2919.25 created no special or additional rights, privileges or benefits for family or household members. Cohabitation created a status to which the statute extended protection, but the state did not create cohabitation. R.C. 2919.25's intent was to protect persons from violence by close family members or household residents, while Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11's intent was to bar the creation or recognition of a legal status approximating marriage. The two did not conflict. "Person living as a spouse" was only a class of persons for purposes of the domestic-violence statutes. It did not create or recognize a legal relationship approximating marriage. Persons in the "living as a spouse" category had no marital rights or duties.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

 

665 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Payne v. Greater Cleveland R.T.A.


NO. 83240


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2003-Ohio-6340; 2003 Ohio App. LEXIS 5669



November 26, 2003, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Civil appeal from Common Pleas Court. Case No. 445031.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bus driver suffered injuries after a third-party motorist struck the bus he was operating. The driver collected workers' compensation benefits from defendant employer. The driver brought suit against the motorist. The employer intervened to assert its right to subrogation, on authority of former Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4123.931. The parties settled. The Common Pleas Court, Ohio, granted the employer summary judgment. The driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that former Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4123.931 was unconstitutional in that parts of the statute violated the Equal Protection Clause of Ohio Const. art. 1, § 2 because it created disparate treatment of claimants who settled their claims and claimants who litigated their claims. The question raised in the appeal was what effect the supreme court's decision had on parties who settled a subrogation claim prior to the release of the decision. A subsequent change in the law could not apply retrospectively in instances in which contractual rights had arisen or a party had acquired vested rights under the prior law. The parties agreed to terminate the subrogation litigation before the supreme court released the decision. Once they settled the matter, contract rights vested with the employer. Consequently, the instant court found that the supreme court's decision could not apply retrospectively.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

666 of 997 DOCUMENTS


City of Cleveland Heights ex rel. Hicks v. City of Cleveland Heights


No. 84884


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


162 Ohio App. 3d 193; 2005-Ohio-3582; 832 N.E.2d 1275; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 3308



July 14, 2005, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY: CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil appeal from Common Pleas Court. Case No. CV-522627.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two city residents, sought review of a judgment from the Cuyahoga County Common Pleas Court (Ohio), which denied their request for a statutory injunction against appellee city, wherein the residents sought to enjoin the operation of a domestic partner registry ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The residents became aware of an initiative petition for an ordinance that would have caused the city to establish a domestic partner registry. Thereafter, the ordinance was approved by a referendum vote and the city commenced administering the registry. The city law director declined the resident's request to bring an injunction action on behalf of the city. Accordingly, the resident brought the instant action, asserting that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it abused the city's corporate powers under Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3. The other resident joined the action. Thereafter, the trial court denied their request for an injunction, based on its determination that no irreparable harm was shown, that the city was within its home rule authority, and that there was no constitutional violation. On appeal, the court found that the trial court's ruling was not erroneous. The court held that the ordinance was a matter of local self-government within art. XVIII, § 3, as the registry conferred no right or obligation upon registrants, it was administered exclusively within the city, and it had no effect outside the territory of the city. Accordingly, it was lawful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Rollins v. State


Nos. 96192, 96193, and 96194


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2011-Ohio-3264; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 2747



June 30, 2011, Released and Journalized


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case Nos. CV-646989, CV-647275, and CV-649265.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee registrants filed petitions in the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), contesting their reclassifications under Ohio's Adam Walsh Act, R.C. Chapter 2950 (2008), as Tier III sex offenders, arguing that it violated numerous constitutional rights. The trial court vacated the new classifications and reinstated those previously applied under the Ohio Megan's Law, R.C. Chapter 2950 (amended 2008). The State of Ohio appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State of Ohio contended that the registrants were not classified under Megan's Law by an Ohio court as the records in the registrants' cases contained no mention of a classification hearing or a court-ordered classification. The State, therefore, argued that reclassifying the registrants under the Adam Walsh Act was not a violation of the separation of powers doctrine as their original classifications were automatic under the law. The State also argued that the registrants did not demonstrate by clear and convincing evidence that they were previously classified by an Ohio court. On appeal, the court found that regardless of the manner in which the registrants were originally classified, R.C. 2950.031 and 2950.032 had been severed and no longer were to be enforced. Thus, the trial court did not err in vacating the new classifications which were imposed by the Attorney General of Ohio and in reinstating those classifications of the registrants which were previously applied under the Ohio Megan's Law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of N. Canton v. City of Canton


No. 2006-0293


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


114 Ohio St. 3d 253; 2007-Ohio-4005; 871 N.E.2d 586; 2007 Ohio LEXIS 1924


April 3, 2007, Submitted 
August 22, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Stark County, No. 2005-CA-00123,
City of N. Canton v. City of Canton, 2005 Ohio 6953, 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 6268 (Ohio Ct. App., Stark County, Dec. 27, 2005).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city one sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals for Stark County (Ohio), which affirmed a trial court's decision dismissing city one's suit against appellees, city two and a county board of commissioners, regarding annexation proceedings and challenging the constitutionality of R.C. 709.02(E)'s exclusion of railroads from the definition of "owner" for purposes of annexation proceedings.


OVERVIEW: City one entered into an agreement with a transit authority providing for the annexation of a portion of the authority's property to city one. Three days later, city two filed a petition with the board for annexation of some of the same land land; however, city two's petition did not contain the signature of any representative of the authority. The board passed a resolution granting city two's petition. In its action against appellees, city two challenged the constitutionality of § 709.02(E), which did not require the authority's signature on city two's annexation petition. The court held that city one lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 709.02(E) on the basis that the effect of the statute on the authority destroyed city one's contract rights in the authority's property. City one was not a member of the class of owners identified or allegedly being discriminated against by the statute, and no exception to this rule applied. City one lacked a sufficiently close relationship with the authority to assert the constitutional challenge for the authority. Further, city one did not demonstrate that the authority was hindered from asserting its own rights in the matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals.

State v. Cowan


No. 2003-1406


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


103 Ohio St. 3d 144; 2004-Ohio-4777; 814 N.E.2d 846; 2004 Ohio LEXIS 2132


March 30, 2004, Submitted  
September 22, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Portage County, Nos. 2002-P-0029, 2002-P-0030, and 2002-P-0031, 2003-Ohio-3547.
State v. Cowan, 2003 Ohio 3547, 2003 Ohio App. LEXIS 3252 (Ohio Ct. App., Portage County, July 3, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the court of appeals affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals for Portage County (Ohio), which reversed the convictions imposed on defendant by the trial court, based on the appellate court's determination that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 955.22 unconstitutionally deprived defendant of her due process rights. Defendant had been convicted of various offenses arising from incidents involving her dog.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's neighbor informed a dog warden that defendant's dogs had attacked his wife. The warden made the determination that defendant's dogs were vicious. The warden informed defendant of her responsibilities as to confining the dogs under the vicious-dog law. On two subsequent occasions, the warden was summoned to defendant's residence due to complaints that her dogs were not confined pursuant to the vicious-dog law. Charges were filed against her under various sections of § 955.22. Her motions to dismiss, based on challenges to the statute's constitutionality, were denied, and she was convicted and sentenced. On appeal, the appellate court reversed the convictions, finding that § 955.22 violated defendant's due process rights by allowing the warden unfettered discretion to label the dogs as dangerous and/or vicious, and because there was no appeal mechanism. On further review, the court found that the inability of defendant to have contradicted the warden's opinion prior to his determination having been made violated her due process rights. Further, even at her criminal trial, the jury did not consider whether the dog met the definition of "vicious" or "dangerous."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

Gahanna v. Petraziello


No. 00AP-1480, No. 00AP-1481


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 4570



October 11, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by City of Gahanna v. Petruziello, 2004 Ohio 2133, 2004 Ohio App. LEXIS 1830 (Ohio Ct. App., Franklin County, Apr. 27, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALS from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city appealed judgments of the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) granting appellee developer's motion to dismiss the city's appeal for lack of standing, in the court's review of a decision by a zoning appeals board.


OVERVIEW: After the developer's application for approval of a development plan was denied by the planning commission, the board overturned the decision and granted the application. Soon thereafter, the city passed an ordinance allowing it to seek review of the board's determinations. The city and the objectors appealed the determination. The trial court dismissed the city's appeal for lack of standing and proceeded to hear the matter on the merits. The appellate court held that the ordinance was unequivocally intended to operate retrospectively. It did not create new obligations with respect to the developer's substantive rights. The developer knew of the city's position since the city had participated in the underlying hearings. Because standing was jurisdictional, the trial court's dismissal of the city's appeal precluded a ruling on the merits as to the city's action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the cause was remanded to the trial court for a determination on the merits of the city's appeal.

 

674 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Hanners v. Ho Wah Genting Wire & Cable SDN BHD


No. 09AP-361


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2009-Ohio-6481; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 5432



December 10, 2009, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 08CVG10-15218).



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee estate administrators filed a wrongful death action against, among others, appellants, the manufacturers of an electrical extension cord that was alleged to have started the fire that killed the decedents, seeking compensatory and punitive damages. The manufacturers moved to bifurcate the punitive damages proceedings under R.C. 2315.21(B), which the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denied. The manufacturers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturers argued that the trial court erred by declaring R.C. 2315.21(B) to be unconstitutional. The appellate court held that, first, because the trial court determined the constitutionality of R.C. 2315.21(B), there was jurisdiction to review the trial court's determination as a final order under R.C. 2505.02(B). However, the trial court erred by denying the manufacturers' motion to bifurcate the punitive damages proceedings pursuant to R.C. 2315.21(B) because it was a substantive law. While it mandated a particular procedure for tort actions, that mandate was for the purpose of creating and defining a defendant's right to request bifurcation to ensure that the jury did not inappropriately consider the defendant's misconduct when also determining questions of liability and compensatory damages. Although R.C. 2315.21(B) was necessarily packaged in procedural wrapping, based on the Ohio General Assembly's express intent to create a right of bifurcation to address potential unfairness, the law was substantive. Thus, R.C. 2315.21(B) did not conflict with Civ. R. 42(B) in such a way as to violate the separation of powers required by Ohio Const. art. IV, § 5(B).


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of the manufacturers' motion to bifurcate the punitive damages proceedings pursuant to R.C. 2315.21(B) was reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Sears v. State


CASE NO. CA2008-07-068


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CLERMONT COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3541; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3051



July 20, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Review pending at Sears v. State, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1507, 2009 Ohio 6210, 917 N.E.2d 810, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3383 (2009)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 126 Ohio St. 3d 322, 2010 Ohio 3753, 933 N.E.2d 801, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CLERMONT COUNTY COURT OF COMMON PLEAS. Case No. 2008 CVH 00212.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sex offender contested his reclassification as a tier II sex offender pursuant to R.C. Chapter 2950, as amended by Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) (S.B. 10), in the Clermont County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) and sought a declaratory judgment that his reclassification was unconstitutional. The trial court overruled his petition and found S.B. 10 constitutional. The offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: The offender said S.B. 10 violated the ex post facto, due process, and double jeopardy clauses of the United States Constitution, the retroactivity clause of the Ohio Constitution, and the bar against cruel and unusual punishment. The appellate court found it previously held S.B. 10 did not violate these protections. S.B. 10 did not violate the separation of powers requirement of the United States Constitution because (1) classifying sex offenders was a legislative mandate, not an inherent judicial power, and (2) the legislature did not abrogate final judicial decisions without amending the underlying applicable law, but, instead, enacted a new law changing the different sexual offender classifications and time spans for registration requirements, among other things, and requiring that the new procedures be applied to offenders currently registering under the old law or currently incarcerated for committing a sexually oriented offense. The reclassification and related requirements of S.B. 10 did not violate the offender's right to contract under the United States and Ohio Constitutions because it did not interfere with a vested contractual right.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Cord


C.A. NO. 20057


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 5453



November 22, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE MUNICIPAL COURT OF AKRON. COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE NO. 99 TRD 17758.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Akron Municipal Court, Summit County, Ohio, finding him guilty of violating Akron, Ohio, City Code § 72.24(B) for failing to make a proper right-hand turn.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted after he struck a vehicle traveling in the right lane while attempting to turn right into his driveway from the left lane. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court's decision was not against the manifest weight of the evidence because it was supported by the testimony of an investigating officer, who testified that the other vehicle's skid marks and damage showed that the collision occurred just before appellant's driveway, and that appellant's vehicle was turning and caused the other vehicle to go off the road. The trial court did not err by refusing to grant appellant's motion to dismiss because there was sufficient evidence showing appellant did not make the right-hand turn as close as practicable to the right-hand curb. The court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague because it gave appellant sufficient notice that his conduct was outside the acceptable range.


OUTCOME: Judgment modified to reflect that appellant was found guilty of an improper right turn. As modified, judgment affirmed because the trial court's judgment was supported by the investigating officer's testimony, appellant's motion to dismiss was properly denied, and the city ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague.

Brown v. Columbus City Schs. Bd. of Educ.


No. 08AP-1067


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3230; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2765



June 30, 2009, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Brown v. Columbus City Schs. Bd. of Educ., 2009 Ohio 6015, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3293 (Ohio, Nov. 18, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 07CVH09-12492).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, taxpayers and school district residents, sued appellees, a board of education, and the Ohio superintendent of public instruction, department of education, and board of education, in the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, claiming the state's school funding system was unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the complaint for lack of standing, and appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellants said it was error to find they lacked standing. The appellate court disagreed because they had no private standing, as they had no direct personal stake in the case's outcome, since they had not suffered and were not threatened with direct and concrete injury in a manner or degree different from the general public, as they alleged only that they were taxpayers and did not allege they were students or parents of students. They only contributed to the school district's funding as other citizens in the district, as opposed to contributing to a special fund, so their pecuniary interests were not affected differently than the general public. The case did not fall under the public-right exception to the personal stake requirement for standing because there was no similar case in which a taxpayer was allowed to bring a declaratory action challenging a school district's method of funding allocation. Also, the case (1) was not an original action seeking an extraordinary writ, (2) did not demand early resolution, and (3) was not of a rare and extraordinary nature.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

679 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Genesis Outdoor, Inc. v. Pol. Twp. Bd. of Zoning Appeals


CASE NO. 12 MA 11


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MAHONING COUNTY


2013-Ohio-1425; 2013 Ohio App. LEXIS 1325



March 26, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from Common Pleas Court, Case No. 08 CV 1836.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff billboard company filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendants, a township zoning director and the township board of zoning appeals, challenging the validity of a township zoning resolution concerning billboards. The Mahoning County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) overruled objections to a magistrate's decision and granted judgment in favor of defendants. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The zoning resolution mandated a 130-foot setback for billboards and also provided mounting and size restrictions. Plaintiff argued that the resolution conflicted with R.C. 519.20 and violated U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV. The court stated that it was the complete prohibition of billboards that conflicted with R.C. 519.20. The resolution did not ban billboard advertising, either by operation of law or in practice. Plaintiff conceded that it would be possible to erect billboards on several of the subject properties, although this might require some interference with existing structures on those properties. Thus, the resolution did not conflict with R.C. 519.20. Next, plaintiff had not waived its First Amendment claim. Although its complaint did not cite the First Amendment, it did cite the Fourteenth Amendment, and the substance of the assertions put defendants on notice of the First Amendment claim. The zoning resolution, however, did not control the communicative aspects of the billboards, but merely set reasonable set-back requirements for structures as permitted by law. It was not a content-based restriction on speech and did not implicate First Amendment concerns.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

No. 99AP-364


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 95

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas, Division of Domestic Relations, Juvenile Branch.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile appealed judgment of Franklin County Court of Common Pleas, Division of Domestic Relations (Ohio), which overruled defendant's objections to magistrate's decision overruling appellant's motion to declare Ohio Rev. The court rejected appellant's contention that § 2903.13 was unconstitutional because it provided an enhanced penalty where victim was police or probation officer. Trial court did not err in finding there was sufficient evidence to support magistrate's decision, and magistrate's findings were not against manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; appellant's contentions that denial of her motion for jury trial violated due process rights and was violative of equal protection were without merit, as the state was justified in treating juveniles differently than adults because of its interests in preserving and promoting the child's welfare.

Belich v. City of Olmsted Falls


Nos. 84537 and 84807


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2005-Ohio-190; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 212



January 20, 2005, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil appeal from Common Pleas Court. Case No. CV-496216.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought judicial review in the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) of the decisions of appellees, a city, its city council and a planning commission, which found the landowner's use of its property was not a permitted use and denied its application for a conditional use permit. The trial court upheld the decisions reviewed and enjoined the landowner's operations without a valid permit. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner ran a concrete recycling business. The appellate court held the owner did not show that the use was ever a lawful one, so it was not a nonconforming use. The applicable zoning ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague as it notified the owner of land use restrictions, and the lack of definitions of prohibited "scrap yards" and "waste material processors" did not make the ordinance vague. Given noise and dust complaints about the property, the owner did not show the ordinance was unconstitutional as applied to the property, as it did not show the ordinance was clearly arbitrary without substantial relation to the public health. The owner's property use was included in the ordinance. The zoning administrator's authority to find proscribed uses did not overcome the ordinance's presumed validity. Estoppel could not prevent the city from enforcing its zoning ordinances. Neither the planning commission nor the city council made a required inquiry into whether the owner met the criteria for a conditional use permit. The trial court's injunction was proper insofar as the owner was operating without a conditional use permit.


OUTCOME: Insofar as the owner was currently operating without a conditional use permit, the trial court's injunction was affirmed, but the trial court's judgment affirming the owner's administrative appeal was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court with directions to remand it to the planning commission to review the owner's application for a conditional use permit.

Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Melhado v. Warden, Marion Corr. Inst., 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 60043 (S.D. Ohio, Apr. 30, 2014)

683 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Fabian v. City of Steubenville


CASE NO. 00 JE 33


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, JEFFERSON COUNTY


2001-Ohio-3522; 2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 4533



September 28, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from Jefferson County Common Pleas Court, Case No. 99 CV 163.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs city employee, and his wife, filed a suit for intentional tort, claiming that defendants city and assistant plant supervisor knew the injury to the employee would occur and that the assistant supervisor's acted outside the scope of his employment or in a reckless or wanton manner. The Jefferson County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) granted summary judgment for defendants and dismissed the case. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: After a chlorine gas leak, the employee rushed into the affected room thinking that his supervisor was in danger. He was hospitalized for his injuries. The appellate court held that the trial court properly granted summary judgment. First, the city was immune from suit under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. ch. 2744, the Political Subdivision Tort Liability Act, as intentional torts could not arise out of the employment relationship. Second, ch. 2744 did not violate equal protection. Plaintiffs did not have a fundamental right to sue the city and the class protected by ch. 2744 was political subdivisions. Further, it did not impermissibly draw a distinction between sovereign and private tortfeasors. Finally, even if the assistant supervisor did act wantonly and recklessly, the employee would not be able to recover from the city because the city would still be immune from suit under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744.02(A) and the assistant supervisor would be immune under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4123.741.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Rivera


C.A. Nos. 08CA009426, 08CA009427


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LORAIN COUNTY


2009-Ohio-1428; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 1245



March 30, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Subsequent appeal at State v. McCloud, 2012 Ohio 5220, 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 4564 (Ohio Ct. App., Lorain County, Nov. 13, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS COUNTY OF LORAIN, OHIO. CASE Nos. 04CR065940, 05CR068067.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Ohio's motion for leave to appeal an order from the Lorain County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which held that execution by lethal injection under R.C. 2949.22 was unconstitutional, was granted. The two defendants in the underlying criminal matters sought dismissal due to lack of a final appealable order under R.C. 2505.02 and Ohio Const. art. IV, § 3(B)(2), and alternatively, they filed cross-appeals.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants were separately indicted for multiple offenses, including aggravated murder with a death specification. They sought to have the specification dismissed from their indictments based on the alleged unconstitutionality of the method of lethal injection used. After multiple hearings, the trial court held that use of a combination of drugs for a lethal injection under § 2949.22 was unconstitutional. Statutory language reflecting that procedure was severed and a new protocol was ordered implemented. The State appealed, and defendants sought dismissal due to lack of a final appealable order and they also filed a cross-appeal. The court held that no final appealable order existed under art. IV, § 3(B)(2) and § 2505.02. The trial court order was not a declaratory judgment under R.C. 2721.02(A), as there was no actual controversy. Further, the order did not grant a provisional remedy for purposes of § 2505.02(B)(4). as the trial court's proceeding was not ancillary to the underlying criminal case. Lastly, the criminal matter was not a special proceeding for purposes of § 2505.02(B)(2), and § 2949.22 did not create an "action" for a quick and painless death.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

State ex rel. HGC Enters. v. Buehrer


No. 12AP-482


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2013-Ohio-2108; 2013 Ohio App. LEXIS 2009



May 23, 2013, Rendered


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Objections overruled; writ of mandamus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator applicant filed an action requesting the issuance of a writ of mandamus ordering respondent, the Ohio Bureau of Workers' Compensation (BWC), to vacate its order which denied the applicant's request for the issuance of a new policy number and to issue the applicant its own policy number. A magistrate recommended that the writ was to be denied. The applicant objected.


OVERVIEW: The applicant began operating a pizza restaurant franchise at a site where another business had previously operated a pizza restaurant franchise with the same franchiser. The principal of the previous franchisee was the son of the applicant's principal. After receiving the applicant's application for coverage, the BWC applied Ohio Admin. Code 4123-17-13(C) and determined that the applicant was essentially the same employer as the prior business and, instead of granting the application for coverage, the BWC concluded that the applicant already had coverage in the form of the policy already issued to the prior business. The applicant argued that the BWC, pursuant to R.C. 4123.32(C), should have applied Ohio Admin. Code 4123-17-02 and determined whether the applicant was a successor employer to the prior business. The reviewing court found that the BWC did not abuse its discretion in applying Ohio Admin. Code 4123-17-13(C) and finding that the applicant was essentially the same employer as the prior business. Moreover, Ohio Admin. Code 4123-17-13(C) was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The objections were overruled, and the writ of mandamus was denied.

Young v. Rogers


CASE NO. CA2001-08-183


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, BUTLER COUNTY


2002-Ohio-5135; 2002 Ohio App. LEXIS 5195



September 30, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM COMMON PLEAS COURT, JUVENILE DIVISION.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed a decision of the Butler County Juvenile Court (Ohio) finding that it did not have jurisdiction to modify a child support order issued in Oklahoma. The Butler County Child Support Enforcement Agency registered a child support order in Butler County Juvenile Court on behalf of appellee mother and the State of Oklahoma.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile court lacked jurisdiction to modify the Oklahoma support order. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3115.48(A)(1) was inapplicable, as the child and the obligee lived in Oklahoma. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3115.48(A)(2) was inapplicable because all parties had not given written consent authorizing an Ohio court to modify the order. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3115.50 was inapplicable because all of the parties who were individuals did not reside in Ohio, and the child lived Oklahoma. Under Ohio law, the juvenile court did not have jurisdiction to modify the order. The federal Full Faith and Credit for Child Support Orders Act dictated the same result, and the case did not fall within any pertinent exceptions. According to state and federal law, Oklahoma, the state that issued the order, was the only state with jurisdiction to modify the order. There was no legal authority to show that the father's equal protection and due process rights were violated. He failed to meet his burden of proving that the relevant state and federal statutes were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

State ex rel. O'Brien v. Heimlich

COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2009-Ohio-1550; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 1266



March 31, 2009, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by State ex rel. O'Brien v. Heimlich, 121 Ohio St. 3d 1478, 2009 Ohio 2111, 905 N.E.2d 656, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 1193 (2009)
Discretionary appeal not allowed by State ex rel. O'Brien v. Heimlich, 2009 Ohio 4233, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2341 (Ohio, Aug. 26, 2009)

APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 07CVH03-4443).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sexually oriented offender (SOO) sought review of a judgment from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which granted summary judgment to appellee prosecuting attorney (PA) in his action, seeking to enjoin the inmate from residing within 1,000 feet of a school premises pursuant to the residency restrictions for certain SOOs pursuant to R.C. 2950.031.

Pursuant to the PA's authority under § 2950.031, he sought an injunction to prevent the SOO from residing at a particular address. The PA provided the SOO's conviction and an affidavit from a county auditor that the residence was approximately 625 feet from an elementary school. The trial court granted the PA's motion, finding that the evidence supported it and that § 2950.031 withstood constitutional challenge. The SOO was not precluded from owning, renting, or leasing property, and there was no fundamental right for the SOO to live where he wished. The residency restriction was rationally related to a legitimate governmental interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Hayden


CASE NO. 99-L-037


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 3198



July 14, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 98 CR 000428.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his murder conviction in Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), claiming felony-murder statute, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2903.02(B), was unconstitutional and conviction was not supported by the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of felony murder and sought review of his conviction. The court affirmed. The felony-murder statute, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2903.02(B), was not unconstitutional. A clear nexus existed between the felony and the homicide. Appellant repeatedly and knowingly stomped on the victim's head, which eventually lead to death. State satisfied the mens rea for murder by proving the intent of the underlying felony, felonious assault. Sufficient evidence existed to support the conviction and it was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. Appellant and his friends began punching and kicking an unknown man, the victim, whom they thought was carrying a weapon and may have been responsible for attacking appellant's cousin. Appellant admitted to kicking victim, even after realizing victim was unarmed. Two witnesses observed appellant stomping and kicking victim's head and upper body.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed because a sufficient nexus existed between the felonious assault and murder and sufficient evidence supported the conviction where appellant was shown to have repeatedly and knowingly stomped and kicked the victim's head, causing eventual death.

State v. Grimes


Case No. 06CA17


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, WASHINGTON COUNTY


2006-Ohio-6360; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 6312



November 24, 2006, Date Journalized


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Grimes, 113 Ohio St. 3d 1444, 2007 Ohio 1266, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 735 (Ohio, Mar. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL APPEAL FROM COMMON PLEAS COURT.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Washington County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which convicted him of burglary, in violation of R.C. § 2911.12(A)(3), and imposed a maximum term of imprisonment on him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on three charges. He entered into an agreement with the prosecution, whereby defendant entered a guilty plea to a reduced charge of burglary in exchange for the dismissal of the remaining charges. The trial court conducted a colloquy regarding the plea and then accepted it and found defendant guilty. He was sentenced to a maximum term of imprisonment. On appeal, the court noted that as Foster was decided prior to defendant's sentencing hearing, his failure to raise that issue before the trial court could be construed as a waiver for purposes of appeal. However, even assuming that it was properly reviewable, defendant's claim that the sentence imposed violated the ex post facto clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and the due process clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV lacked merit. The range of prison terms before and after Foster for a third degree felony were the same. Accordingly, defendant's claim that an enlargement occurred with respect to R.C. § 2929.14 or punishments generally lacked merit. There was no showing that defendant would have acted differently if he had known that parts of § 2929.14 would have been severed as unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. McKinley


CASE NO. 8-05-14


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT, LOGAN COUNTY


2006-Ohio-2507; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 2379



May 22, 2006, Date of Judgment Entry


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted by, Stay granted by State v. McKinley, 110 Ohio St. 3d 1462, 2006 Ohio 4288, 852 N.E.2d 1212, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 2526 (2006)
Reversed by In re Ohio Domestic-Violence Statute Cases, 114 Ohio St. 3d 430, 2007 Ohio 4552, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2199 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Common Pleas Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest in the Logan County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) to domestic violence, in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2919.25, after his motion to dismiss, claiming the statute was unconstitutional, under Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11, was denied. He appealed the denial of his motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant assaulted his live-in girlfriend. The appellate court held he could claim the denial of his motion to dismiss was prejudicial error, under Ohio R. Crim. P. 12(I), despite his no contest plea, and the court's jurisdiction was not defeated by his failure to serve the Ohio Attorney General, as he sought no declaratory relief. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2919.25, as applied, violated the Defense of Marriage Amendment, Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11, because the statute recognized a legal status for cohabitants. Cohabitation, as applied to one man and one woman, who did not parent a child together, was intended to approximate the design, qualities, significance or effect of marriage. Section 2919.25 created no legal status for cohabitants, contrary to Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11, because the statute only created a class of victims based on their relationship with the offender, but, because it included cohabitants within its definition of "family or household member," thereby extending the statute's protection to cohabitants, it recognized the legal status of cohabitation, so it was unconstitutional as applied to heterosexual couples who had not mutually parented children.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded with directions to dismiss the indictment. A question regarding whether Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11 rendered Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2919.25 unconstitutional as applied to unmarried, heterosexual cohabitants without mutual children was certified.

 

694 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gooding


Case No. 08 CA 5


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, COSHOCTON COUNTY


2008-Ohio-5954; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 5000



November 14, 2008, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 07 CR 0131.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to three counts of sexual battery, in violation of R.C. 2907.03(A)(5), third-degree felonies. The Coshocton County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) sentenced him to two years in prison and classified him as a Tier III sex offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio) violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws and the prohibition against retroactive laws. The appellate court held that Cook was applicable to the new version of R.C. Chapter 2950 and the new classification scheme, registration, and notification requirements contained therein did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause of the United States Constitution or the prohibition against retroactive laws contained in Ohio Const. art. II, § 28. The registration and notification provisions of R.C. Chapter 2950 did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause because its provisions served the remedial purpose of protecting the public. Also, because the sex offender registration statutes were remedial in nature, they did not violate the ban on retroactive laws as set forth in Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 since no vested right had been created.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
