State v. Hudson


CASE NO. 9-12-38


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT, MARION COUNTY


2013-Ohio-647; 986 N.E.2d 1128; 2013 Ohio App. LEXIS 581



February 25, 2013, Date of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Marion County Common Pleas Court. Trial Court No. 11-CR-0647.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded no contest in the Marion County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) to a bill of information charging him with one count of failure to provide notice of change of address in violation of R.C. 2950.05(A). The trial court found defendant guilty and sentenced him to a term of community control. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sexual offender classification stemmed from his 1996 conviction for gross sexual imposition. He argued that his ten-year registration period under the Ohio Megan's Law commenced on his release from prison and, therefore, had terminated. He further argued that R.C. 2950.07(D) (1999), which tolled the registration period for any time during which he was re-incarcerated and was effective subsequent to his conviction, did not apply retroactively; and, if it did, violated Ohio Const. art. II, § 28, the prohibition against ex post facto laws. He finally argued that R.C. 2950.07(D) violated his right to procedural due process. On appeal, the court found that, because R.C. 2950.07(D) was remedial in nature, it did not violate Ohio Const. art. II, § 28, and it was properly applied to defendant. In addition, because defendant was not entitled to a further hearing to challenge his initial duty to register as a sexual offender, he was not entitled to a further hearing to challenge his continued obligation to register pursuant to R.C. 2950.07(D) as that continued duty also attached as a matter of law and stemmed from his original conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Broadview Heights v. Stovall


No. 93322


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2010-Ohio-3867; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 3268



August 19, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Broadview Heights v. Stovall, 127 Ohio St. 3d 1504, 2011 Ohio 19, 939 N.E.2d 1267, 2011 Ohio LEXIS 111 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Criminal Appeal from the Parma Municipal Court. Case No. 2009 TRD 00599.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Parma Municipal Court, Ohio, which convicted her of resisting an enforcing official, in violation of Broadview Heights, Ohio, Ordinances § 404.02.


OVERVIEW: After being stopped for speeding, defendant exited her vehicle many times after being asked to return to the vehicle. She was convicted, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court held that the conviction was supported by sufficient evidence. The evidence showed that defendant was instructed to get into her vehicle, she repeatedly exited the vehicle, and she violated the orders of the officer in doing so. Defendant did not raise an argument in the trial court that Broadview Heights, Ohio, Ordinances § 404.02 was facially overbroad. There was no plain error because other similar challenges had been rejected. Also, § 404.02 generally tracked the language of R.C. 4513.36. As to whether Broadview Heights, Ohio, Ordinances § 404.02 was overbroad as applied, it was noted that the officer could have required defendant to remain in her vehicle while obtaining information. The proper focus in this type of prosecution was on defendant's conduct and its effect on the officer's ability to perform his lawful duties.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Dohm


CASE NO. 2009-L-076


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2010-Ohio-6567; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 5418



December 30, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On reconsideration by State v. Dohm, 2011 Ohio 1160, 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 1001 (Ohio Ct. App., Lake County, Mar. 11, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 CR 000605.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) convicted defendant of two counts of trafficking in cocaine, in violation of R.C. 2925.04(A)(1). He was sentenced to three years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in permitting the State to keep the confidential informant's (CI) identity confidential in a public trial where the informant's name was already known to the defendant. The appellate court held that the State did have a valid, reasonable foundation for keeping the CI's name confidential. By keeping his identity off the record, the police could still use him as a confidential informant for controlled drug buys in the future. Further, defense counsel agreed that concealing his identity was not a problem, so long as the CI did not deny his past criminal history. Thus, because no additional reservations were expressed by defense counsel regarding the concealment of the informant's identity, any error issuing from the concealment was invited. However, the trial court erred in failing to adhere to the statutory mandates set forth in recently amended R.C. 2929.14(E)(4) and R.C. 2929.19(B)(2)(c). The trial court neither made the necessary findings for imposing consecutive sentences as required by R.C. 2929.14(E)(4) nor stated its reasons to support those findings as required by R.C. 2929.19(B)(2)(c).


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. However, the sentence was reversed and the case was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Harding


C.A. CASE NO. 20801


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2006-Ohio-481; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 411



February 3, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Harding, 109 Ohio St. 3d 1497, 2006 Ohio 2762, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 1796 (Ohio, June 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] (Criminal Appeal from Common Pleas Court). T.C. NO. 03 CR 4646.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which convicted him of aggravated vehicular assault (AVA), in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2903.08(A)(1)(a). The trial court imposed a mandatory term of imprisonment, suspended defendant's driver's license for a period of time, and imposed a fine.


OVERVIEW: After drinking in a bar, defendant drove through a stop sign and collided with another vehicle. Field sobriety tests were administered and defendant was arrested and given a breathalyzer test. On appeal from his conviction, the court found that although the breathalyzer results were admitted without expert testimony, such error was harmless due to defendant's admission that he was drinking and other evidence of his intoxication. Testimony from the victim as to her injuries was harmless error under Ohio R. Evid. 401 and 403(A), as there was significant other evidence of defendant's guilt. Exclusion of defendant's expert's testimony as to the reliability of the breath test generally under § 4511.19(D) was not error, as testimony challenging defendant's specific test results was allowed. Constitutional challenges to the testing scheme were not preserved, although there was no plain error. As Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2903.08(A) was a strict liability statute, no recklessness instruction was required and sentencing instructions were proper. The mandatory sentence did not violate equal protection or constitute cruel and unusual punishment, and the conviction was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

699 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Osting v. City of Sidney


CASE NUMBER 17-2000-21


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT, SHELBY COUNTY


2001-Ohio-2175; 2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 1254



March 20, 2001, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from Common Pleas Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, city taxpayers, prayed for declaratory and injunctive relief under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 733.56, 2721.03 to have a city zoning ordinance invalidated. Defendants included the city. The Court of Common Pleas of Shelby County (Ohio) granted summary judgment for defendants. Plaintiffs appealed. The issue was whether or not the actions taken by the city council were procedurally proper according to the controlling city ordinances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city rezoned lots from I-2, heavy industrial zone, to B-2, community business zone, pursuant to a planning commission recommendation to allow for a large retail store to be built. Two weeks after defendant city passed that ordinance (A-2203), plaintiffs filed a referendum petition with defendant. Defendant city's council, in an effort to bypass the referendum, adopted an emergency ordinance (A-2207) that instantly repealed the rezoning ordinance, and a few minutes later unanimously adopted an emergency ordinance (A-2208), that instantly rezoned the lots in exactly the same manner as the original ordinance had previously done, thus effectively blocking the previously filed referendum and preventing the filing of any future referendum. The process followed by defendant city in enacting A-2208 failed to follow the unambiguous language provided by the city's code of ordinances, to hold a hearing upon proper notice, and thus, was not proper. Plaintiffs established that defendant city clearly abused its corporate powers when it enacted A-2208. The appeals court declared A-2208 to be invalid and A-2207 valid as merely a revocation of A-2203.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and invalidated an ordinance.

 

700 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Eckhart


Case No. 10-CA-15


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LICKING COUNTY


2010-Ohio-4842; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 4093



September 30, 2010, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Licking County Court of Common Pleas Case No. 09-CR-383.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Licking County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which convicted him of pandering obscenity involving a minor and pandering sexually oriented matter involving a minor and sentenced him to twenty-four months in prison. Defendant contended, in part, that his sentence was contrary to law and that it was not supported by the record.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred when sentencing him because it did not make any of the findings in R.C. 2929.14 and did not give the reasons in support of that finding. However, § 2929.14 was found unconstitutional in Foster and severed from the statutory scheme; thus, it was not error to not include findings under § 2929.14. Further, the U.S. Supreme Court's pronouncement in Oregon v. Ice did not change the outcome of the case. Since defendant failed to raise his argument in the trial court, he waived all but plain error. He could not show plain error under Civ. R. 52 as the court's prior precedent held that Ice did not resurrect § 2929.14(E)(4) nor did the Ohio General Assembly's amendment of § 2929.14 in 2009. Finally, the trial court did not err in failing to permit defendant to enter into a diversion program under R.C. 2935.36 as defendant was only entitled to be considered for participation in the program. The record revealed that he was considered and then rejected by the prosecuting attorney for legitimate reasons.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

701 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Brinkman v. Miami Univ.


CASE NO. CV 2005-11-3736


STATE OF OHIO, COURT OF COMMON PLEAS, BUTLER COUNTY


139 Ohio Misc. 2d 114; 2005-Ohio-7161; 861 N.E.2d 925; 2005 Ohio Misc. LEXIS 608



November 22, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Brinkman v. Miami Univ., 2007 Ohio 4372, 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 3910 (Ohio Ct. App., Butler County, Aug. 27, 2007)



DISPOSITION:  Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a state university and various of its policy makers, filed a motion for summary judgment in an action by plaintiff taxpayer/citizen, alleging that the university's provision of medical-insurance benefits to those it classified as same-sex domestic partners of its employees violated the Ohio Constitution. The taxpayer sought a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer/citizen brought his action, claiming that Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11 was violated by the university's policy regarding provision of its medical insurance benefits to same-sex domestic partners of its employees. The university based its summary judgment motion on its claim that the taxpayer lacked standing to assert the claim. The court found that the taxpayer lacked the requisite, adverse legal interest in the dispute to maintain standing. As a taxpayer, he failed to show standing because he was not a member of a special class that had funded the particular expenditures, and he was not damaged individually and concretely. As a citizen, he failed to show that he had public-rights standing, as that was only available to those who sought extraordinary writs. The taxpayer's request for declaratory and injunctive relief was not within the type of writ subject to public-rights standing. The issue of whether tax money was used to make the payments at issue was not relevant, as no standing was found in order to reach the merits of the claim.


OUTCOME: The court granted the university's motion for summary judgment.

 

702 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Schaller v. Rogers


No. 08AP-591


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2008-Ohio-4464; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 3774



September 4, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Schaller v. Cordray, 2009 Ohio 361, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 298 (Ohio, Feb. 4, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 08CVH07-09639).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant new law repeal petitioners (NLPs) sought review of a judgment from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which denied their request for a temporary restraining order and a preliminary injunction (PI) to prohibit appellees, the Ohio Attorney General and the Ohio Secretary of State, from enforcing R.C. 3519.01(B) and 3519.05. The matter arose in an action by the NLPs, seeking repeal of Sub. H.B. 545, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2008).


OVERVIEW: After passage of H.B. 545, the NLPs filed three petitions proposing to repeal H.B. 545. Thereafter, the NLPs filed their action, seeking a declaration that §§ 3519.01(B) and 3519.05 were unconstitutional and invalid, as well as injunctive relief. It was noted that appellees had certified the accuracy of the last petition. The trial court denied the request for temporary relief due to a lack of showing by the NLPs of a likelihood of success on the merits. On appeal, the court initially noted that § 3519.01(C) was inapplicable, as a challenge had been raised to the statutory process rather than a certification decision. The court found that the General Assembly had changed and developed the process faced by those who sought to repeal a state law by referendum. Ohio Const. art. II, § 1g did not preclude additional requirements to the process as long as they facilitated, and did not limit or restrict, the reserved powers of referendum or initiative. Further, the time requirements in § 3519.01 did not completely impede passage of a law under Ohio Const. art. II, § 1c. Accordingly, the necessary showing of a likelihood of success on the merits for purposes of a PI was not made.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Daniels


CASE NUMBER 12-06-15


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT, PUTNAM COUNTY


2007-Ohio-2281; 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 2118



May 14, 2007, Date of Judgment Entry


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Daniels, 115 Ohio St. 3d 1441, 2007 Ohio 5567, 875 N.E.2d 102, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2641 (Oct. 24, 2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Daniels v. Anderson, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 121502 (N.D. Ohio, Nov. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Common Pleas Court.
In re Ohio Crim. Sentencing Statutes Cases, 109 Ohio St. 3d 313, 2006 Ohio 2109, 847 N.E.2d 1174, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 1161 (May 3, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the sentence imposed by the Putnam County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio). Defendant had pleaded guilty to one count of endangering children under R.C. § 2919.22(B)(1) and (E)(2)(d) and to one count of involuntary manslaughter under R.C. § 2903.04(A). Defendant had been sentenced to eight years and ten years respectively, with the sentences to be served consecutively.


OVERVIEW: The case arose from the death of defendant's son due to shaken-impact syndrome. Although the child endangering conviction had been initially reversed as the bill of information failed to state an essential element of the crime, defendant subsequently pleaded guilty to the same count in an amended bill of information. After the sentence was affirmed on an initial appeal, the state supreme court remanded for resentencing pursuant to Foster. The trial court imposed the same sentence, and defendant filed the instant appeal, arguing that the sentence was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, finding that the Foster holding did not violate the due process clause. The court noted that defendant was on notice of the potential penalties for his unlawful conduct as the statutory range of sentences for the felonies to which he pleaded guilty had remained unchanged. Because R.C. § 1.50 allowed for the severance remedy applied in Foster, the court held that the separation of powers principle had not been violated. As the retroactive application of Foster to cases on direct review was mandated by the state supreme court, the trial court properly resentenced defendant in accordance with Foster.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence.

Haddad v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


Case No. 1999CA00262


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, STARK COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 759



February 28, 2000, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Civil Appeal from Stark County Court of Common Pleas, Case 1997CV02429.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After an automobile accident wherein appellant husband was seriously injured, appellants' damages exceeded the driver's liability insurance amount, resulting in their lawsuit against appellee insurance company; appellants challenged the judgment of the Stark County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), granting summary judgment in favor of appellee.


OVERVIEW: A car went out of control and crashed head-on into appellant husband. The vehicle that hit appellants was insured by appellee insurance company, providing underinsured motorist coverage. Appellants were also insured by appellee, with the same policy limits. Appellants sued the other driver and collected her per person limit of liability coverage. Because damages exceeded that amount, appellants sued appellee insurance company, averring that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3937.18 was unconstitutional. Both sides moved for summary judgment; appellee's motion was granted and appellants challenged the ruling. The judgment was affirmed; the court found the statute constitutional, appellants were not entitled to underinsured motorist proceeds, because their policy limits were the same as those of the tort feasor. Underinsured motorist coverage was granted under an insurance contract, the statute permitted insurers to set off amounts available for payment from a tort feasors liability against the insureds underinsured motorist coverage limits.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, in light of the court's finding the statute constitutional. Alteration of the contractual relationship between an insurer and insured did not impinge the constitutional right to seek remedy through an action against the tort feasor.

Adamson v. State


CASE NO. 2008-L-045


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-6996; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 5868



December 31, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Review pending at Adamson v. State, 124 Ohio St. 3d 1539, 2010 Ohio 1557, 924 N.E.2d 843, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 938 (2010)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Lake County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 MS 000018.
State v. Adamson, 1995 Ohio App. LEXIS 1076 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, Mar. 23, 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted sex offender challenged a decision from the Lake County Court of Common Pleas, Ohio, which reclassified him from a sexually oriented offender to a Tier III sex offender as required by the Adam Walsh Act, S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007).


OVERVIEW: The offender was found guilty of rape and other offenses. His petition to challenge this reclassification under S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) was denied. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that S.B. 10 was not unconstitutional. First, there was no separation of powers violation because reclassification did not vacate or modify a prior final judgment. The offender had no reasonable expectation of finality in the collateral consequence of his former classification. Next, there was no ex post facto violation because S.B. 10's regulatory system was not punitive in nature. Federal case law on this subject was persuasive. S.B. 10 also did not violation Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 because the statute was procedural in nature. Further, there was no double jeopardy violation under U.S. Const. amend. V or Ohio Const. art. I, § 10 since S.B. 10 was non-punitive in nature. Finally, the offender had no standing to argue that S.B. 10 violated constitutional protections against the impairment of contracts because there was no plea agreement in this case. At any rate, sex offender registration and notification statutes did not create a contract with the offender.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

City of Dayton v. State


Appellate Case No. 22221


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


176 Ohio App. 3d 469; 2008-Ohio-2589; 892 N.E.2d 506; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 2179



May 30, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by Dayton v. State, 119 Ohio St. 3d 1406, 2008 Ohio 3880, 891 N.E.2d 767, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 2219 (2008)
Discretionary appeal allowed by Dayton v. State, 119 Ohio St. 3d 1501, 2008 Ohio 5467, 895 N.E.2d 565, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 3012 (2008)
Affirmed by City of Dayton v. State, 2009 Ohio 4119, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2254 (Ohio, Aug. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
(Civil Appeal from Common Pleas Court). Trial Court Case No. 2006-CV-3507.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sought review of a judgment from the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which granted summary judgment to defendant, the State of Ohio, and third-party defendant firefighters union in the city's declaratory judgment action. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of R.C. 9.481 against challenge by the city, and it held that it prevailed over residency requirements adopted by the city.


OVERVIEW: The city had a residency requirement for its employees pursuant to Dayton, Ohio, Charter § 102. However, R.C. 9.481 prohibited a political subdivision such as the city from imposing residency requirements for its employees. Accordingly, the city brought suit to challenge the constitutionality of § 9.481. The trial court granted summary judgment to the State and the union, upholding the constitutionality of § 9.481 and determining that it prevailed over the city's residency requirement. On appeal, the court reviewed numerous precedents on the issue. It determined that the enactment of § 9.481 was authorized by the broad grant of authority to the General Assembly to provide for the general welfare of working persons under Ohio Const. art. II, § 34. Further, such authority could not be impaired by the "home rule" provision of Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3 or any other provision of the Ohio Constitution. The role of the judiciary was not impermissibly interfered with by the General Assembly's enactment of R.C. 9.481, and § 9.481 did not violate the Uniformity Clause of Ohio Const. art. II, § 26. As R.C. 9.481 was a general law, a claim of arbitrary classifications lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State ex rel. Kuhar v. Medina County Bd. of Elections


No. 2006-0328


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


108 Ohio St. 3d 515; 2006-Ohio-1079; 844 N.E.2d 1179; 2006 Ohio LEXIS 1977


March 6, 2006, Submitted  
March 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Kuhar v. Medina County Bd. of Elections, 2006 Ohio 5427, 2006 Ohio 5427, 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 5412 (Ohio Ct. App., Medina County, Oct. 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: State ex rel. Kuhar v. Medina County, 108 Ohio St. 3d 1482, 2006 Ohio 884, 843 N.E.2d 192, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 525 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Cause dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an expedited election case, relator elector sought to prevent respondent board of elections from conducting primary and general elections for municipal court clerk. The motion of the Ohio Attorney General to intervene as a respondent was granted.


OVERVIEW: The elector claimed that an amendment to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1901.31(A)(1)(a), which made the Medina, Ohio, Municipal Court Clerk an elected position, violated the single subject rule in Ohio Const. art. II, § 15(D). The supreme court held the elector actually sought (1) a declaratory judgment that the amendment was unconstitutional and (2) a prohibitory injunction preventing the elections board from conducting primary and general elections for municipal court clerk. Such relief was not properly sought in a complaint for mandamus, so the supreme court had no jurisdiction. Any possible limited exception to the general rule barring an extraordinary action in mandamus to contest the constitutionality of legislation did not apply as this was not a "rare and extraordinary case" in which the challenged statute operated directly and broadly to divest courts of judicial power. According to the general rule and absent any possible exception warranting departure from that rule, the supreme court lacked jurisdiction over the elector's claim and had to dismiss it.


OUTCOME: The complaint was dismissed.

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed from the judgment of the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), finding him to be a sexual predator.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant pled guilty to one count of rape and was sentenced. The trial court subsequently conducted a hearing and determined defendant to be a sexual predator. The court held the legislation was not unconstitutional under equal protection, due process, ex post facto, or retroactivity challenges.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the trial court's determination that defendant was a sexual predator was supported by sufficient evidence, the procedural aspects of his sexual predator hearing satisfied due process, and the sexual predator legislation was not unconstitutional.

711 of 997 DOCUMENTS



City of Cleveland v. State


Nos. 89486 and 89565


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2008-Ohio-2655; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 2246



May 22, 2008, Released 
June 2, 2008, Journalized


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by Cleveland v. State, 119 Ohio St. 3d 1406, 2008 Ohio 3880, 891 N.E.2d 767, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 2016 (2008)
Discretionary appeal allowed by, Motion denied by Cleveland v. State, 119 Ohio St. 3d 1485, 2008 Ohio 5273, 894 N.E.2d 1243, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 2848 (2008)
Reversed by City of Cleveland v. State, 2009 Ohio 4118, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2253 (Ohio, Aug. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case Nos. CV-590414 and CV-590463.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city's suit against appellee State of Ohio, in the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) to declare R.C. 9.481, barring employee residency requirements, unconstitutional, was consolidated with appellees' unions' suit against the city, its mayor, its safety director, and its civil service commission to declare the statute constitutional. The trial court granted summary judgment to the State and the unions, and the city appealed.


OVERVIEW: Cleveland, Ohio, Charter § 74 imposed a residency requirement for city employees. The appellate court held R.C. 9.481 did not supersede the city's home rule authority to enforce this residency requirement because the statute was not validly enacted under Ohio Const. art. II, § 34, as it was not economic legislation, nor did it have a nexus between its legislative end and the working environment, and upholding it would extinguish the boundaries between State power and a municipality's authority to legislate the employee-employer relationship. The statute was not a general law because it did not state police, sanitary, or similar regulations, rather than purporting only to grant or limit the city's legislative power to state police, sanitary, or similar regulations, nor did it prescribe a rule of conduct upon citizens generally. Its exemptions for "volunteers" and employees who had to respond to emergencies and disasters did not state police, sanitary, or similar regulations and only limited the city's legislative authority. It did not prescribe a rule of conduct upon citizens generally since it imposed a restriction on the conduct of political subdivisions, not citizens.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

State v. Cephus


C.A. CASE NO. 20505


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


161 Ohio App. 3d 385; 2005-Ohio-2752; 830 N.E.2d 433; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 2583



June 3, 2005, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY: (Criminal Appeal from Municipal Court). T.C. CASE NOS. 03CRB9622, 03CRB9653.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of an Ohio Municipal Court, which convicted her for violating city ordinances which prohibited unlawful conduct of persons at city commission meetings, disorderly conduct, and obstruction of official business, in violation of Dayton, Ohio, Revised Code General Ordinances §§ 30.06(A)(3), 137.01(A)(2), and 131.02(A), respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant often attended city commission meetings and spoke during the public comment portion of the meeting. However, at two such meetings, defendant refused to stop talking after her allotted three-minute comment time expired. She also refused to leave the podium, engaged in a loud verbal exchange with another speaker, and had to be escorted by police from the meeting. She was charged in two separate complaints, which were consolidated for trial. Defendant's motions in limine and for dismissal were overruled, and she was convicted and sentenced. On appeal, the court found that Dayton, Ohio, Revised Code General Ordinances § 30.06(A)(3) was not void for vagueness, as a person of reasonable intelligence would understand when conduct became "boisterous." Further, it was not overbroad, as the restrictions were content-neutral. Admission of evidence of defendant's conduct on prior occasions, pursuant to Ohio R. Evid. 404(B), was relevant to prove her purposeful intent for purposes of the obstructing official business charge. The offenses were not allied offenses of similar import within Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2941.25, and the evidence was sufficient to support the obstruction charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Kistler v. Conrad


Nos. 04AP-1095 and 04AP-1100


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2006-Ohio-3308; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 3227



June 29, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Kistler v. Mabe, 2006 Ohio 6171, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 3307 (Ohio, Nov. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 03CVF12-13425).



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Administrator of the Ohio Bureau of Workers' Compensation (OBWC), sought review of a judgment from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which reversed the OBWC's order that revoked the certification of appellee physician as a provider in the OBWC's Health Partnership Program (HPP) based on Ohio Admin. Code § 4123-6-02.2(B)(5).


OVERVIEW: The physician was convicted in the Florida federal court of one count of conspiring to defraud insurance companies by submitting false and inflated medical bills. He retained his medical licenses and maintained a family practice in Ohio since 1980. He was certified as an HPP provider and was recertified. However, after a hearing, the certification was revoked under Ohio Admin. Code § 4123-6-02.2(B)(5). On appeal, the trial court reversed the revocation, finding that § 4123-6-02.2(B)(5), as applied to the physician, violated his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection. On further review, the court held that there was no substantive due process or equal protection violation by application of § 4123-6-02.2(B)(5) to the physician, as the rule had a rational relationship to legitimate state interests. As no discretion was exercised by the OBWC in denying recertification or in interpreting Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4121.441, promissory estoppel was inapplicable. However, Ohio Admin. Code § 4123-6-02.2(B)(5) was validly implemented within the OBWC's authority. Consideration of the physician's sealed records was proper within Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 2953.32 and 2953.33(B).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter with instructions to reinstate the OBWC's order that revoked the physician's certification as an HPP provider.

State v. Golson


C.A. CASE NO. 22927


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2010-Ohio-560; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 482



February 19, 2010, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Golson, 125 Ohio St. 3d 1450, 2010 Ohio 2510, 927 N.E.2d 1129, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1581 (2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Golson v. Warden, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 76202 (S.D. Ohio, June 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Criminal appeal from Common Pleas Court. T.C. NO. 1998-CR-4083/2.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for two counts of aggravated robbery, with a deadly weapon, and one count of kidnapping. There were multiple firearm specifications. At resentencing, the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) sentenced him to a total of 29 years in prison, six years of which were for the firearm specifications. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The appellate court held that defendant failed to establish that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant was resentenced, not pursuant to the mandates of Foster, but pursuant to R.C. 2929.191, because the trial court neglected to inform him that he would be subject to a mandatory period of post-release control following his release from prison. Regardless, after Foster, the trial court was permitted to impose greater than minimum and consecutive sentences without judicial factfinding. Finally, because defendant failed to provide a sentencing transcript, the record was inadequate to review any error regarding allied offenses of similar import.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

720 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hubbard


CASE NO. CA2004-12-018


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, PREBLE COUNTY


2005-Ohio-6425; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 5785



December 5, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL APPEAL FROM PREBLE COUNTY COURT OF COMMON PLEAS. Case No. 04-CR-008997.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest in the Preble County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) to attempted pandering obscenity involving a minor, under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2907.321, after the trial court denied his motions to suppress and to dismiss. He appealed the denial of his motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Defendant created writings and drawings depicting an actual child engaged in fictional sexual conduct. The appellate court held the State could prohibit the possession of such material without abridging defendant's constitutional rights because the prevention of sexual exploitation of children was a government objective of surpassing importance. His writings and drawings were harmful to the physiological, emotional, and mental health of the child. There was no requirement that such material be disseminated before defendant could be held criminally liable, as the private possession of child pornography could be constitutionally prohibited, nor did the material have to depict actual events, because the State had a compelling interest in preventing the child's exploitation. His obscene drawings and writings depicted a real child, so a bar against legislation banning child pornography which does not depict real children was not offended. Because the material depicted a real child, the State could constitutionally prohibit its creation and possession, and Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2907.321, as applied to defendant, was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Strickland


No. 01AP-1032


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2002-Ohio-411; 2002 Ohio App. LEXIS 400



February 5, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Franklin County (Ohio) which overruled his motion to vacate and set aside the degree of the offense and sentence pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2953.21.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that S.B. 2, § 2953.21 (Ohio 1996) substantially prejudiced defendant, that the bill denied defendant of equal protection under the law, and defendant's sentence was unconstitutionally disproportionate to the new statute. The appellate court found that the new bill had been found to be constitutional in all respects. Further, a trial court's failure to retroactively apply the provisions of the bill did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment or a bill of attainder. Lastly, the provisions of the bill did not violate the uniform operation of laws under the Ohio Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

City of S. Euclid v. Drago

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the South Euclid Municipal Court (Ohio) which denied his motion to seal the record of his conviction for domestic violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of a misdemeanor domestic violence crime. He successfully completed his probation and applied for the expungement of his records. After the completion of his probation, but prior to his application for expungement, the legislature amended the relevant statute to preclude the expungement of such crimes. The trial court held that the expungement statute was remedial in nature, and therefore the constitutional provisions against ex post facto laws did not apply. The appellate court undertook an analysis of the relevant statutes and determined that the defendant had not demonstrated that the alleged ex post facto application altered the definition of criminal conduct or increased the penalty for his crime. The appellate court concluded that the retroactive application of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2953.36(C) did not violate the constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto legislation and upheld the trial court's judgment which denied defendant's motion to have his records expunged.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAWRENCE COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 1211



March 17, 2000, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [*1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.

Jackson v. Bartec, Inc.


No. 10AP-173


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2010-Ohio-5558; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 4692



November 16, 2010, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by Jackson v. Bartec, Inc., 128 Ohio St. 3d 1444, 2011 Ohio 1618, 944 N.E.2d 694, 2011 Ohio LEXIS 857 (2011)
Motion denied by Jackson v. Bartec, Inc., 129 Ohio St. 3d 1482, 2011 Ohio 4916, 954 N.E.2d 127, 2011 Ohio LEXIS 2367 (2011)
Affirmed by Wymsylo v. Bartec, Inc., 2012 Ohio 2187, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 1279 (Ohio, May 23, 2012)
Motion denied by Wymsylo v. Bartec, Inc., 2012 Ohio 3334, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 1932 (Ohio, July 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 09CVH08-12197).



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant/cross-appellee, Director of Ohio Department of Health (ODH) challenged a judgment of the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas, Ohio that both denied ODH's request for a permanent injunction and vacated ten existing violations entered against appellees/cross-appellants, corporation and its chief executive officer, all arising under Ohio's Smoke Free Workplace Act, R.C. Chapter 3794.


OVERVIEW: The trial court, by vacating the corporation's 10 existing violations, necessarily found some of the arguments in its request for declaratory judgment to be persuasive, and although the trial court did not expressly rule on the corporation's cross-claim against the Attorney General for permanent injunction, the trial court's decision to vacate the corporation's 10 existing violations rendered the Attorney General unable to collect any fines resulting from those violations. Because the 10 orders finding violations were final pursuant to R.C. 2505.02, the trial court should not have entertained the corporation's collateral attack on them. Therefore, the trial court erred as a matter of law in vacating the corporation's 10 existing final violations of the Smoke Free Act. The trial court erred when it denied ODH's complaint seeking a statutory injunction pursuant to R.C. 3794.09(D) against the corporation where the evidence was overwhelming that the corporation repeatedly and intentionally violated the Smoke Free Act, failed to comply with its provisions as R.C. 3794.09(D) required, and in so doing exposed patrons and employees to the very harm the statute was designed to prevent.


OUTCOME: The Ohio Department of Health's (ODH) three assignments of error were sustained, the corporation's three assignments of error on cross-appeal were overruled, and the judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded with instructions to issue the injunction ODH requested.

Longbottom v. Mercy Hosp. Clermont


No. 2012-1260


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


137 Ohio St. 3d 103; 2013-Ohio-4068; 998 N.E.2d 419; 2013 Ohio LEXIS 2148


May 8, 2013, Submitted 
September 24, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
CERTIFIED by the Court of Appeals for Clermont County, Nos. CA2011-01-005 and CA2011-01-006,
Longbottom v. Mercy Hosp. Clermont, 2012 Ohio 2148, 971 N.E.2d 379, 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 1869 (Ohio Ct. App., Clermont County, 2012).



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the version of the prejudgment interest statute, R.C. 1343.03(C), as amended effective June 2, 2004, can be applied retroactively to claims accruing before June 2, 2004. HOLDINGS: [1]-Because R.C. 1343.03(C) applied to tort actions filed on or after June 2, 2004, regardless of when the cause of action accrued, the refiled complaint became subject to the amended prejudgment interest statute because it was filed after the legislation had gone into effect. Therefore, the amended version of R.C. 1343.03(C) governed the award of prejudgment interest in the medical malpractice case.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

State v. Haines


Appellate Case No. 23222


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2010-Ohio-1123; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 929



March 19, 2010, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
(Civil Appeal from Common Pleas Court). Trial Court Case No. 08-CV-691.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted sex offender challenged a decision from an Ohio common pleas court, which overruled his petition to contest reclassification under R.C. Chapter 2950, as amended by S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007).


OVERVIEW: The offender was convicted of gross sexual imposition and sexual battery in 1996. In December 2007, he received a notice of his new classification and registration duties. His petition contesting reclassification was overruled, and the offender challenged that decision. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the offender became subject to the provisions of S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) on January 1, 2008. Regardless of the status of the law prior to that date, the offender was required after that date to comply with the registration requirements of the new law. Next, the argument that S.B. 10 violated the right to protection from ex post facto laws, the right to substantive due process, the right to contract, and the right to procedural due process had been rejected previously. There was no separation of powers violation either. Regarding residency restrictions, the offender did not have standing because he did not allege or establish that he was deprived of his property rights. Even if he did have standing, his constitutional argument had been rejected previously. Finally, the offender had no vested contractual right with which the Ohio Legislature interfered.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

727 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


CASE NO. 2005-T-0100


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, TRUMBULL COUNTY


168 Ohio App. 3d 314; 2006-Ohio-4174; 859 N.E.2d 1017; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 4134



August 11, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Brown, 112 Ohio St. 3d 1442, 2007 Ohio 152, 860 N.E.2d 766, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 109 (Ohio, Jan. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 04 CR 712.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his motion to dismiss was denied, defendant pled no contest to two counts of improperly handling firearms in a motor vehicle, in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2923.16. The Trumbull County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) sentenced him to five years of community control, which contained various conditions, including the permanent forfeiture of his concealed carry license. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2923.16(E)(1) and (3) unnecessarily infringed upon his constitutional right to bear arms. The appellate court held that the trial court did not err by concluding that the statute was constitutional, pursuant to Ohio Const. art. I, § 4. Since Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2923.16(E)(1) and (3) placed less restrictions on the right to bear arms than the former version of the statute, which the Supreme Court of Ohio found to be constitutional, the subsections were constitutional. Further, the provisions were not vague. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2923.16(E)(1) clearly provided how a person with a concealed carry license could transport a loaded firearm in a motor vehicle. The language was clear and unambiguous. The statute clearly stated that the loaded firearm must be secured in a locked glove compartment. The fact that defendant's glove compartment did not lock did not make the statute void for vagueness. Nor did the statute lead to arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement because the firearm either was, or was not, secured in a manner that complied with the statute. Likewise, the statute passed a void-for-vagueness test.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Snee v. Jackson Twp. Bd. of Zoning Appeals


Case No. 2003CA00109


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, STARK COUNTY


2003-Ohio-5319; 2003 Ohio App. LEXIS 4791



September 29, 2003, Date of Judgment Entry


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Snee v. Jackson Twp. Bd. of Zoning Appeals, 2005 Ohio 229, 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 225 (Ohio Ct. App., Stark County, Jan. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 2002CV03472.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business owner sought review of a decision of appellee Jackson Township Board of Zoning Appeals (Ohio) which had denied the business owner's appeal of a stop order notice served on him for a sign violation. The Court of Common Pleas for Stark County (Ohio) affirmed the decision of the board of zoning appeals. The business owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The regulation at issue was Jackson Township, Ohio, Zoning Regulation art. V, ch. 501, § 501.6(C). The trial court found that the decision of the board of zoning appeals was supported by the evidence, and also found the signage regulation was constitutional. The business owner had requested a de novo hearing, seeking, inter alia, review of the constitutionality of the zoning regulation. The trial court found that it lacked jurisdiction to rule on the constitutional issue. The appellate court ruled that the issue of constitutionality of a zoning regulation was not within the scope of a zoning appeals board. The original jurisdiction to test constitutionality was in judicial review and was required to be tried originally in the Court of Common Pleas. The trial court's generalized conclusion and claim of lack of jurisdiction was in error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

In re Gant


CASE NO. 1-08-11


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT, ALLEN COUNTY


2008-Ohio-5198; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 4368



October 6, 2008, Date of Judgment Entry


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by In re Gant, 121 Ohio St. 3d 1424, 2009 Ohio 1296, 903 N.E.2d 324, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 757 (2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by In re Cases Held for the Decision in In re D.J.S., 130 Ohio St. 3d 253, 2011 Ohio 5349, 957 N.E.2d 288, 2011 Ohio LEXIS 2648 (2011)
Stay denied by, Motion denied by In re M.D.G., 2012 Ohio 1143, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 726 (Ohio, Mar. 21, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: An Appeal from Common Pleas Court, Juvenile Division.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Allen County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) adjudicated appellant, a juvenile, to be a juvenile delinquent based on his admission to attempted rape, it applied S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2008) (S.B. 10), to him and found him to be a tier III juvenile offender registrant. Appellant sought review of this finding.


OVERVIEW: Appellant said applying S.B. 10 violated the ban on retroactive laws. The appellate court found the Ohio Supreme Court held prior, similar, legislation did not violate this ban because it was remedial, and there was no reason to think S.B. 10 would be viewed differently. For this reason, S.B. 10 did not violate the ex post facto clause, nor did it violate the double jeopardy clauses of the Ohio and United States Constitutions, as it did not impose punishment. It did not violate appellant's right to contract, based on the State's prior representation that it would seek a minimum sex offender classification, because it was held, in response to the same argument as to prior, similar, legislation, that an offender had no reasonable expectation that his crime would not be subject to future legislation, and there was no reason to think the Ohio Supreme Court would depart from this rationale. S.B. 10 did not violate juvenile justice's history and purpose because (1) it let appellant be reevaluated, prove his rehabilitation, and have his status lowered or removed, and (2) the legislature did not intend to exempt juveniles from sex offender registration requirements.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Moore v. City of Middletown


No. 2010-1363


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


133 Ohio St. 3d 55; 2012-Ohio-3897; 975 N.E.2d 977; 2012 Ohio LEXIS 2043


September 6, 2011, Submitted 
August 30, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Butler County, No. CA2009-08-205, 2010 Ohio 2962.
Moore v. City of Middletown, 2010 Ohio 2962, 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 2464 (Ohio Ct. App., Butler County, June 28, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Seeking a writ of mandamus and a declaratory judgment on due process and equal protection claims, appellant landowners alleged that appellee, a foreign municipality, rezoned land that was adjacent to their property in another municipality for the benefit of private enterprise. OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the appellate court's decision that held that appellants did not have standing to assert due process and equal protection claims in a declaratory judgment action. 733 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vernon


CASE NO. 2008-L-066


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3937; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3353



August 7, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Reserved by State v. Vernon, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1508, 2009 Ohio 6210, 917 N.E.2d 811, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3427 (2009)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Lake County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 MS 000014.
State v. Vernon, 2007 Ohio 3378, 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 3099 (Ohio Ct. App., Lake County, June 29, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sex offender was convicted and sentenced for rape, and was classified as a sexual predator. After receiving a Notice of New Classification and Registration Duties under Ohio's Adam Walsh Act (Act), R.C. Chapter 2950, reclassifying him as a Tier III sex offender, he filed a petition to contest the application of the Act to him. The Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denied the petition. The offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: The offender argued that S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio) violated the constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws and retroactive legislation. The appellate court held that Ohio's Adam Walsh Act did not violate the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto legislation. The Ex Post Facto Clause did not preclude Ohio from making reasonable categorical judgments that conviction of specified crimes should entail particular regulatory consequences. Thus, S.B. 10 was not unconstitutional due to the fact that its classification system was based solely on the type of crime committed by the offender. Further, the offender failed to provide any authority indicating that he possessed a reasonable expectation of finality in his original classification. His expectation of finality was limited to his conviction and did not include his former classification. His previous classification was nothing more than a collateral consequence arising from his criminal conduct. As a result, in amending Ohio's classification scheme and making it retroactive to apply to all sex offenders, including the offender, the Ohio General Assembly did not abrogate a final judgment in favor of the offender.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Wenninger


No. CR 2002 2234


STATE OF OHIO, COURT OF COMMON PLEAS, BROWN COUNTY


125 Ohio Misc. 2d 55; 2003-Ohio-5521; 798 N.E.2d 68; 2003 Ohio Misc. LEXIS 35



March 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 29, 2003.
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Wenninger, 2010 Ohio 1009, 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 830 (Ohio Ct. App., Brown County, Mar. 15, 2010)
Related proceeding at State ex rel. Varnau v. Wenninger, 2010 Ohio 3813, 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 3231 (Ohio Ct. App., Brown County, Aug. 16, 2010)

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in a two-count indictment alleging violations of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3599.36, election falsification, and Ohio Rev. The second count alleged that defendant violated Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2921.13(A)(1) by knowingly making a false statement in an official proceeding, and violated § 2921.13(A)(3) by knowingly making a false statement with the purpose to mislead a public official. 735 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barnes


CASE NO. 99-T-0068


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, TRUMBULL COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 6127



December 22, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 81 CR 256.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the Trumbull County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), finding him guilty of two counts of rape, in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2907.02, and two counts of aggravated burglary, in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2911.11.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to two counts of rape, in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2907.02, and two counts of aggravated burglary, in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2911.11. Appellant was found to be a sexual predator. On appeal, eight assignments of error were raised . The first seven challenged the constitutionality of Ohio's sexual predator laws, and the final one was a manifest weight challenge to the determination that he was a sexual predator. The court rejected the argument that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. ch. 2950 was void for vagueness since it compelled a court to make a preponderance determination based upon clear and convincing evidence. The court also did not agree that the statute was an unconstitutional bill of attainder. The trial court's decision was based, in large part, on the expert testimony. Experts agreed that appellant met the qualifications of a sexual predator. Appellant's own expert offered the opinion that appellant should not be left unsupervised in areas where women were available and alone. When experts from both sides concluded that the defendant was a sexual predator, the court was hard-pressed to determine otherwise.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Court rejected appellant's arguments that sexual predator laws were unconstitutional and that appellant was not sexual predator.

 

736 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lange


CASE NO. 10-07-11


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT, MERCER COUNTY


2008-Ohio-1011; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 883



March 10, 2008, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: An Appeal from Common Pleas Court.
State v. Lange, 2007 Ohio 2280, 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 2117 (Ohio Ct. App., Mercer County, May 14, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to witness intimidation and abduction and was sentenced. Later, the Mercer County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) sua sponte issued a nunc pro tunc judgment entry to notify him about post-release control. The sentence was reversed in part. On remand, the trial court held a hearing and notified defendant that he was subject to post-release control and resentenced him to the original sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that imposing post-release control at a later date violated finality of sentencing and double jeopardy principles. The appellate court held that, because he raised identical arguments in his first appeal, he was barred by the doctrine of res judicata from raising the arguments again. Regardless, under both R.C. 2929.191 and judicial precedent, the trial court had the authority to conduct the resentencing hearing to impose post-release control and to issue its subsequent corrective entry, since defendant's prison term had not yet expired. Further, applying Foster on a remand for resentencing did not violate due process. The statutory sentencing range for third-degree felonies had not changed under R.C. 2929.14(A)(3) and the presumption of vindictiveness principles regarding increased sentences still applied. Additionally, the trial court did conduct a new, complete resentencing hearing pursuant to R.C. 2929.191(C) before issuing its corrective judgment entry. Thus, the trial court complied with R.C. 2929.191(C). Finally, R.C. 2929.191 did not violate the one-subject rule since all of the issues in the bill dealt with criminal justice matters.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

737 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grays


NO. 82410


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2003-Ohio-6889; 2003 Ohio App. LEXIS 6224



December 18, 2003, Date of Announcement of Decision


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Grays, 102 Ohio St. 3d 1459, 2004 Ohio 2569, 809 N.E.2d 32, 2004 Ohio LEXIS 1228 (Ohio, May 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from Common Pleas Court. Case No. CR-399318.
State v. Grays, 2001 Ohio 4251, 2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 5397 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, Dec. 6, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for fraudulent acts concerning vehicle identification numbers and receiving stolen property based on an administrative warrantless search of his towing and salvage company. The State appealed the finding by the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) that Cleveland, Ohio, Codified Ordinance § 601.15 was unconstitutional and, therefore, suppressed all the evidence confiscated by the police.


OVERVIEW: The police entered defendant's property and conducted a warrantless search of the salvage yard under the authority of Cleveland, Ohio, Codified Ordinance § 601.15. The police found several vehicles and parts with missing vehicle identification numbers. The appellate court had already determined an earlier version of § 601.15 was constitutional. That version was substantially similar except the new ordinance included "motor vehicle parts" as included in the search. Thus, the appellate court had already determined that adequate limitations were placed on the time, place, and scope of the inspection. Although the trial court found it was not bound by the appellate court's decision, it was indeed bound by that earlier decision. The trial court also found the ordinance unconstitutional because it permitted searches that were not based on probable cause. However, it ignored the United States Supreme Court precedent establishing the policy that closely regulated industries had reduced protection from the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Schamer v. W. & S. Life Ins. Co.


APPEAL NO. C-040057


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, HAMILTON COUNTY


2004-Ohio-4249; 2004 Ohio App. LEXIS 3858



August 13, 2004, Judgment Entry on Appeal


NOTICE:

 [**1] THESE ARE NOT OFFICIAL HEADNOTES OR SYLLABI AND ARE NEITHER APPROVED IN ADVANCE NOR ENDORSED BY THE COURT. PLEASE REVIEW THE CASE IN FULL.


PRIOR HISTORY: Civil Appeal From: Hamilton County Court of Common Pleas. TRIAL NO. A-0304695.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hamilton County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) entered judgments that granted appellee employer's motion to dismiss and dismissed appellant terminated employee's claims against the employer for age discrimination and libel after the employer fired her and claimed in a document it filed with a trade association that the firing involved the "falsification of records." The terminated employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The terminated employee worked for the employer as a securities representative. Her employment was then terminated. Nearly one year later, she filed a complaint alleging that the termination was based on her age. She also claimed that the employer had libeled her when it filed a form with a trade association that indicated that her termination was due to her "falsification of records." The employer moved to dismiss, and alleged, as to the age discrimination claim, that the claim had been filed after the expiration of the 180-day statute of limitations set forth in Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4112.02(N). It also alleged that, as to the libel claim, the terminated employee had signed a release regarding any claims arising from the filing of the form. The trial court granted the employer's motion to dismiss as to both claims. On appeal, the appellate court found her age discrimination claim was not timely filed and that the statute did not deny her equal protection, as it was rationally related to a legitimate state interest. However, it found the libel claim was improperly dismissed because an issue remained regarding the parties' intent surrounding the scope of the release.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment dismissing the age-discrimination claim was affirmed; however, the trial court's judgment dismissing the libel claim was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Thrower v. City of Akron


C.A. No. 21153


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


2003-Ohio-1307; 2003 Ohio App. LEXIS 1216



March 19, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by, Sub nomine at Thrower v. Akron Hous. Appeals Bd., 99 Ohio St. 3d 1467, 2003 Ohio 3669, 791 N.E.2d 983, 2003 Ohio LEXIS 1902 (Ohio, July 16, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE No. CV 00-10-4669.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Summit County Court of Common Pleas, Ohio, held that Akron, Ohio, Codified Ordinance § 150.12 was unconstitutional for lack of a sufficient reasonable notice requirement. Appellant, the City of Akron Department of Public Health, Housing Division (City), sought further review.


OVERVIEW: In its appeal, the City first challenged the jurisdiction of the common pleas court. But, the appeals court was unwilling to conclude from an informal certification that a notice of appeal was never filed with the Housing Appeals Board and included in its administrative record. The City bore the burden of affirmatively demonstrating error on appeal. With no affirmative showing that the citizen failed to file a notice of appeal with the Board, the City's argument failed. But, the appeals court agreed that the common pleas court erred when it found that Akron, Ohio, Codified Ordinance § 150.12(B) violated due process requirements and was therefore unconstitutional. The citizen had actual notice of the violations, evidenced by the fact that he timely appealed the violations and condemnation order to the Board, which granted him a hearing. While he may not have been personally served with the notice of the violations or of the condemnation award, he had actual notice of them and admitted that he received them. As to the citizen's cross-appeal, there was no violation of his due process rights because he received actual notice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

740 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Spencer v. Lakeview Sch. Dist.


CASE NO. 2002-T-0175


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, TRUMBULL COUNTY


2004-Ohio-5303; 2004 Ohio App. LEXIS 4798



September 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Spencer v. Lakeview Sch. Dist., 2006 Ohio 3429, 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 3370 (Ohio Ct. App., Trumbull County, June 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 00 CV 150.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents sued defendants school district, gym teacher, and principal alleging survivorship, and wrongful death claims. The parents amended their complaint and sought a declaration that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744 et seq. was unconstitutional. The Trumbull County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denied the parents' motion for summary judgment, and granted summary judgment for defendants on all claims. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: During gym class, the 14-year-old son suffered an asthma attack and asked the teacher if he could retrieve his inhaler from his locker. Five to 10 minutes later, a different teacher found the son on the floor of the locker room, unconscious and not breathing. He never regained consciousness. The appellate court held that there was no precedent that held that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744 et seq., the immunity statute, was unconstitutional. However, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744.02(B)(4) provided an exception to immunity for negligence occurring on school grounds. Further, there was a genuine issue of material fact as to whether the principal or the gym teacher were negligent. While the school board was entitled to immunity under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744.03(A)(5) for its discretionary decisions such as the level of medical staffing and training of staff, there was a genuine issue of material fact as to whether defendants were entitled to immunity under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744.03(A)(3). Finally, the parents did fail to present evidence sufficient to create an issue of material fact as to whether the gym teacher or the principal were reckless.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed with respect to: whether the statute provided an exception to immunity for negligence occurring on school grounds; the finding that the teacher and the principal were not negligent; and whether the employees of the school board were negligent. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

Tradesmen Int'l, Inc. v. City of Massillon


Case No. 2002CA00251


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, STARK COUNTY


2003-Ohio-2490; 2003 Ohio App. LEXIS 2272



May 12, 2003, Date of Judgment Entry

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Stark County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) held that the Massillon Electrical Code, Massillon, Ohio, Codified Ordinance ch. 1313, was constitutional. Plaintiff construction employment agency appealed.


OVERVIEW: The agency challenged the judgment entered, arguing primarily that the current electrical code violated Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3. The appeals court agreed, in part. Further, the appeals court held that imposition of joint and several liability on the agency was a non-justiciable issue, as it had not sued, nor had any entity sought to hold it jointly and severally liable, for the work been sued. Pursuant to this holding, the remaining two assignments were moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Deer Park Inn v. Ohio Dep't of Health


No. 09AP-67


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


185 Ohio App. 3d 524; 2009-Ohio-6836; 924 N.E.2d 898; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 5737



December 24, 2009, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Deer Park Inn v. Ohio Dep't of Health, 2010 Ohio 1392, 2010 Ohio 1392, 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 1168 (Ohio Ct. App., Franklin County, Mar. 31, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 08CVF-07-10275).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public bar challenged a decision from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas, Ohio, which affirmed appellee health district's decision that the Ohio Smokefree Act, R.C. Chapter 3794, had been violated.


OVERVIEW: The health district sent inspectors to the public bar to check for violations of the Act. A letter sent to the public bar notified it of an observed smoking violation, but omitted any mention of missing signage. The health district later sent a letter of warning based on two violations. The trial court upheld the health district's determinations, and this appeal followed. In partially affirming, the appellate court found that the actions of the health district were inappropriate with respect to the alleged sign violation. There was no opportunity for the public bar to avail itself of the limited procedure afforded to first-time violators. Next, the procedure set forth in Ohio Admin. Code 3701-52-08(D) was commensurate with the nature of the violation and the severity of the penalty, a simple warning letter. The Act did not violate constitutional guarantees to substantive due process and equal protection. The Act was also not unconstitutionally void for vagueness. As the term "permit" was commonly defined, the ban clearly prohibited a proprietor from allowing, consenting, or expressly assenting to smoking within an establishment.


OUTCOME: The portion of the decision relating to a violation for failure to post "no smoking" signs on the premises was reversed. On remand, the health district was instructed to rescind the prior warning letter and to modify its finding and warning letter to reflect that the public bar only permitted smoking on the premises. The rest of the decision was affirmed.

COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, VINTON COUNTY

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The sex offender registrant was not entitled to summary judgment because he did not affirmatively prove his innocence of the act upon which his imprisonment was imposed, failure to register, as required by R.C. 2743.48(A)(5), and failed to prove that he was a "wrongfully imprisoned individual." OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Tanner


Case No. CT2007-0025


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MUSKINGUM COUNTY


2007-Ohio-7175; 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 6291



December 31, 2007, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Muskingum County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Case No. CR2002-0264.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his sentence imposed by the Muskingum County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio). Defendant was resentenced under Foster to one year in prison for receiving stolen property and five years in prison for failing to comply with the order or signal of a police officer; the terms were to be served consecutively. That sentence was the same as what had been imposed originally.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's conviction and sentence had been affirmed on direct appeal and defendant's motion for post-conviction relief had been denied, defendant filed a federal habeas petition; the federal district court vacated defendant's sentence and ordered that he be resentenced under Blakely and Foster. The trial court resentenced defendant to the same aggregate six-year prison sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed. Based on existing precedent, defendant's resentencing under Foster did not violate his rights to a trial by jury or due process or violate the ex post facto clause of the United States Constitution. Foster also gave the trial court discretion to impose consecutive sentences within the statutory range without being required to make findings or give its reasons for doing so. The rule of lenity in R.C. 2901.04(A) did not apply because Foster had clearly and unambiguously severed the unconstitutional portions of the relevant statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Stowers v. Ohio Dep't of Agric.


C.A. No. 10CA009782


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LORAIN COUNTY


2011-Ohio-2710; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 2313



June 6, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Stowers v. Ohio Dep't of Agric., 2011 Ohio 5605, 2011 Ohio LEXIS 2721 (Ohio, Nov. 2, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS COUNTY OF LORAIN, OHIO. CASE No. 08CV159968.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a membership grocery company and its owners, sought a declaration that R.C. 3717.21 and related provisions were unconstitutional as applied to them, a return of all seized property, and injunctions. The Lorain County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) granted summary judgment for the Ohio Department of Agriculture and the Lorain County General Health District. Appellants filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that the company was not constitute a retail food establishment required to be licensed. The appellate court held that the trial court did not err in finding that R.C. 3717.21 required the company to be licensed as a retail food establishment. Even though a membership was required, because the company was a premises where food was stored, processed, prepared, manufactured, or otherwise held or handled for sale to a person who was the ultimate consumer, it was a retail food establishment subject to the licensing requirement of R.C. 3717.21. Although members ordered their products before appellants purchased them, appellants nonetheless gave those products to members in exchange for money and they made a profit well in excess of the cost of transporting and storing the food. Further, appellants did not show any due process violation under Ohio Const. art. I, § 1. The legislature could have reasonably found that food safety bore a substantial relationship to the public health and that regulation of the company and similar types of operations would improve food safety and, consequently, the public health. Finally, there was no equal protection violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
