748 of 997 DOCUMENTS



Hyle v. Porter


No. 2006-2187


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


117 Ohio St. 3d 165; 2008-Ohio-542; 882 N.E.2d 899; 2008 Ohio LEXIS 389


October 10, 2007, Submitted 
February 20, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
CERTIFIED by the Court of Appeals for Hamilton County, No. C-050768, 170 Ohio App.3d 710, 2006 Ohio 5454, 868 N.E.2d 1047.
Hyle v. Porter, 170 Ohio App. 3d 710, 2006 Ohio 5454, 868 N.E.2d 1047, 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 5456 (Ohio Ct. App., Hamilton County, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a township legal officer, sought to enjoin appellant sexually oriented offender from continuing to occupy the offender's residence, under former R.C. 2950.031, now R.C. 2950.034. The trial court granted the requested injunction, and the First District Court of Appeals (Ohio) affirmed. The offender sought further review.


OVERVIEW: After the offender was found to be a sexually oriented offender, the legislature passed former R.C. 2950.031, barring certain sex offenders from living within 1,000 feet of a school, which the trial court applied retroactively to the offender. The supreme court held R.C. 1.48 presumed the statute was prospective unless it "clearly proclaimed" a retroactive application. Neither the statute's description of convicted sex offenders nor its description of prohibited acts clearly declared a retroactive intent. Ambiguous language regarding prospective or retroactive application did not rebut the prospective presumption. The use of a form of the past tense did not show retroactivity, nor did a description of prohibited acts in the present tense purport to cover similar past acts, and two verbs in the description of prohibited acts could reasonably denote distinct, present-tense meanings. A claim that R.C. Chapter 2950 as a whole applied retroactively, making it unnecessary to expressly state a retroactive intent unless otherwise stated, was rejected since R.C. 1.48 did not require a statute's prospective nature to be stated.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed.

State v. Thompson

COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ASHTABULA COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 6090

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was charged with importuning in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2907.07(B), challenged the judgment of the Ashtabula County Court, Eastern Division (Ohio), denying motion to dismiss the charge filed against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a male, propositioned a jogger, also a male, to engage in sexual activity with him. The jogger declined to respond, and defendant continued his entreaty. As a result, defendant was charged, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2907.07(B), with soliciting someone of the same sex to engage in sexual activity, knowing that such solicitation was offensive to the other person or was reckless in that regard. Defendant moved to dismiss, arguing that the statute's punishment of homosexual, and not heterosexual, activity violated his right to equal protection of the laws, established in U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ohio Const. art. 1, § 2. Heterosexual propositions, argued defendant, could be just as vulgar and offensive and just as likely to invite violence as homosexual propositions. Thus, argued defendant, the statute was not rationally related to a legitimate state interest. The court found defendant's argument persuasive, and invited the state supreme court to review the issue, but based on prior precedent, the court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: Reluctantly, the court affirmed the lower court's decision denying defendant's motion to dismiss, based on equal protection grounds, the criminal charge that defendant solicited another person of the same sex to engage in sexual activity knowing the solicitation was offensive to the other person.

 

751 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hill


C.A. CASE NO. 23171


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2010-Ohio-2834; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 2327



June 18, 2010, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
(Criminal appeal from Common Pleas Court). T.C. NO. 96 CR 1412.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted sex offender challenged a decision from an Ohio Common Pleas Court, which denied his petition challenging his reclassification as a Tier II sex offender.


OVERVIEW: The offender entered into a plea agreement relating to several crimes. He was required to register as a sexually oriented offender, due to a violation of R.C. 2905.01(A)(4), for a period of 10 years. The offender was released, but was later placed back in custody when his shock probation was revoked. While imprisoned, the offender received a notice of a new classification and registration duties. The offender's motion to contest the reclassification was denied, and this appeal followed. In reversing, the appellate court determined that R.C. 2950.031 and R.C. 2950.032, which required the Ohio Attorney General to reclassify sex offenders whose classifications had already been adjudicated by a court and made the subject of a final order, violated the separation of powers doctrine. These provisions were severed from the Adam Walsh Act, S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007), and were no longer enforceable. Therefore, the offender's reclassification was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the classification and registration order imposed previously were reinstated.

 

752 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Adams


C.A. NO. 99CA007478


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LORAIN COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 4691



October 4, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS, COUNTY OF LORAIN, OHIO. CASE NO. 99 CR 053694.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed escape conviction, in Lorain County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), arguing that prosecution for this offense after violating post-release control under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2921.34(A)(1) violated Ohio Const. art. I, § 1 (fundamental freedoms) and Ohio Const. art. I, § 9 (cruel and unusual punishment).


OVERVIEW: Defendant violated his post-release control and was prosecuted for escape under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2921.34(A)(1), which did not exempt parolees from the definition of detainees for purposes of the Ohio offense of escape. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the application of the escape statute to him, under Ohio Const. art. I, § 9, which contained a prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment identical to the one at U.S. Const. amend. VIII, and Ohio Const. art. I, § 1, which generally guaranteed liberty and privacy. The court followed guidelines used in construing the federal cruel and unusual punishment provision, and determined that defendant's punishment was not shockingly disproportionate to his offense. It then determined that this limitation on defendant's liberty was a reasonable exercise of the police power, preventing escapes from lawful detention by the least restrictive means feasible. The choice to charge with escape was within prosecutorial discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, because the penalty was not so greatly disproportionate to the offense as to shock the sense of justice of the community and because the escape statute was a reasonable exercise of the police power.

Moore v. County of Lake


CASE NO. 2009-L-053


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two parents and a minor child, challenged a decision from the Lake County Court of Common Pleas, Ohio, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, the Lake County Department of Job and Family Services (LCDJFS) and its employees, in an action alleging reckless placement of a foster child and other causes of action.

Finally, it was typical and appropriate for new foster parents to require further training.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Bonner, 118 Ohio St. 3d 1433, 2008 Ohio 2595, 887 N.E.2d 1202, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 1497 (2008)
Post-conviction proceeding at State v. Bonner, 2012 Ohio 1166, 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 1024 (Ohio Ct. App., Summit County, Mar. 21, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the state supreme court reversed defendant's seven-year sentence, imposed upon his conviction for possession of cocaine, and remanded the matter for resentencing, the Summit County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) again sentenced defendant to seven years in prison. Defendant contended that the remedy in Foster violated the Due Process and Ex Post Facto Clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from the trial court's judgment resentencing him pursuant to Foster, defendant contended that his sentence was unconstitutional because the remedy in Foster violated the due process and ex post facto provisions of the U.S. and Ohio Constitutions. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Walker v. City of Toledo


Court of Appeals No. L-12-1056


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LUCAS COUNTY


2013-Ohio-2809; 994 N.E.2d 467; 2013 Ohio App. LEXIS 2853



June 28, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by Walker v. Toledo, 137 Ohio St. 3d 1421, 2013-Ohio-5285, 998 N.E.2d 1177, 2013 Ohio LEXIS 2828 (2013)
Reversed by, Remanded by Walker v. City of Toledo, 2014-Ohio-5461, 2014 Ohio LEXIS 3117 (Ohio, Dec. 18, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Trial Court No. CI0201101922.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant auto owner filed a putative class action against appellees, a city and traffic enforcement camera company, asserting an unjust enrichment claim and challenging the constitutionality of a city ordinance. Appellees filed a Civ.R. 12(B)(6) motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim for which relief could be granted. The Lucas County, Ohio, Court of Common Pleas, granted the motion and dismissed the case; appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: The company maintained a system that took pictures of vehicles that went through red lights and measured vehicle speed. Appellant alleged that appellees shared revenues generated from auto owners who were sent a civil notice of liability after being photographed during a red light or speed violation. Appellant received a such notice and paid a civil penalty. The appellate court held that as an administrative agency had no authority to determine an ordinance's constitutionality, appellant had not been required to exhaust his administrative remedies before filing suit. By enacting an ordinance that set up a civil enforcement system for red light and speeding camera system violations, the city attempted to divest the municipal court of some or all of its jurisdiction by establishing an administrative alternative without the legislature's express approval; it thereby violated Ohio Const. art. IV, § 1, and the ordinance was therefore void. Appellant's claim that the city police never established an administrative appeal process should not have been dismissed; as due process required notice and a meaningful opportunity to be heard, the absence of any process was problematic.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Arnold

State v. Myers


C.A. CASE NO. 21612


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2007-Ohio-2602; 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 2424



May 25, 2007, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] (Criminal Appeal from Common Pleas Court). T.C. NO. 2005 CR 04654.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which convicted him of escape, in violation of R.C. § 2921.34(A)(1). The trial court had held that § 2921.34 was constitutional, and it imposed a mandatory term of incarceration on defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant failed to report to his parole officer between a specified period of time after he was placed on parole for robbery, and he was charged with escape. The trial court overruled defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the escape statute, and he entered a no contest plea to the charge. The trial court found him guilty and sentenced him, and defendant sought review. The court found that § 2921.34 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VIII, as the sentence imposed on defendant, which was the minimum available sentence for the sentencing range, was not grossly disproportionate to his offense. Further, the stiffening of punishments available for committing escape furthered the Ohio General Assembly's intent to deter such conduct. There was also no equal protection violation under U.S. Const. amend. XVIII and Ohio Const. art. I, § 2, as the graduated penalty scale was rationally related to the State's interest in protecting the public. There was a reasonable assumption that the public faced a greater risk from those individuals who committed more serious offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Rodriguez


Court of Appeals No. H-05-020


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, HURON COUNTY


2006-Ohio-3378; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 3289



June 30, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Stay granted by State v. Rodriguez, 111 Ohio St. 3d 1468, 2006 Ohio 5625, 855 N.E.2d 1258, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 3125 (2006)
Affirmed by In re Ohio Domestic-Violence Statute Cases, 114 Ohio St. 3d 430, 2007 Ohio 4552, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2199 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Trial Court No. CRB-0501150.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Norwalk Municipal Court (Ohio) of domestic violence, under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2919.25. He appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2919.25, as applied, violated the Marriage Amendment, Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11, by conferring a special legal status on unmarried persons, as he and his victim cohabited. The appellate court held the argument's analysis had to ask what rights and liabilities attached to the parties' relationship by virtue of the statute and if they approximated marriage. Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11 only barred recognizing a "legal status" approximating marriage. The statute created a legal status for cohabitants, and the Marriage Amendment's phrase "intends to approximate. . . marriage" modified "legal status," not "relationships of unmarried individuals," so a legal status could not approximate the design of marriage. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2919.25 gave domestic violence victims and perpetrators a legal status, but the Marriage Amendment only barred a legal status approximating marriage. The statute conferred rights and liabilities on relationships resembling marriage, but only recognized that people lived together as if married, and did not intend to approximate marriage, nor did the legal status it conferred approximate marriage in fact.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, and the record was certified to the Ohio Supreme Court for review of whether the statute violated Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11 as applied to a "person living as a spouse."

Home Builders Ass'n of Dayton v. City of Lebanon


CASE NOS. CA2005-01-002, CA2005-01-005


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, WARREN COUNTY


167 Ohio App. 3d 247; 2006-Ohio-595; 854 N.E.2d 1097; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 560



February 13, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Home Builders Ass'n of Dayton & Miami Valley v. Lebanon, 110 Ohio St. 3d 1439, 2006 Ohio 3862, 852 N.E.2d 188, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 2218 (Ohio, Aug. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL APPEAL FROM WARREN COUNTY COURT OF COMMON PLEAS. Case No. 2002CV59491.
Home Builders Ass'n v. City of Lebanon, 2004 Ohio 4526, 2004 Ohio App. LEXIS 4111 (Ohio Ct. App., Warren County, Aug. 30, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City appealed a decision of the Warren County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) finding unconstitutional the City's ordinance requiring that all newly-constructed commercial and residential units be connected to the City's broadband telecommunications system. Appellee homebuilders cross-appealed from findings that they could not maintain their taxpayer suit under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 733.56 and 733.59 or their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action.


OVERVIEW: The City argued that the mandatory connection portion of Lebanon, Ohio, Codified Ordinances § 916.02(16) was not an unconstitutional taking. The appellate court held that the homebuilders did not consent to the taking by agreeing to abide by the electric department's rules. The City was not using its telecommunications system in connection with the supply of electricity. While the City might use the system in connection with the supply of electricity in the future, such use was uncertain. The telecommunications fee portion of § 916.02(16) was severable from the mandatory connection portion. Under § 916.02(16) minus the severed portion, the City could only collect the fee from those units that requested connection to the system. The homebuilders' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action failed as they had an adequate state law remedy. The homebuilders were not entitled to attorney fees. Finally, the homebuilders lacked standing to bring a taxpayer action as the interests pursued by the homebuilders were primarily related to a narrow class of taxpayers, those engaging in new construction within the City. Thus, the homebuilders were not entitled to attorney fees under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 733.61.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Adkins


No. 2010-0465


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


129 Ohio St. 3d 287; 2011-Ohio-3141; 951 N.E.2d 766; 2011 Ohio LEXIS 1683


April 20, 2011, Submitted 
July 5, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Delaware County, No. 09 CAA 02 0012, 2010 Ohio 307.
State v. Adkins, 2010 Ohio 307, 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 244 (Ohio Ct. App., Delaware County, Jan. 28, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the Court of Appeals for Delaware County, Ohio, which affirmed a trial court's decision that a juvenile adjudication was properly considered as a prior offense supporting a felony conviction for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol (OVI).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with OVI. Under R.C. 4511.19(G)(1)(d), OVI was a fourth-degree felony if appellant had been convicted of or pled guilty to five OVIs in 20 years. Appellant argued that a prior juvenile adjudication was improperly considered as a prior conviction for purposes of R.C. 4511.19(G)(1)(d). In affirming, the supreme court determined that R.C. 2901.08 was not retrospective because it had no effect until a new OVI offense occurred. R.C. 2901.08 did not run afoul of either R.C. 1.48 or Ohio Const. art. II, § 28. Moreover, R.C. 2901.08 was not unconstitutionally retroactive. Appellant here was not being punished for a previous juvenile adjudication; rather, he was being punished for his current offense. Enhancement or penalty statutes did not change the penalty imposed for an earlier conviction.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Originally, defendant was convicted of three counts of gross sexual imposition, sentenced to prison, and designated a sexual predator under Ohio's version of Megan's Law. Pursuant to the Ohio Adam Walsh Act (AWA), he was reclassified as a Tier III sex offender. 765 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cornwell


CASE NO. 00-C.A.-223


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MAHONING COUNTY


149 Ohio App. 3d 212; 2002-Ohio-5178; 776 N.E.2d 572; 2002 Ohio App. LEXIS 5240



September 23, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from the Youngstown Municipal Court of Mahoning County, Ohio. Case No. 00 TRD 2668.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Youngstown Municipal Court of Mahoning County (Ohio) convicted defendant of violating the former Youngstown, Ohio, Ordinance § 539.07(b)(1) by playing loud and disturbing music from his vehicle. Defendant appealed, arguing that § 539.07(b)(1) was unconstitutionally vague, overbroad under the Fourteenth Amendment, and violated the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court, in affirming, compared the language of § 539.07(b)(1) (prohibiting maintenance of an audio system in a motor vehicle at such volume as to disturb the quiet, comfort, or repose of other persons or at a volume which was plainly audible to persons other than the occupants of that vehicle) with language of another city's ordinance (prohibiting disturbance of the peace and quiet), to decide that § 539.07(b)(1) was constitutionally sound. The other city's ordinance was interpreted to prohibit the playing of music and amplification of sound in a manner which could be anticipated to offend the reasonable person--the individual of common sensibilities--in such basic human activities as conversation or sleep. That standard of construction, which did not impose criminal liability for conduct that disturbed only hypersensitive persons, vitiated the claimed vagueness of the ordinance. Both ordinances' standards were sufficiently clear to withstand a void for vagueness challenge. Section 539.07(b)(1) was not unconstitutionally overbroad. Defendant could still exercise his First Amendment rights without disturbing other persons' rights to be free from unwelcome noise.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed from a summary judgment of the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) in favor of defendant officials--the warden, the corrections department director, and the state attorney general, challenging the officials' power to pursue collection of a judgment entered against him in a lawsuit on behalf of the state victims' fund by garnishment of his prison earnings.

State v. Dobson


C.A. CASE NO. 2008 CA 43


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MIAMI COUNTY


2010-Ohio-279; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 228



January 29, 2010, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
(Civil appeal from Common Pleas Court). T.C. NO. 071038.
State v. Dobson, 2005 Ohio 123, 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 120 (Ohio Ct. App., Montgomery County, Jan. 14, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted sex offender challenged a decision from the Miami County Court of Common Pleas, Ohio, which overruled his constitutional challenges to R.C. Chapter 2950, as amended by S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007), and dismissed his petition to contest his reclassification under that statute.


OVERVIEW: The offender was registered as a sexually oriented offender after a rape conviction. After the enactment of S.B. 10, the offender received notice that he had been reclassified as a Tier III sex offender. The trial court dismissed the offender's petition after determining that the reclassification was correct and rejecting the offender's constitutional challenges. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that, even assuming that certain provisions of the Ohio sex offender laws were repealed between July 2007 and January 1, 2008, the offender became subject to the provisions of S.B. 10 effective on that latter date. Further, all of the offender's constitutional challenges to S.B. 10 had been previously rejected. Further, the Ohio Legislature did not violate the separation of powers doctrine by enacting S.B. 10, and there was no procedural due process violation because a convicted felon did not have a reasonable expectation that his criminal conduct would not have been subject to further legislation. Finally, the offender lacked standing to argue that his substantive due process rights were violated by the residency restrictions.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

In re J.M.


CASE NO. 16-12-01


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT, WYANDOT COUNTY

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Wyandot County Common Pleas Court, Juvenile Division. Trial Court No. A 2071139.
In re Cases Held for the Decision in In re D.J.S., 130 Ohio St. 3d 253, 2011 Ohio 5349, 957 N.E.2d 288, 2011 Ohio LEXIS 2648 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile sought review of a judgment from the Wyandot County Common Pleas Court, Juvenile Division (Ohio), which designated him as a juvenile sex offender (JSO) after a sexual offender designation hearing was held. He had admitted to gross sexual imposition, in violation of R.C. 2907.05(A)(4) and 2152.02(F).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with being a delinquent child and he entered an admission to the charge. After a disposition hearing, a term of commitment was imposed, and defendant was designated as a Tier II sex offender. After two sets of appeals, a new sexual offender designation hearing was held, whereupon defendant was designated as a JSO. It was noted that at the time of the hearing, defendant was already 20 years old and had completed his disposition. On appeal, the court found that the juvenile court had jurisdiction to classify defendant, as it was correcting a dispositional error following a remand from the Supreme Court of Ohio. Further, there was no error under S.Ct.Prac.R. 11.1. and 11.4 by the juvenile court classifying defendant as a JSO after the effective date of the Supreme Court's judgment entry but before it was mandated to do so. XIV and Ohio Const. art. I, § 2, as the age classification scheme bore a rational relationship to a legitimate government interest of protecting the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the juvenile court.

State v. Shelton


NO. 83289


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2004-Ohio-5484; 2004 Ohio App. LEXIS 4992



October 14, 2004, Date of Announcement of Decision


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Shelton, 105 Ohio St. 3d 1454, 2005 Ohio 763, 823 N.E.2d 458, 2005 Ohio LEXIS 385 (2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Shelton v. Ohio, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 6911 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from Common Pleas Court. Case No. CR-229891.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Originally, defendant pled guilty to sexual battery and was placed on probation. Six months later, he raped a 16-year-old girl. He pled guilty to two counts of rape, and he was sentenced to eight to 25 years on each count, to run concurrently. Subsequently, following a hearing, the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) classified defendant as a sexual predator, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. ch. 2950. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the recently amended version of Megan's Law, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(D), should have been declared an unconstitutional ex post facto law. The appellate court declined to address the retroactive issue, finding that the statute had been declared non-punitive and constitutional. Further, sufficient evidence supported the trial court's classification of defendant as a sexual predator. The hearing transcript indicated that the trial court engaged in the requisite discussion and consideration. The fact that defendant raped two women in two separate offenses was relevant in finding his conduct exhibited a pattern. The first rape occurred just months after he was on probation for the first sexual offense. He also used weapons, displayed cruelty, and made threats of cruelty in both incidents. Additionally, the trial court considered the fact that defendant took many years to take and/or pass sexual offender classes and that defendant had committed numerous infractions during his first four years of imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Franklin


No. 08AP-900


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


182 Ohio App. 3d 410; 2009-Ohio-2664; 912 N.E.2d 1197; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2307



June 9, 2009, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by State v. Franklin, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1422, 2009 Ohio 5340, 914 N.E.2d 1063, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2958 (2009)
Review pending at State v. Franklin, 126 Ohio St. 3d 1533, 2010 Ohio 3825, 931 N.E.2d 1097, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1950 (2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Franklin v. Knab, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 44288 (S.D. Ohio, Mar. 24, 2011)
Reversed by, Remanded by Cases Held for the Decision in State v. Williams, 130 Ohio St. 3d 254, 2011 Ohio 5348, 957 N.E.2d 289, 2011 Ohio LEXIS 2649 (Ohio, Oct. 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 07CR10-7610).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of sexual battery. The Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) sentenced him to four years in prison on each count, to be served consecutively, and classified him as a Tier III sex offender with lifetime registration duties. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by sentencing him to a prison term greater than that of his codefendant. The appellate court held that the trial court did not err when it sentenced defendant. The record precluded sufficient comparison between defendant and his codefendant. The record did not specify the charges to which the codefendant pled guilty and his criminal record was not known. Thus, the sentences could not be compared. The trial court stated in its sentencing entry that it considered the purposes and principles of sentencing set forth in R.C. 2929.11 and the factors set forth in R.C. 2929.12. In addition, it weighed the factors as set forth in the applicable provisions of R.C. 2929.13 and R.C. 2929.14. That statement established that the trial court satisfied the consistency requirement in R.C. 2929.11(B). Further, the record supported the sentence. Defendant had two prior juvenile adjudications and nine prior adult convictions, and he had not been amenable to previous sanctions. His criminal record spanned almost 30 years at the time of sentencing, he had one probation revocation, and he was on community control when he committed the sex offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Keefer v. Ohio Dep't of Job & Family Servs.


No. 03AP-391


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2003-Ohio-6557; 2003 Ohio App. LEXIS 5852



December 9, 2003, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] (C.P.C. No. 02-CVH-4839). APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) granted judgment to appellee, the Department of Job and Family Services (Department), and denied a motion for preliminary injunction filed by appellant employees, in their suit regarding their reassignment, demotion, and freeze in their pay. The employees appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employees challenged the judgment entered, first contending that with the implementation of Am. Sub. H.B. 470, § 19, Gen. Assem. (Ohio) (the amended bill), the Department failed to comply with the federal merit selection system prescribed in 5 C.F.R. § 900. However, the legislature's intent was for the amended bill to have effect for a prescribed two-year period of time, temporarily giving the Department's Director the power to transfer and/or reassign employees without seeking approval of the Director of the Department of Administrative Services. Second, they failed to satisfy the elements for an injunction, specifically that they were likely to succeed on the merits, would suffer irreparable harm if it were not granted, and that the public interest would be served by the injunction. Finally, the amended bill provided for the administration of the civil service, albeit in a different format than before. However, this varying format in and of itself did not violate the Ohio Constitution, but comported with the principles of Ohio Const. art. XV, § 10.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

774 of 997 DOCUMENTS


In re Henneke


CASE NO. CA2011-05-039


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CLERMONT COUNTY


2012-Ohio-996; 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 865



March 12, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by In re Suitability of Henneke, 2012 Ohio 3334, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 1866 (Ohio, July 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CIVIL APPEAL FROM CLERMONT COUNTY COURT OF COMMON PLEAS. Case No. 2010 CVF 01469.
Henneke v. Ohio Dep't of Ins., 2011 Ohio 5366, 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 4396 (Ohio Ct. App., Franklin County, Oct. 18, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bail bondsman was charged with violating violated R.C. 3905.932 and Ohio Admin. Code 3901-1-66 for soliciting on the grounds of a detention facility or court. She challenged a judgment of the Clermont County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which affirmed the decision of appellee, the Ohio Department of Insurance, to revoke her surety bail bond license and to impose a fine.


OVERVIEW: The bondsman argued that R.C. 3905.932 was an unconstitutional prohibition on commercial free speech and was unconstitutionally vague. The court of appeals held that R.C. 3905.932 was reasonably well tailored to achieve its desired objectives. The State's interest in an effective, uninterrupted judicial process was a substantial one. The State successfully asserted a substantial interest in protecting the public from the unwanted intrusions associated with solicitation. A diverse array of witnesses provided detailed anecdotal evidence of the coercive and disruptive nature of solicitation in courthouses and detention facilities. The ban on bail bond solicitation in courts and detention centers targeted several concrete, non-speculative harms and alleviated those harms to a material degree. R.C. 3905.932 was not unconstitutionally vague for failing to provide a more precise definition of the term "solicit." It gave people of ordinary intelligence fair notice and sufficient guidance to conform their conduct to the law. Not only did Ohio Admin. Code 3901-1-66(I)(1) specify additional prohibited behavior, but it also listed activities that remained permissible on court grounds.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the judgment.

 

775 of 997 DOCUMENTS


James v. A-Best Prods. Co.


CASE NOS. 07-MA-42, 07-MA-43, 07-MA-44, 07-MA-45, 07-MA-46, 07-MA-47, 07-MA-48, 07-MA-49, 07-MA-50, 07-MA-51


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MAHONING COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3335; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2825



June 30, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from Court of Common Pleas of Mahoning County, Ohio. Court Case Nos: 02CV151, 02CV743, 02CV1188, 02CV1710, 02CV150, 02CV2432, 02CV746, 02CV745, 02CV2062, 02CV742.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, companies involved with asbestos, sought review of decisions from the Mahoning County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which allowed claims by appellees, 109 asbestos-related injury sufferers (ISs), to move forward upon finding that each IS had submitted sufficient evidence to show a prima-facie case in compliance with the requirements of R.C. Chapter 2307 and Am. Sub. H.B. 292, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2004).


OVERVIEW: The ISs filed 10 cases involving asbestos-related claims against numerous companies. In separate decisions, the trial court determined that there was sufficient evidence to allow the claims to move forward. The decisions were implicitly based on the trial court's prior conclusion that application of new definitional requirements under H.B. 292 to the claims was an unconstitutional retroactive application. Accordingly, the trial court applied the common law standard to the claims. On appeal, the court initially found that the decisions by the trial court were final and appealable as provisional remedies under R.C. 2505.02(A)(3). It disagreed with the trial court's ruling. Rather, it noted that the Ohio Supreme Court had determined that the threshold evidentiary requirements of R.C. 2307.91, 2307.92, and 2307.93, arising from H.B. 292, did not offend the retroactivity clause of the Ohio Constitution when applied to cases pending on the effective date. Accordingly, the trial court should have applied those statutory provisions. The ISs' submissions of one-page forms that were completed by doctors who read their chest x-rays were insufficient to establish the prima-facie cases.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions of the trial court and remanded the matter with instructions to the trial court to administratively dismiss the claims. The dismissals were without prejudice and the trial court retained jurisdiction to reinstate the claims upon a proper prima facie showing.

Satow v. Columbiana County Budget Comm'n


CASE NO. 04-CO-13


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, COLUMBIANA COUNTY


2005-Ohio-5312; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 4835



September 28, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Satow v. Columbiana County Budget Comm'n, 108 Ohio St. 3d 1475, 2006 Ohio 665, 842 N.E.2d 1054, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 409 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from Common Pleas Court. Case No. 03CV493.
City of E. Liverpool v. Columbiana County Budget Comm'n, 2005 Ohio Tax LEXIS 5 (Ohio B.T.A., Jan. 3, 2005)
State ex rel. Satow v. Gausse-Milliken, 98 Ohio St. 3d 479, 2003 Ohio 2074, 786 N.E.2d 1289, 2003 Ohio LEXIS 1168 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a City, its mayor, auditor, and treasurer (individuals), filed a declaratory judgment suit against defendants, a county budget commission, auditor, treasurer, and park district, and several townships, villages, and Cities (CCBC), challenging the constitutionality of Sub. H.B. 329, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2002). The City appealed from a decision of the Columbiana County Common Pleas Court (Ohio) granting summary judgment for the CCBC.


OVERVIEW: The 2003 Alternate Formula for the distribution of Ohio Undivided Local Government Fund and Ohio Undivided Local Government Revenue Assistance Fund money adopted after H.B. 329 was enacted eliminated a requirement that the City approve the formula. The appellate court held that the individuals lacked standing to challenge H.B. 329's constitutionality as they alleged only injuries that harmed the public generally. The individuals also lacked standing under the enforcement of public right doctrine as they did not seek to enforce a current public duty and failed to show that H.B. 329 divested the courts of judicial power. H.B. 329 was not comparable to Am. Sub. H.B. 350, Gen. Assem. (Ohio). The City's claims that the administrative review procedure did not adequately provide an opportunity to present constitutional challenges to legislation and that constitutional challenges to Sub. H.B. 329, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2002) should be pursued directly to the state's highest court were barred by res judicata. The 1990 Alternate Formula did not constitute a contract. Finally, the trial court did not have authority to enjoin future application of the 2003 Alternate Formula was rejected.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

777 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sturbois


Case Nos. 10CA48, 10CA49


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ATHENS COUNTY


2011-Ohio-2728; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 2324



May 27, 2011, Released


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Sturbois, 2010 Ohio 2492, 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 2057 (Ohio Ct. App., Athens County, May 28, 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant rental property owners filed motions to dismiss their violations of Athens, Ohio, City Code 29.03.08.1, based upon a number of arguments, including claims that the ordinance violated their constitutional right to privacy, equal protection, and due process. After the Athens County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denied the motions, the owners pled no contest to the charges. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners challenged the constitutionality of Athens, Ohio, City Code 29.03.08.1. The appellate court held that the ordinance did not violate equal protection under Ohio Const. art. I, § 2 because the city had a rational basis for distinguishing between off-campus rental properties and on campus dormitories when it enacted Athens, Ohio, City Code 29.03.08.1. It was logical for the city to focus an educational program intended to increase compliance with city ordinances on off-campus rental properties on the people who actually lived on, and therefore likely spent the most time on, those properties. Further, Athens, Ohio, City Code 29.03.08.1 did not violate their constitutional right to privacy because nothing in the ordinance impressed a duty on a landlord to investigate or spy on his tenants. Instead, the landlord was to disclose information he already had about his tenants in the process of verifying that he had given those tenants the required educational information. Regardless, the owners lacked standing to assert their tenants' privacy rights because they failed to show any hindrance to their tenants' ability to protect their own privacy interests.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Asish Enters. v. City of Fairview Park


NO. 75088


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 71



January 13, 2000, Date of Announcement of Decision


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Counsel Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Civil appeal from Common Pleas Court. Case No. CV-335,213.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, motel owners and operators, sought review of a judgment from the Cuyahoga County Common Pleas Court (Ohio) denying their requested injunction against appellee, City of Fairview and contending that two ordinances affecting the operation of their businesses were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee City of Fairview Park, with the express intention of prohibiting the use of hotels and motels by permanent guests for which such hotels and motels were not designed, enacted two ordinances. Plaintiffs sought a declaratory judgment finding the ordinances unconstitutional and requesting a temporary injunction against its provisions. The court found action rested upon the flawed proposition that the ordinances prohibited a duly licensed motel from operating as a temporary residence facility under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3731.01(A)(2). The plain language of the ordinances did not prohibit such conduct. The ordinances did not prohibit a "relocating" or "temporary work" guest from occupying, for 30 or more days, a facility which was "specifically constructed" and licensed to provide a temporary residence under that statute. Therefore, because these ordinances did not prohibit what was otherwise allowed they did not conflict with the general state law in the manner challenged.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because plain language of challenged ordinances did not conflict with state statute, but modified because the "reasonable relationship" standard of constitutional review did not apply, rather, the "conflict" standard applied to the constitutional challenge asserted here.

State v. Bump


Case No. 11-COA-028


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ASHLAND COUNTY


2012-Ohio-337; 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 288



January 27, 2012, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Ashland County Common Pleas Court, Trial Court Number 11-CRI-008.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to unauthorized use of a vehicle and theft. The Ashland County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) accepted the plea and sentenced him to 10 months in prison on each count, to be served consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it imposed consecutive sentences. The appellate court held that the sentences were within the statutory guidelines and parameters for felony sentencing. Further, the sentences were not clearly and convincingly contrary to law because the trial court considered the purposes and principles of sentencing and the seriousness and recidivism factors as required in R.C. 2929.11 and R.C. 2929.12 and advised defendant regarding post-release control. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing consecutive sentences because it gave careful and substantial deliberation to the relevant statutory considerations. Because Ohio's former consecutive-sentencing statutory provisions, R.C. 2929.14(E)(4) and R.C. 2929.41(A) had not been revived, no findings were required.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

780 of 997 DOCUMENTS



In re Special Docket No. 73958


No. 2006-1279


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


115 Ohio St. 3d 425; 2007-Ohio-5268; 875 N.E.2d 596; 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2534


June 5, 2007, Submitted 
October 11, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Remanded by In re Special Docket No. 73958, 2008 Ohio 4444, 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 3757 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, Sept. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Cuyahoga County, Nos. 87777 and 87816.
In re Special Docket No. 73958, 113 Ohio St. 3d 1422, 2007 Ohio 1300, 863 N.E.2d 641, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 649 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a tire corporation and others named in 39,000 asbestos-related personal injury cases, filed motions to administratively dismiss certain pending actions. Appellee claimants claimed that retroactive application of the filing requirements under R.C. 2307.92 violated Ohio Const. art. II, § 28. The trial court agreed. The Court of Appeals for Cuyahoga County (Ohio) dismissed the appeal by appellants for lack of a final appealable order.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented was whether the court of appeals correctly dismissed, for lack of a final appealable order, an appeal from a finding by the trial court, rendered pursuant to R.C. 2307.93(A)(3), on the constitutionality of retroactively applying certain statutory provisions. The state supreme court held that the appellate court erred by dismissing the appeal because the trial court rendered a final appealable order, pursuant to R.C. 2505.02(B)(4). The trial court's finding was a provisional remedy pursuant to R.C. 2505.02(A)(3), which determined the action and prevented a judgment with respect to the provisional remedy, and the aggrieved parties would have been unable to obtain a meaningful or effective remedy upon appeal from a final judgment. The trial court's order denied appellants' motion to apply the prima facie filing requirements in R.C. 2307.92, which was enacted with the intent to give priority to asbestos claimants who could demonstrate actual physical harm or illness caused by exposure to asbestos and to enable courts to administratively dismiss the claims of claimants who could not present prima facie evidence of an impairment caused by exposure to asbestos.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appellate court was reversed and the matter was remanded for the appellate court to review appellants' assignments of error.


 

781 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gibson


No. 06AP-509


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2006-Ohio-6899; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 6808



December 26, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Gibson, 2007 Ohio 2208, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 1244 (Ohio, May 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 04CR-4780).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant entered an Alford plea in the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) to rape and felonious assault, and the trial court entered a corrected judgment entry sentencing him to maximum consecutive sentences, he appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court corrected its judgment entry stating prison was not mandatory for defendant's rape conviction. The appellate court held it was unnecessary to clarify that mandatory prison only applied to the rape conviction because the corrected entry's statement that prison was mandatory accurately stated the law. The corrected entry did not say prison was mandatory for felonious assault, nor that both of defendant's prison terms were mandatory. Retroactively applying Foster to defendant's sentence did not violate due process or the ex post facto clause. Foster's severance of unconstitutional sentencing statutes did not raise his presumptive minimum sentence or create an unanticipated remedy by erasing a presumption of minimum and concurrent sentences, because there was no such irrebuttable presumption before Foster. His failure to raise Foster at trial waived the issue on appeal. In addition, defendant knew the statutory sentencing range when he committed his crimes, and Foster did not judicially increase that range or retroactively apply a new statutory maximum to an earlier committed crime. Thus, Foster did not violate due process, or the ex post facto principles therein.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

State v. Weaver


No. 96505


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2011-Ohio-6163; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 5038



December 1, 2011, Released and Journalized


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Criminal Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case Nos. CR-539953 and 540025.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two cases, defendant pled guilty to two counts of breaking and entering, vandalism, and theft. He agreed to pay restitution to the victims in both cases but demanded a hearing. The Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) sentenced him to two years in prison and ordered him to pay $1,780 and $750in restitution. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred because it issued a restitution order without competent and credible evidence of economic harm. The appellate court held that the trial court's restitution order was not an abuse of discretion because the trial court complied with R.C. 2929.18(A)(1) and held a restitution hearing when defendant disputed the amount. The State offered the receipts that were submitted by the victims to the probation department indicating the amounts of their respective economic harm. In opposition, defendant continued a generalized objection and did not present any evidence that would refute the amounts suggested by the victims, such as contrary estimates. Further, the trial court was not required to make any statutory findings as a prerequisite to imposing consecutive sentences. Ohio's former consecutive-sentencing statutory provisions, R.C. 2929.14(E)(4) and R.C. 2929.41(A), which were held unconstitutional in Foster, had not been revived.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

784 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Am. Fedn. & Mun. Emples. Local # 74 v. City of Warren


CASE NO. 2007-T-0110


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, TRUMBULL COUNTY


177 Ohio App. 3d 530; 2008-Ohio-3905; 895 N.E.2d 238; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 3298; 184 L.R.R.M. 2976



August 1, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by Am. Fed'n of State, County & Mun. Employees Local No. 74 v. Warren, 120 Ohio St. 3d 1452, 2008 Ohio 6813, 898 N.E.2d 967, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 3675 (2008)
Affirmed by Am. Fed'n of State v. City of Warren, 2009 Ohio 4120, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2252 (Ohio, Aug. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 2006 CV 01489.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the judgment of the Trumbull County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which, in appellee union's declaratory judgment action, found R.C. 9.481 was constitutionally enacted pursuant to Ohio Const. art. II, § 34 and, therefore, suspended the city's residency requirement for its public employees set forth in Warren, Ohio, Codified Ordinance § 155.05.


OVERVIEW: Section 155.05 required, as a condition of employment, that any person appointed as a non-elected official or city employee become a resident of the city and remain a resident throughout the time of the individual's employment. The Ohio General Assembly later enacted § 9.481, which prohibited municipalities from imposing a residency requirement as a condition of employment. The court held that § 9.481 was constitutionally enacted under Ohio Const. art. II, § 34 since an employee's residency was a matter within the terms or conditions of employment subject to collective bargaining. Thus, in accordance with the Supremacy Clause, § 9.481 prevailed over § 155.05. The court's determination that § 9.481 was constitutionally enacted pursuant to the Supremacy Clause in § 34 rendered unnecessary a "home-rule analysis." However, even after undertaking that analysis, the court concluded that a residency requirement was not purely local in nature and was, therefore, more appropriate for a statewide control by the legislature pursuant to the doctrine of statewide concern; thus, § 155.05 had to yield to § 9.481. Finally, § 9.481 did not violate the Ohio Constitution's Uniformity Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

786 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brooks


CASE NO. 05 MA 31


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MAHONING COUNTY


2006-Ohio-4610; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 4569



September 1, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:

 [**1] THESE ARE NOT OFFICIAL HEADNOTES OR SYLLABI AND ARE NEITHER APPROVED IN ADVANCE NOR ENDORSED BY THE COURT. PLEASE REVIEW THE CASE IN FULL.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Youngstown Municipal Court, Case No. 05CRB454.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Youngstown Municipal Court (Ohio), which imposed a maximum sentence of incarceration on him pursuant to R.C. § 2929.22(C) after he was convicted of receiving stolen property as a first degree misdemeanor, in violation of R.C. § 2913.51.


OVERVIEW: The charge against defendant arose from a stolen motor vehicle that he was seen exiting. Defendant entered into a plea agreement whereby the charge against him was amended to a first degree misdemeanor and he entered a no contest plea. At his sentencing hearing, the judge indicated his annoyance at being lied to by defendant's failure to admit his presence in the car, and a maximum term of incarceration was imposed under R.C. § 2929.22(C). On appeal, the court found that the trial court's sentence was not based on the statutory considerations. However, pursuant to Foster, reversal on that ground was not mandated. Rather, the court concluded that a jury trial right existed for defendant's conviction, which was a petty offense under R.C. § 2929.24(A)(1) where there was a potential penalty of incarceration. Such right was provided by Ohio Const. art. I, §§ 5 and 10, although U.S. Const. amend. VI only applied to serious offenses. Accordingly, applying the reasoning used in Foster to defendant's situation, the court held that the judicial fact-finding required of R.C. § 2929.22(C) for imposition of a maximum sentence violated the jury trial right. The sentencing provision was severed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court with respect to the sentence imposed, and the matter was remanded for resentencing where judicial fact-finding was not to be utilized when considering the proper sentence.

City of Riverside v. State


C.A. CASE NO. 26840


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2016-Ohio-2881; 64 N.E.3d 504; 2016 Ohio App. LEXIS 1772



May 6, 2016, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Civil Appeal from Common Pleas Court). T.C. NO. 13CV4691.
City of Riverside v. State, 2014-Ohio-1974, 2014 Ohio App. LEXIS 1925 (Ohio Ct. App., Montgomery County, May 9, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In an equal protection challenge by a city regarding the constitutionality of R.C. 718.01(C)(13), which created an exemption from municipal income tax for certain air force base employees (AFBEs) and contractors, rational basis review applied because a fundamental right or suspect classification was not involved; [2]-There was no equal protection violation because the State had legitimate interests that were rationally related to § 718.01(C)(13), the exemption was a reasonable accommodation to the AFBEs, and the statutory classification was not arbitrary and capricious; [3]-Section 718.01(C)(13) was based on legitimate state interests, including promotion of the positive relationship between the State and the base, elimination of the administrative burden and negative effect of jobs located within the city, and that the base provided most of the municipal services.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Silverman


No. 06AP-1278, No. 06AP-1279, No. 06AP-1280


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2007-Ohio-6498; 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 5750



December 6, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Silverman, 117 Ohio St. 3d 1459, 2008 Ohio 1635, 884 N.E.2d 68, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 980 (2008)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Silverman v. Lazaroff, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 74819 (S.D. Ohio, Aug. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEALS from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 04CR-1723), (C.P.C. No. 04CR-2338), (C.P.C. No. 05CR-1059).
State v. Silverman, 2006 Ohio 3826, 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 3791 (Ohio Ct. App., Franklin County, July 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate petitioned the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) for postconviction relief after being convicted of tampering with records, tampering with evidence, falsification, forgery, 10 counts of theft, and engaging in a pattern of corrupt activity, and sentenced to 18 years in prison. The trial court granted the State's motion to dismiss and denied the inmate's summary judgment motion, without a hearing. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate fired his counsel during trial. The appellate court held res judicata barred ineffective assistance claims made in his new trial motion and on direct appeal in spite of additional evidence and arguments as the evidence could have been included with the new trial motion, and the arguments could have been made on direct appeal. The credibility of his affidavits could be dismissed as (1) the trial court presided at trial, (2) the affidavits contained and relied on hearsay, and (3) they were cumulative of trial testimony. Counsel's alleged ineffectiveness did not prejudice the inmate because he assumed his own defense. Res judicata barred a claim that his judicial release ineligibility was cruel and unusual and an equal protection violation because he knew he was ineligible when he was sentenced. Since his sentence was not cruel or unusual, requiring him to serve it without judicial release satisfied the Eighth Amendment. Equal protection was not violated because (1) he was not a member of a suspect class, (2) judicial-release eligibility was not a fundamental right, and (3) those ineligible for judicial release due to sentences over ten years were treated similarly.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Smith


Case No. 11-COA-030


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ASHLAND COUNTY


2012-Ohio-338; 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 284



January 27, 2012, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Ashland County Common Pleas Court, Case No. 11-CRI-031.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to burglary, in violation of R.C. 2911.12(A)(3), and breaking and entering, in violation of R.C. 2911.13(A), and theft, in violation of R.C. 2913.02(A)(1). The Ashland County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) accepted the plea, sentenced him to four years of supervision with the Ohio Department of Rehabilitation and Corrections, and ordered him to pay $2,000 in fines. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it imposed consecutive sentences. The appellate court held that the sentences were within the statutory guidelines and parameters for felony sentencing. Further, the sentences were not clearly and convincingly contrary to law because the trial court considered the purposes and principles of sentencing and the seriousness and recidivism factors as required in R.C. 2929.11 and R.C. 2929.12 and advised defendant regarding post-release control. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing consecutive sentences because it gave careful and substantial deliberation to the relevant statutory considerations. Because Ohio's former consecutive-sentencing statutory provisions, R.C. 2929.14(E)(4) and R.C. 2929.41(A) had not been revived, no findings were required.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

In re Farris


C.A. NO. 20102


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


2000-Ohio-6607; 2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 4840



October 18, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS. COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE NO. DN 99-12-1199.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Summit County Court of Common Pleas, Juvenile Division (Ohio), that terminated her parental rights and awarded permanent custody of her daughter to Summit County Children Services Board.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile court involuntarily terminated appellant's parental rights and responsibilities concerning her four children. When it was learned appellant was pregnant, Summit County Children Services Board (CSB) was notified. During her pregnancy, appellant was arrested for drug trafficking and placed on probation. When appellant gave birth, both she and the infant tested positive for amphetamines and methamphetamines. The infant was born with large bleeding blisters on her buttocks, suffered from tremors, similar to seizures, and was fed through a tube in her stomach. Judgment was affirmed. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2151.419(A)(2)(e), in effect when CSB moved for permanent custody, allowed CSB to bypass reasonable efforts in reuniting the parent and child because the parent from whom the child was removed had her parental rights terminated pursuant to § 2151.414, with respect to a sibling of the child.


OUTCOME: Appellant's assignments of error were overruled. The judgment of the juvenile court was affirmed.

State v. Hobbs


Case No. 09CA1


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MEIGS COUNTY


2009-Ohio-7065; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 5908



December 28, 2009, Date Journalized


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CRIMINAL APPEAL FROM COMMON PLEAS COURT.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Meigs County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) to grand theft and aggravated assault. The trial court sentenced defendant. No appeal was taken from that judgment by defendant. Defendant later filed for postconviction relief pursuant to R.C. 2953.21. The trial court denied the petition and, further, prohibited defendant from filing any other motions except those allowed by law. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The grounds defendant asserted in support of his petition for postconviction relief included a narrative of many alleged civil rights violations and included such claims as improper sentencing, ineffective assistance of trial counsel and unconstitutional imprisonment for a civil debt. He also took exception to the trial court's prohibiting defendant from filing any other motions except those allowed by law. On appeal, the court found that three of the four assignments of error raised issues that could have been raised on a direct appeal of defendant's conviction, but were not. Further, although the merits of the claims were nevertheless barred by res judicata, the claims had no merit even if they were properly before the court. As to the trial court's prohibiting defendant from filing any other motions except those allowed by law, the trial court had inherent power to curb frivolous litigation practices to protect the integrity of its own processes. The trial court did not abuse that power by prohibiting defendant from filing frivolous motions in the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Elyria v. Rowe


C.A. NO. 00CA007700


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LORAIN COUNTY


2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 1661



April 11, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE ELYRIA MUNICIPAL COURT. COUNTY OF LORAIN, OHIO. CASE NO. 95 CR 3548.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Elyria Municipal Court (Ohio) convicting him of operating an alarm system at his place of business without the required permit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating an alarm system at his place of business without the required permit, in violation of Elyria, Ohio, Codified Ordinance 703.02. On appeal, he argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss based on double jeopardy, and by convicting him under an ordinance that violated the ex post facto clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The appellate court disagreed. First, although the offenses for which defendant was convicted took place under similar circumstances, each offense was a different act, performed at a different time, with police responding to alarms on two separate occasions. Therefore, there was no double jeopardy violation. Furthermore, defendant was convicted due to his failure to obtain a permit in 1995 and 1999, illegal acts that occurred after the effective date of the ordinance. The ordinance was not an ex post facto law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Smith


CASE NO. 2002-G-2488


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, GEAUGA COUNTY


2004-Ohio-3853; 2004 Ohio App. LEXIS 3447



July 16, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Smith, 103 Ohio St. 3d 1526, 2004 Ohio 5852, 817 N.E.2d 409, 2004 Ohio LEXIS 2665


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 02 C 000047.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of rape, felonies in the first degree. The Geauga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) accepted the plea. Following a hearing, defendant was adjudicated a sexual predator, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(B). He was ordered to serve seven years imprisonment on each count, to be served concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant began having sex with the victims when they were 10 and 11 years old. The appellate court held that the trial court's adjudication of defendant as a sexual predator was supported by clear and convincing evidence as the trial court properly concluded, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(B)(3), that defendant was likely to commit another sexual offense in the future. The trial court found that defendant was diagnosed as a pedophile, that he was obsessed with a 12-year-old child, and that he would most likely desire to continue the sexual relationship with the child. Other statutory factors included: the age of the victims; the fact that there were multiple victims; they were family members; and the nature and number of times the sexual offenses occurred. However, although the trial court conducted an extensive review of the statutory factors at the adjudication hearing and issued a separate judgment entry at the conclusion of the sexual predator hearing which enumerated its statutory findings, it failed to comply with the requirements enumerated in Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(B)(4) by failing to include its findings in the judgment of conviction.


OUTCOME: Because the trial court did not comply with the sexual predator statute in issuing the judgment of conviction, the matter was remanded to the trial court for the sole issue of making its findings in the judgment of conviction. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Smith


No. 92550


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2010-Ohio-2880; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 2383



June 24, 2010, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Criminal Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CR-509799.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 1988, defendant was convicted of rape, kidnapping, and gross sexual imposition. After completing his sentence, pursuant to R.C. 2950.031 and R.C. 2950.032, of the Adam Walsh Act, he was reclassified as a Tier III sex offender, with a 90-day registration requirement. The Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) convicted dim of failure to verify his current address, in violation of R.C. 2950.06(F). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it found him guilty of failing to verify his current address. The appellate court held that defendant's reclassification as a Tier III sex offender was unlawful, and could not serve as the predicate for the crime for which he was indicted and convicted, failure to register under R.C. 2950.06(F). The attorney general reclassified defendant based upon R.C. 2950.031 and R.C. 2950.032, which had been declared unconstitutional because they violated the doctrine of separation of powers. The statutes could not be applied to offenders previously adjudicated by judges under Megan's Law, former R.C. Chapter 2950, and the classification of sexually oriented offender and community-notification and registration orders imposed previously by the trial court had to be reinstated.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

Horstman v. Cincinnati Ins. Co.


C.A. CASE NO. 18430


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 5354



November 17, 2000, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] T.C. CASE NO. 97-1710.



DISPOSITION: The Horstmans' assignment of error is overruled. Both appeals are, therefore, denied, and the judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed and defendant insurance company cross-appealed the decision of the trial court (Ohio) which awarded plaintiffs prejudgment interest but denied plaintiffs attorney fees in a cause action brought against defendant by plaintiff for underinsured motorist benefits.


OVERVIEW: Following a motor vehicle accident, plaintiffs brought a declaratory judgment cause of action against defendant insurance company for underinsured motorist benefits. The trial court found that plaintiffs were not entitled to underinsured motorist benefits and dismissed plaintiffs' action. On remand, the trial court found that the plaintiffs were entitled to underinsured motorist benefits in the amount of $ 100,000. Plaintiffs then moved for prejudgment interest and attorney fees. The trial court awarded plaintiffs prejudgment interest but denied them attorney fees. The appellate court affirmed. Prejudgment interest was appropriate under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1343.03(A) because plaintiffs' claim for underinsured motorist benefits was a contract claim and the benefits were due and payable based on an instrument of writing. Prejudgment interest began accruing from the date of the accident because plaintiffs were denied use of the benefits while defendant enjoyed economic gain. Plaintiffs were not entitled to attorney fees, however, because Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2721.16 was remedial in nature and its prohibition against attorney fees was intended to be retroactive.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Plaintiffs were entitled to prejudgment interest on their underinsured motorist claim because their claim arose in contract. Plaintiffs were not entitled to attorney fees, however, because the statutory prohibition against attorney fees was intended to be retroactive.

State v. Bowman


No. 02AP-1025


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2003-Ohio-5341; 2003 Ohio App. LEXIS 4800



October 7, 2003, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] (C.P.C. No. 01CR-08-4948). APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; amendment dated 9/19/2002 and corrected judgment entry dated 9/20/2002 vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pled guilty to abduction, and upon completion of the sentencing hearing, the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) orally pronounced defendant a sexual predator. In its later judgment entry and sentencing addendum, the trial court classified defendant as a sexually oriented offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After defendant appealed, the trial court changed the judgment entry and sentencing addendum to show that defendant was classified as a sexual predator. The appellate court ruled that the trial court's oral pronouncement was not a judgment. The later judgment entry and sentencing addendum, ruling that defendant was a sexually oriented offender, was a judgment. Since the trial court's later amendment of its sentencing addendum and corrected judgment entry was done after the appeal was filed and was inconsistent with the appellate court's jurisdiction, the trial court did not have jurisdiction amend its ruling, and those orders were nullities. The trial court's application of former Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.01(D)(2)(a) to defendant did not violate substantive due process guarantees. Defendant's contention that his classification as a sexually oriented offender violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment was unpersuasive. Since the appellate court determined that the trial court's post-appeal changes were nullities, defendant's argument that the evidence did not support his classification as a sexual predator was moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

800 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Loyd v. Lovelady


No. 2004-1465


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


108 Ohio St. 3d 86; 2006-Ohio-161; 840 N.E.2d 1062; 2006 Ohio LEXIS 218


June 14, 2005, Submitted  
February 1, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State ex rel. Loyd v. Lovelady, 108 Ohio St. 3d 1513, 2006 Ohio 1329, 844 N.E.2d 857, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 782 (Ohio, Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Cuyahoga County, No. 83090, 2004 Ohio 3617.
State ex rel. Lloyd v. Lovelady, 2004 Ohio 3617, 2004 Ohio App. LEXIS 3294 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, July 8, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the trial court denied appellee alleged father's motion for relief from a paternity determination, under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3119.961 et seq., the Court of Appeals for Cuyahoga County (Ohio) reversed. The Ohio Supreme Court accepted a discretionary appeal.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3119.961 et seq., providing for relief from determinations of paternity, were unconstitutional because they infringed upon the exclusive authority of the Ohio Supreme Court to prescribe procedural rules for Ohio courts. The court of appeals found § 3119.961 et seq. did not violate constitutional separation of powers, because those sections established a substantive right, not a procedural right. The supreme court held the general assembly, in enacting the statutes' predecessor, specifically provided that it was a person's substantive right to obtain relief from a judgment requiring the person to pay child support, and the statutes were enacted to make it less likely that a person would be forced to support a child that was not his. While Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 3119.961 and 3119.962 were packaged in procedural wrapping, the general assembly clearly intended to create a substantive right to address potential injustice. The statutes did not conflict with Ohio R. Civ. P. 60(B) in such a way as to violate separation of powers, under Ohio Const. art. IV, § 5(B).


OUTCOME: The lower court's judgment was affirmed.
